# WhoeverWants Development Environment

## Project Overview

**WhoeverWants** is an anonymous questioning application for group decision-making. Users create and vote on questions without accounts or sign-ups, sharing via link.

- **Live site**: https://whoeverwants.com
- **Repository**: https://github.com/samcarey/whoeverwants
- **License**: Dual MIT / Apache 2.0

## Active Plan

The Supabase-to-Python migration and infrastructure improvements (Phases 1-10) are complete. The current architecture is: Vercel (frontend) + DigitalOcean droplet (FastAPI API + PostgreSQL).

**Next major change: poll redesign.** Every question becomes a poll wrapping one or more questions. A category bubble bar (one bubble per `BUILT_IN_TYPES` entry plus "Other" ŌĆö `BUBBLE_ENTRIES` in `app/create-poll/page.tsx`) replaces the single new group button on groups. Tapping a bubble seeds a fresh draft with that category preselected and opens the new-question modal.

> **Historical note on What/When/Where:** Earlier iterations of the redesign shipped a 3-bubble bar (What/When/Where) that preselected via `?mode=time` / `?category=restaurant`. That trichotomy was eliminated; references to "What/When/Where" in Phase 2.3 / Navigation Layout / Always-On Draft Poll Card sections below are historical context, NOT the current UI. The current bar is per-category.

### Group-as-a-hub: make a group a legible shared decision space (gaps 1/3/4 SHIPPED + merged, MayŌĆōJune 2026)

**Thesis.** The app's real competitor is the group chat thread where decisions die ("so are we doing Friday??" ├Ś 40 messages, no resolution). A single poll is a weak substitute; a *group* a circle returns to ŌĆö where decisions accrete and outcomes are legible ŌĆö is a strong one, and the multi-question event poll ("plan the whole night in one link") is its sharpest expression. This initiative makes a group feel like a lightweight shared decision space, NOT a folder of polls. **Explicitly NOT a chat** ŌĆö the value is the decision layer the chat lacks; do not add messaging.

**Foundations already shipped (build on, don't rebuild):** first-class groups (`group_id` + group short_id, title override, avatar image, privacy, invites, join requests, claim, invite-members address book); notifications on new-poll / poll-closed / phase-transition with per-group mute; the home group list with per-group unread indicators + countdowns + awaiting-first sort; atomic multi-question polls with per-question abstain. What's missing is the *legibility* layer on top.

**ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ STATUS (June 2026): SHIPPED + MERGED to `main`. Gaps 1 + 4 (the follow/ignore To Do ┬Ę New ┬Ę Old tabs + home rollup) landed via #575; the account-aware Old-set push suppression that gap 3 was waiting on landed via #576. Gap 2 is deleted/deferred (see below).** Open questions B + C were resolved with the spec's proposed defaults (inline Ō£Ģ/+ button, no auto-aging), reviewed by the owner on a dev-server link, and merged ŌĆö no longer pending. Historical context: a prototype of the original gaps (segmented Open/Decided filter + 3 layout variants + decisions-ledger drawer + "the plan" summary + outcome-notification body + home rollup) was built on branch `claude/group-hub-ui-variants-FzkNe`, deployed, and compared by the owner, who picked the **segmented-filter** layout and **redefined the semantics** into the follow/ignore model below; that prototype was reverted and the spec merged before the from-scratch implementation (originally on `claude/todo-selection-handling-EfPMu`) landed on `main`.

> **UPDATE (June 2026, `claude/group-page-inline-lists-OoQ3K`): the To Do ┬Ę New ┬Ę Old TABS are now INLINE LABELED SECTIONS, "New" is relabeled "Relevant", and the group page DEFAULTS TO SCROLL-TO-TOP (the bottom-pin subsystem was deleted).** The sticky segmented control is GONE. `GroupContent` now splits polls into three mutually-exclusive lists via a `sections` useMemo (`SECTION_DEFS` = `[{todo,"To Do"},{new,"Relevant"},{old,"Old"}]`, filtered to non-empty) and renders them stacked in order, each preceded by a plain header (`text-[19.2px] font-semibold uppercase`, muted, `border-b-2` under-line divider ŌĆö heavier than the rows' `border-b`, `mt-[0.9rem]` gap above non-first sections). `visibleGroupedQuestions` is the flat concat of the section groups (still drives virtualization/anchor/scroll-helpers). Each card gets `effectiveTab={section.tab}` + `isTodo={section.tab === "todo"}` (a card in a section classifies to that tab by construction ŌĆö cheaper than the old per-card `classifyPollTab`). Empty lists render no header. `selectedTab`/`selectTab`/`getRememberedGroupTab`/`rememberGroupTab` + the `lib/groupTabMemory` usage here are REMOVED (the sections show all at once, so there's no selected-tab state to remember ŌĆö `clearGroupTabs()` in `app/page.tsx` is now a harmless no-op against an unused store). **Scroll: fresh visit (and homeŌåÆback-to-group, both no saved scroll) now `window.scrollTo(0, 0)` ŌĆö TOP, not bottom.** Top is stable as content grows downward, so the whole bottom-pin subsystem was deleted: `BOTTOM_PIN_DURATION_MS`, `bottomPinDeadlineRef`, the bottom-pin rAF loop, `applyScrollAdjustmentRef` + its per-render layout effect + the ResizeObserver's `applyScrollAdjustment` call + docEl observation, and the overlay-bottom-pin (`overlayShouldBottomPin`/`overlayBottomOffset` + its effect) are all gone. `anchorGroupKey` flipped to `visibleGroupedQuestions[0]` (first/top group) so the top cards mount first; the fresh-nav slide overlay shows the top (`cardsTransformOffset = overlayCardsOffset`, undefined ŌåÆ no transform). The saved-scroll RESTORE path (within-group back, groupŌåöpoll) is UNCHANGED ŌĆö it still mounts every card up-front + re-applies the saved scrollY via the persistent restore-pin. Many bullets below (scroll strategy, bottom-pin, groupTabMemory, "lands on awaiting card or bottom", "Fresh nav pre-position to bottom") describe the PRE-update behavior ŌĆö this note supersedes them.

**Gap 1 + 4 ŌĆö SHIPPED + MERGED (#575 follow/ignore tabs + home rollup; #576 account-aware Old-set push suppression). What shipped, resolving the open questions with the spec's proposed defaults:**
  - **Server-side state (open question A ŌĆö RESOLVED: server-side, account-aware).** Migration 134 `poll_follow_state(poll_id, browser_id, state Ōłł ('new','old'), updated_at)`, PK `(poll_id, browser_id)` + index on `browser_id`. No row = `'new'` (default-follow). `services/follow_state.py`: `effective_follow_states(conn, poll_ids, *, browser_ids)` (account-aware read ŌĆö most-recently-updated row across the caller's linked browsers wins, via `clock_timestamp()` recency so same-transaction writes still order); `old_poll_ids_for_browsers` (browser-scoped, for badge/push suppression); `set_follow_state` (Ō£Ģ ŌåÆ 'old', + ŌåÆ 'new', upsert). `PollResponse.viewer_follow_state` is threaded per-viewer through `polls_for_poll_ids` via a new `viewer_browser_id` param (mirrors `viewer_user_id`); set on both `/api/groups/mine` + `/by-route-id`. `POST /api/polls/{id}/follow-state {state}` (per-viewer, reversible, NOT a creator action, orthogonal to membership ŌĆö open question D confirmed). Anonymous viewers key on `browser_id` alone (open question G confirmed).
  - **Notification + badge suppression.** `compute_badge_count` excludes Old polls **account-aware** (`old_poll_ids_for_browsers(bids)`, both to-do + unread modes). `fan_out_poll_closed` + `fan_out_phase_transition` exclude `'old'` recipients via the `_NOT_IGNORED` SQL fragment (mirrors `_PREF_JOIN`/`_PREF_ON_TRUE`) ŌĆö **account-aware** (cross-device): a member browser is skipped when the EFFECTIVE follow state (most-recently-updated `poll_follow_state` row across every browser linked to the member's account, resolved via the `gm_ub.user_id` already joined by `_PREF_JOIN`) is `'old'`, so Ō£Ģ on device A silences device B's push for the same account. Anonymous members (`gm_ub.user_id IS NULL`) fall back to their own browser's row ŌĆö the `au.user_id = NULL` join matches nothing so the union reduces to `gm.browser_id`. Recency-based union semantics match the badge path's `effective_follow_states`. New-poll fan-out is untouched (a brand-new poll can't be Old yet). **Gap 3's "compose with Old-set suppression" TODO is now satisfied for poll-closed** (the `_NOT_IGNORED` clause). Recipient-SELECTION is testable (`server/tests/test_notification_events.py::test_ignore_on_one_device_silences_account_push`); push DELIVERY isn't demoable (needs a real subscription).
  - **FE.** `lib/followState.ts`: pure `classifyPollTab(poll, voted, abstained, nowMs)` (Old ŌåÆ 'old'; followed + needs-input ŌåÆ 'todo'; else 'new') + `tallyFollowTabs`. NOTE: `pollNeedsInput` intentionally diverges from `isPollUnread`'s todoMode (it COUNTS active-prephase-contributable polls as To Do; the badge does not) ŌĆö cross-referenced in both files so the difference reads as deliberate. `Poll.viewer_follow_state` on the type + `toPoll`; `apiSetPollFollowState(pollId, state)` patches the per-poll + accessible-polls caches; `isPollContentEqual` (groupRefresh) includes the field so a cross-device flip reflects on the 5s refresh. Group page (`GroupPage.tsx`): a sticky **To Do ┬Ę New ┬Ę Old** segmented control (default tab = To Do if any, else New; `selectedTab` null until tapped), filters `visibleGroupedQuestions` (New shows every followed poll ŌĆö To Do ŌŖå New), empty-state per tab. `GroupCardItem`: **swipe the row LEFT past a threshold to act on the poll** ŌĆö this REPLACED the inline Ō£Ģ/+ button (the button + its four-event `stopPropagation` dance are gone). The action is state-dependent: **Old ŌåÆ re-follow (green "Follow")**, **To Do ŌåÆ ABSTAIN (gold "ŌĆö Abstain")**, **New-non-todo ŌåÆ ignore (red "Ō£Ģ Ignore" ŌåÆ Old)** (`swipeAction` in `GroupCardItem.tsx`). Abstain quick-action: `onAbstain` ŌåÆ GroupPage `handleSwipeAbstain` ŌåÆ `useGroupVoting.submitPollAbstain(pollId, subQuestions)` ŌĆö abstains ONLY the still-unanswered sub-questions (never overwrites an existing vote; a multi-question poll is To Do while ANY sub-question is unanswered), optimistic local voted/abstained flip + revert on failure. Abstaining is a vote, so it's **name-gated**: `handleSwipeAbstain` stashes a retry thunk + opens `<AccountGateModal message="to abstain">` when `isValidUserName(getUserName())` is false; the card receives `nameReady` so it knows whether to play the exit animation vs snap back to the gate. The follow toggle (ignore/re-follow) is still optimistic `patchGroupPolls` + revert via `handleToggleFollow`. **Per-card props from GroupPage: `isTodo` (= `classifyPollTab(...) === 'todo'`), `effectiveTab`, `nameReady`, `onAbstain`** (all in `arePropsEqual`'s cheap-boolean block except the stable `onAbstain` handler). Mechanics (all in `GroupCardItem.tsx`): `handleTouchMove` axis-locks on first >8px motion (`axisRef` 'h'|'v'); a horizontal lock sets `swipingRef` + drives a card-local `dragX` (clamped `[-SWIPE_MAX(130), 0]` ŌĆö LEFTWARD only, so it never collides with the page's rightward `useSwipeBackGesture`, which ignores `dx Ōēż 0`). **Only the EXPOSED strip lights up**: the action backdrop is `absolute inset-y-0 right-0 z-0` with `width = -dragX` (tracks the gap exactly, not `inset-0`), and while swiping the content background is forced neutral `bg-background` (the `hover:`/`active:`/`isPressed` tint classes are dropped via the `swiping` gate) so the whole row no longer tints. `haptic.light()` fires once on threshold crossing (`crossedRef`), `haptic.medium()` on commit. **Commit (past-threshold release) plays a slide-out + collapse exit when it removes the card from the current tab** (`swipeCanExit = swipeWillExit && (action !== 'abstain' || nameReady)`; `swipeWillExit` is false only for abstain on the New tab, where the card stays New): `setExiting(true)` slides the content `translateX(-100%)` AND collapses the outer **grid** (`grid-template-rows 1fr ŌåÆ 0fr`, with a `min-h-0` inner track + `overflow-hidden` only-while-exiting so the rows below animate up to fill the gap and the date tooltip isn't clipped at rest), then `commitSwipe()` fires on the collapse's `grid-template-rows` transitionEnd ŌĆö after which the card leaves the filtered list and unmounts (already at 0 height / off-screen, no pop). Non-exit commits (abstain on New tab, or nameless ŌåÆ gate) fire immediately + snap back. The visual rectangle (border-b, backdrop, amber bar, content) lives one level inside the grid so its border collapses with it; the amber unread bar is `z-20` so it stays pinned above the sliding content. **Touch-only by design** (matches long-press ŌåÆ modal, also touch-only ŌĆö no desktop-mouse equivalent). Home rollup (Gap 4): `GroupList`/`GroupListItem` show "N to do ┬Ę M new" per group row.
  - **Open questions B (Ō£Ģ/+ affordance) + C (no auto-aging) shipped per the proposals** ŌĆö they were design-sensitive, so the owner reviewed the dev-server link before merge. Tests: `server/tests/test_follow_state.py` (7), `tests/__tests__/follow-state.test.ts` (8).
  - **Gap 2 of the original spec (sticky/transform coupling on the segmented control): the sticky bar relies on the cards-wrapper transform being transient (true in the steady-state real route). If that transform ever becomes persistent, hoist the control out of the transformed wrapper ŌĆö noted inline.**

**Gap 1 (LOCKED) ŌĆö the group page is a per-poll follow/ignore manager with three tabs: `To Do ┬Ę New ┬Ę Old`.** This replaces the original "Open/Decided filter + decisions ledger" idea. It's a segmented filter at the top of the group page (the V1 "filter" layout the owner chose), but the three tabs are a *following* model, not an open/closed split:
  - **To Do** ŌĆö polls that need THIS viewer's input: not in Old, open + votable now (past any prephase, deadline not passed), and the viewer hasn't responded (voted/abstained). A poll in an active prephase the viewer can contribute to (suggestion / availability collection) counts as To Do. (To Do ŌŖå New.)
  - **New** ŌĆö polls the viewer is *following*: every poll (open OR closed) that the viewer hasn't dismissed. A poll lands here on creation and **stays in New until the viewer taps a red Ō£Ģ on it** ŌĆö which works whether the poll is open or closed. Closed-and-still-followed polls live here so the viewer sees the outcome; the Ō£Ģ is the only thing that removes a poll from New (no time-based auto-aging ŌĆö see open question C).
  - **Old** ŌĆö polls the viewer dismissed (Ō£Ģ'd). A poll **stays in Old until the viewer taps a + on it in the Old list**, which returns it to New. Old is *sticky*: new activity on an Old poll (a phase transition, a reopen, a new vote, closing) does **NOT** pull it back to New/To Do ŌĆö only the + does. Old is the per-viewer "I'm ignoring this" archive; the poll is still in the group, just filed away.
  - **This is fundamentally a follow/ignore system** ŌĆö what the viewer is tracking vs tuning out ŌĆö NOT an open/closed or decided view. The decisions-ledger / "Outcomes" drawer from the prototype is dropped; closed polls show their winner pill inline in New (and Old) as today.
  - **No "awaiting you" helper text under the segmented control** ŌĆö it's redundant with the To Do tab. (The prototype rendered "N awaiting your response" under the filter; do not.)
  - **Notification suppression: no notifications of any kind for polls in the viewer's Old set** ŌĆö poll-closed, phase-transition, and the future outcome push (gap 3) all skip Old polls for that viewer. This is the whole point of "ignore": the server notification fan-out must join the per-viewer follow state and exclude Old polls. (New-poll notifications are unaffected ŌĆö a brand-new poll can't be Old yet.)

**Gap 4 (LOCKED, refined) ŌĆö home-list per-group rollup shows only `To Do` and `New` counts.** Each group row surfaces "N to do ┬Ę M new" (NOT closed / decided / old counts). To Do = the per-group To Do count above; New = followed (non-Old) poll count. Gives cross-group triage ("which group needs me, which has fresh activity") without surfacing the archive.

**Gap 2 ŌĆö DELETED.** The multi-question "the plan" consolidated summary is removed from this initiative. The owner has a different idea for multi-question event polls, TBD in a later session. Do NOT build the "Fri 7pm ┬Ę Thai ┬Ę Escape Room after" consolidated card; the prototype's `PollPlanSummary` was reverted.

**Gap 3 (SHIPPED ŌĆö outcome notifications).** The poll-closed push now delivers the *outcome* on line 2: body `Decided: Thai ┬Ę Sat Apr 28, 7 PM` instead of the poll title. Implemented server-side in `routers/polls.py`: `_poll_decision_summary(conn, poll_id, question_rows)` joins each question's `_question_decision_label` (winner) with ` ┬Ę `; `_build_close_notification` sets `body = f"Decided: {summary}"` when a decision was reached, else **falls back to the poll-title body** (no votes / a tie / all-abstain). Per-question label rules: yes_no ŌåÆ `Yes`/`No` (tie ŌåÆ skipped); ranked_choice ŌåÆ the winning option text; time ŌåÆ `_format_slot_label(slot_key)` ("Sat Apr 28, 7 PM"). The winner comes from the existing `_compute_results(...)` (imported from `services.questions`, `include_tentative_time_options=False`). Summary is capped at 120 chars. **Old-set suppression ŌĆö DONE (#576):** `fan_out_poll_closed` now skips viewers who Ō£Ģ'd the poll via the account-aware `_NOT_IGNORED` SQL fragment (the recipient-selection change landed with gap 1; see the Gap 1 + 4 block above). Delivery can't be demoed (needs a real push subscription); the recipient-selection + payload are what's testable ŌĆö covered by `server/tests/test_notification_events.py` (`test_close_notification_*` + `test_format_slot_label`). The existing yes_no close test asserts the title-fallback body for a no-votes poll, which the fallback preserves.

**RESOLVED open questions (gap 1 shipped ŌĆö kept as the decision record; how each was actually resolved is in the Gap 1 + 4 block above; the original "Decision needed / Confirm" prompts below are answered):**
  - **A. Where does the follow (New/Old) state live?** It MUST be server-side and account-aware, because (1) the notification fan-out runs on the server and has to skip each viewer's Old polls, and (2) follow/ignore should sync across a user's devices. Proposed: a new table `poll_follow_state(poll_id, browser_id, state)` with `state Ōłł ('new','old')`, no row = `'new'` (default-follow), keyed by `browser_id` with the usual `user_browsers` account-union on reads (mirror `group_members` / `load_user_visibility`). Ō£Ģ writes `'old'`; + writes `'new'`. This was the biggest piece (a real migration + endpoints + a fan-out join). ŌåÆ RESOLVED: built exactly as proposed ŌĆö migration 134 + `services/follow_state.py` + the `_NOT_IGNORED` fan-out join.
  - **B. Ō£Ģ / + affordance.** Inline icon button on each row (red Ō£Ģ on To Do/New rows, green + on Old rows) vs a swipe action vs long-press menu. Proposed: inline icon button, no confirmation (reversible). The row already has tapŌåÆdetail + long-pressŌåÆaction-modal, so the button must not collide with those. Decision needed.
  - **C. Does New auto-age long-closed polls, or only the Ō£Ģ removes them?** Owner said "stays in New until the user hits a red Ō£Ģ" ŌåÆ only Ō£Ģ. But a busy group could accumulate dozens of closed-but-never-dismissed polls in New. Confirm: New keeps ALL non-Old polls forever (Ō£Ģ is the only control), or closed polls auto-move to Old after some window.
  - **D. Relationship to existing forget/leave-group.** This per-poll follow state is orthogonal to group membership. Ō£Ģ ("ignore this poll") ŌēĀ forget-group / `apiLeaveGroup` ("leave the whole group, remove from home"). Both must coexist. Confirm the Ō£Ģ does not touch membership.
  - **E. To Do for multi-question polls.** "Needs input" when the viewer hasn't responded to ANY sub-question, or to ALL? Proposed: To Do while at least one sub-question is unanswered (matches the existing "awaiting" / gold-bar predicate). Confirm.
  - **F. Default tab on group open + home count source.** Proposed default tab: To Do if the group has any, else New. Home counts: server returns per-group To Do/New counts (or the FE computes them from the follow-state set it already has). Decide where the counts are computed.
  - **G. Anonymous viewers.** Follow state keys on `browser_id` so anonymous users get in-app filtering + notification suppression too; the account-union just widens it for signed-in users. Confirm acceptable.

**Risks that compound in a persistent hub (cross-references):** late-joiner history loss (now partly addressed ŌĆö see the "closed before you joined" handling in the Migration-106 / #553 notes); two-round time-poll drop-off (social-test recommendation #6) erodes trust if scheduling keeps stalling; roster identity issues (the ballot-privacy TODO) are felt continuously since the same names recur.

**Process note (satisfied for the gap-1 build; the rule still applies to future design-sensitive work):** the gap-1 Ō£Ģ/+ affordance + row chrome were design-sensitive, so the build was deployed to a dev server and the owner reviewed the link before merge. Keep following this deploy-and-review pattern for new design-sensitive interactions rather than shipping unilaterally.

## DigitalOcean Droplets ŌĆö Two-Tier Deploy

WhoeverWants runs on **two** DigitalOcean droplets that are software-identical (same `scripts/provision-droplet.sh`, same Docker stack, same migrations). Only the public hostnames and deploy trigger differ ŌĆö see "Development Workflow" below for the gating.

- **`whoeverwants` (prod)** ŌĆö `142.93.60.29`, fronts `api.whoeverwants.com` + `hooks.api.whoeverwants.com`. Deploys when a GitHub Release is published, pinned to the release's tag.
- **`latest` (pre-prod canary)** ŌĆö `104.248.61.202`, fronts `api.latest.whoeverwants.com` + `hooks.api.latest.whoeverwants.com`. Deploys on every push to `main` so the latest code is exercised in its final configuration (release-mode build, droplet, Caddy, Postgres) before a production release.

Behavior is driven by `/etc/droplet-label` on each droplet (`""` = prod, `"latest"` = canary). `scripts/dev-webhook.py` reads it at startup. `scripts/provision-droplet.sh` accepts `DROPLET_LABEL=latest` to provision a canary; default behavior is prod.

### Server Specs (both droplets ŌĆö match exactly)
| Property | Value |
|----------|-------|
| Image | Ubuntu 24.04 LTS |
| Size | s-1vcpu-1gb (1 GB RAM, 24 GB SSD) |
| Region | nyc1 |
| User | `root` |

| Hostname | IP | Tier | Public hosts |
|----------|----|----|--------------|
| `whoeverwants` | `142.93.60.29` | prod | `api.whoeverwants.com`, `hooks.api.whoeverwants.com` |
| `latest` | `104.248.61.202` | canary | `api.latest.whoeverwants.com`, `hooks.api.latest.whoeverwants.com` |

### Remote Command Execution

Both droplets are reachable over their own sslip.io URL via a sibling pair of helpers:

```bash
# Prod droplet
bash scripts/remote.sh "command" [working_dir] [timeout_seconds]

# Latest (canary) droplet
bash scripts/remote-latest.sh "command" [working_dir] [timeout_seconds]
```

Both honor the same JSON protocol; only the env vars differ. Examples:

```bash
bash scripts/remote.sh "hostname && uptime"                  # prod
bash scripts/remote-latest.sh "hostname && uptime"           # latest
bash scripts/remote.sh "docker compose logs --tail 50" /root/whoeverwants
bash scripts/remote-latest.sh "cat /etc/droplet-label"       # should print "latest"
```

### Required Environment Variables

The following environment variables must be available. In the Claude Code web environment, these are pre-set as environment variables (not in a `.env` file).

```
DROPLET_API_URL=https://142-93-60-29.sslip.io
DROPLET_API_TOKEN=<bearer token>
LATEST_DROPLET_API_URL=https://104-248-61-202.sslip.io
LATEST_DROPLET_API_TOKEN=<bearer token for latest droplet>
DIGITAL_OCEAN_TOKEN=<DO API v2 token>
VERCEL_API_TOKEN=<vercel api token>
GITHUB_API_TOKEN=<github fine-grained PAT>
```

- `DROPLET_API_URL` / `DROPLET_API_TOKEN` ŌĆö Prod droplet cmd-api. Used by `scripts/remote.sh`.
- `LATEST_DROPLET_API_URL` / `LATEST_DROPLET_API_TOKEN` ŌĆö Latest (canary) droplet cmd-api. Used by `scripts/remote-latest.sh`.
- `DIGITAL_OCEAN_TOKEN` ŌĆö DigitalOcean API token. Used when creating / managing droplets (e.g. spinning up a fresh latest droplet via cloud-init).
- `VERCEL_API_TOKEN` ŌĆö Authenticate requests to the [Vercel REST API](https://vercel.com/docs/rest-api) for managing frontend deployments.
- `GITHUB_API_TOKEN` ŌĆö GitHub fine-grained Personal Access Token scoped to `samcarey/whoeverwants`. Permissions: Pull Requests (R/W), Issues (Read), Contents (R/W), Commit Statuses (Read), Actions (Read). Used for creating PRs, reading issues, and checking CI status via the GitHub REST API. Note: webhook admin is NOT in the scope, so adding/editing GitHub webhooks must be done manually in the GitHub UI.

> **SECURITY**: These tokens must NEVER be committed to git ŌĆö not in CLAUDE.md, `.env`, or any tracked file. Store them only in environment variables. The droplet token was previously leaked via a git commit (fa805e7), leading to a Kinsing cryptominer compromise that required a full droplet rebuild (old IP 157.245.129.162 ŌåÆ current 142.93.60.29).

### Security Hardening

The droplet is hardened with:
- **UFW firewall**: Only ports 22 (SSH), 80 (HTTP), 443 (HTTPS) are open
- **SSH**: Password auth disabled, key-only login (`PermitRootLogin prohibit-password`)
- **cmd-api**: Request logging (timestamp, IP, command) and rate limiting (60 req/min per IP)
- **FastAPI**: Rate limiting (120 GET/min, 30 POST/min per IP)
- **Automated backups**: Daily pg_dump at 3 AM, 14-day retention
- **Health checks**: Every 5 minutes with auto-recovery

### Development Workflow

**Full-Stack Dev Servers** (auto-deployed per-branch on push, hosted on the Mac mini ŌĆö see the "Mac Mini Dev Box" section below for the architecture):
1. **Write code** in this environment (Claude Code sandbox)
2. **Commit and push** to GitHub
3. GitHub webhook on the Mac creates/updates the dev server for THIS branch
4. Your dev site URL is derived from the branch name: `<branch-slug>.dev.whoeverwants.com`

Each dev server gets its own:
- **Next.js frontend** on port 3001-3010 (in-VM, fronted by Caddy)
- **FastAPI backend** on port 8000 (container-internal)
- **PostgreSQL database** (separate DB in the shared PostgreSQL container, named `dev_<branch_slug_underscored>`)
- **All migrations from the branch** auto-applied on creation and update

**Frontend** (Vercel):
- Single Vercel project (`prj_07PAXGI2wG74cGRKREB0BiIDUWSn`); same build artifact serves both tiers.
- Push to `main` ŌåÆ Vercel builds + aliases the deployment to `latest.whoeverwants.com`.
- Publishing a GitHub Release ŌåÆ Vercel alias for `whoeverwants.com` is moved to that build (release deployment promoted to prod).
- API destination is selected at request time via `host`-conditional rewrites in `next.config.ts`: `latest.whoeverwants.com` ŌåÆ `api.latest.whoeverwants.com`; everything else ŌåÆ `api.whoeverwants.com` (or branch preview for non-main builds). **As of May 2026 the browser BYPASSES these rewrites** (see next bullet); the rewrites remain wired up for dev mode and as the SSR fallback.
- **Browser-to-API calls bypass Vercel's edge proxy in production builds (May 2026 onward).** `lib/api/_internal.ts: computeApiOrigin` returns an absolute URL in production browser builds (host-conditional: `whoeverwants.com` ŌåÆ `https://api.whoeverwants.com`, `latest.whoeverwants.com` ŌåÆ `https://api.latest.whoeverwants.com`, branch preview ŌåÆ `https://<slug>.api.whoeverwants.com`) and an empty string ("relative") in dev so the per-branch Mac dev server's Next.js rewrite to the in-container FastAPI keeps working. SSR keeps its existing absolute-URL branch (unchanged). The bypass is forced by a Vercel-side regression: starting May 13 2026, Let's Encrypt rolled out new "Generation Y" intermediates (E5ŌĆōE9 ECDSA, R10ŌĆōR14 RSA ŌĆö including the now-default E8 and R12) following a halt-and-reissue incident on May 8 caused by missing `id-kp-serverAuth` EKU fields per new CA/B Forum rules. Vercel's edge proxy then fails the TLS handshake to upstream targets signed by the new intermediates on roughly 5ŌĆō10% of US POPs, returning `ROUTER_EXTERNAL_TARGET_HANDSHAKE_ERROR` 502s on every `/api/*` rewrite (the certs themselves are universally trusted by every standard TLS client ŌĆö curl, browsers, mobile WebViews; the bug is specifically in Vercel's edge trust store). Multiple Vercel Pro customers reported it on community.vercel.com, no fix as of the original switch. Going direct via CORS sidesteps the broken hop entirely. The FastAPI's CORS config (`allow_origins=["*"]`, `allow_credentials=False`) handles cross-origin POSTs cleanly; `X-Browser-Id` is the identity header (not a cookie), so the no-credentials preflight is the simple one. **Three image / direct-fetch URL builders also use `API_ORIGIN`** (`buildGroupImageUrl` in `lib/groupUtils.ts`, `buildUserImageUrl` in `lib/api/users.ts`, the log-forwarder POST target in `lib/clientLogForwarder.ts`) ŌĆö `<img src>` and the forwarder's `fetch keepalive` call don't go through `fetchWithBase`, so they need the prefix explicitly. Next.js rewrites in `next.config.ts` are kept intact for dev; in prod the browser just never matches them. **Reversible**: when Vercel ships the trust-store fix, revert this change to restore same-origin proxy. Anchor symptom for "is the Vercel proxy broken again?": every `/api/*` POST to `https://whoeverwants.com/api/*` returns 502 with body `An error occurred with this application. ROUTER_EXTERNAL_TARGET_HANDSHAKE_ERROR <region>::<request-id>`, while the same call to `https://api.whoeverwants.com/api/*` directly returns 200/201 from the same network. Don't reintroduce relative `/api/*` URLs in code paths the browser uses in prod (inline `fetch('/api/...')`, `<img src="/api/...">`) without first checking whether the Vercel-edge regression has actually been fixed. Diagnostic: compare cert intermediate (`echo | openssl s_client -connect api.whoeverwants.com:443 | openssl x509 -noout -issuer`) against the canary's working cert ŌĆö anything not E7 or older is a regression candidate. **The `/api/git-info` route is the exception**: it's a Next.js route handler (`app/api/git-info/route.ts`) served by the same Vercel deployment, no external proxy ŌĆö keep that fetch relative.
- **`/api/(.*)` MUST NOT carry a blanket `Cache-Control: public, max-age=N`.** Most API endpoints are identity-dependent ŌĆö `/api/groups/by-route-id/{id}`, `/api/groups/mine`, `/api/users/me/*` all partition by the `X-Browser-Id` request header. Without `Vary: X-Browser-Id`, any cache (Vercel edge, iOS WKWebView's HTTP cache, intermediate proxies) keys on URL alone and serves one user's response to every other user. Symptom found in `claude/fix-ios-poll-visibility-nmSFA`: iOS TestFlight user creates a poll in a previously-empty group, navigates home ŌåÆ group, sees the empty-group placeholder for up to 2 hours because the WebView cached the pre-creation `[]` response from `/api/groups/by-route-id/~6`. The home page was correct (POST responses aren't normally cached), the group page wasn't (GET on a URL that returned `[]` was cached). Fixed by removing the `/api/(.*)` headers block in `next.config.ts` ŌĆö the upstream FastAPI sets `Cache-Control: public, max-age=31536000, immutable` only on image bytes endpoints (groups + users image GETs); everything else passes through with no Cache-Control header, which means no caching at the CDN/WebView layer. If a future API endpoint genuinely benefits from caching, set the header on the FastAPI response directly with appropriate `Vary` ŌĆö don't reintroduce the blanket Next.js rule. **`Vary: X-Browser-Id` alone isn't a clean solution either**: cache partitions per browser_id explode to millions of entries on the CDN and provide no actual reuse. Identity-dependent endpoints want `no-store` semantics, which is what they get with no header set.
- **Trailing asterisks are stripped from page URLs by `middleware.ts` (308 redirect).** Links to the site frequently get pasted with accidental trailing `**` ŌĆö a Markdown-bolded URL `**https://whoeverwants.com/g/~6/p/D**` leaks the closing `**` onto the end of the real URL. The Next.js middleware tests `request.nextUrl.href` against `/(?:\*|%2[Aa])+$/` (covers literal `*` AND percent-encoded `%2A`, on either the path or query-string end, since the junk is always at the very end of the URL) and redirects to the stripped URL. Safe because no real route ends in an asterisk (short_ids are base62 + `~`). The matcher excludes `api/`, `_next/`, `favicon.ico`, and any path with a file extension. This is the project's ONLY `middleware.ts` ŌĆö if you add other middleware concerns, fold them into the same `middleware` function rather than adding a second file (Next.js supports only one).
- **Deployment Protection / Vercel SSO is OFF (`ssoProtection: null`).** Because `productionBranch=production` and `latest.whoeverwants.com` tracks `main`, Vercel classifies the `latest` alias as a preview deployment ŌĆö so any SSO setting that protects previews (including the default `prod_deployment_urls_and_all_previews`) gates `latest` with an "Authenticating..." splash on first load. We accept that PR preview URLs (`<branch>-<hash>.vercel.app`) are publicly reachable as the cost of keeping `latest` open. To toggle: `curl -X PATCH -H "Authorization: Bearer $VERCEL_API_TOKEN" -H "Content-Type: application/json" https://api.vercel.com/v9/projects/prj_07PAXGI2wG74cGRKREB0BiIDUWSn -d '{"ssoProtection": null}'` (off) / `-d '{"ssoProtection": {"deploymentType": "prod_deployment_urls_and_all_previews"}}'` (on). No Vercel setting splits PR previews from the `latest` alias ŌĆö they're both "previews" to Vercel.

**Latest tier ŌĆö canary backend** (Python API on `latest` droplet, auto-deployed on push to `main`):
- Push to `main` fires the GitHub webhook ŌåÆ `hooks.api.latest.whoeverwants.com` ŌåÆ `scripts/dev-webhook.py` (reads `/etc/droplet-label=latest`) ŌåÆ `git pull origin main` ŌåÆ `docker compose up -d --build` ŌåÆ apply pending migrations ŌåÆ `/health` verify.
- Deploy logs: `bash scripts/remote-latest.sh "tail -50 /var/log/dev-webhook.log" /root`
- Manual rebuild: `bash scripts/remote-latest.sh "docker compose up -d --build" /root/whoeverwants`
- API logs: `bash scripts/remote-latest.sh "docker compose logs --tail 100" /root/whoeverwants`

**Production backend** (Python API on `whoeverwants` droplet, auto-deployed only on GitHub Release):
- Publishing a non-draft / non-prerelease GitHub Release fires the webhook ŌåÆ `hooks.api.whoeverwants.com` ŌåÆ `scripts/dev-webhook.py` (reads `/etc/droplet-label=""`) ŌåÆ `git fetch --tags && git checkout tags/<release-tag>` ŌåÆ `docker compose up -d --build` ŌåÆ apply pending migrations ŌåÆ `/health` verify. Push events to `main` are explicitly ignored on this tier.
- Deploy logs: `bash scripts/remote.sh "tail -50 /var/log/dev-webhook.log" /root`
- Manual rebuild: `bash scripts/remote.sh "docker compose up -d --build" /root/whoeverwants`
- API logs: `bash scripts/remote.sh "docker compose logs --tail 100" /root/whoeverwants`
- **To ship**: cut a GitHub Release. The release's tag must exist on `main` (or any branch ŌĆö but the convention is to publish from a `main` commit that's already running cleanly on `latest.whoeverwants.com`).
- **Auto-deploy can silently fail on uncommitted local mods.** The webhook does a plain `git pull`; if the droplet's `/root/whoeverwants` checkout has any unstaged file (typically `scripts/dev-server-manager.sh` after a hotfix), the pull aborts with `error: Your local changes to the following files would be overwritten by merge`, the webhook logs the failure but the deploy "completes" with no rebuild. Vercel meanwhile auto-deploys the new FE ŌåÆ FE/API contract drift. Symptom from a recent occurrence (#290 deploy stuck): every `POST /api/polls` with `group_id: <uuid>` came back with a brand-new group_id in the response ŌĆö the old server didn't read `group_id` at all (still expected the retired `follow_up_to` field), so polls "disappeared" into freshly-minted groups. Diagnostic: `tail /var/log/dev-webhook.log | grep -A3 'Git pull failed'` to spot the blocking file; on the droplet, `cd /root/whoeverwants && git status` to confirm; `git log --oneline -3` to confirm the actual deployed commit. Fix: stash the local diff, `git pull`, apply any pending migrations, `docker compose up -d --build`. Recovery for orphaned data: any group minted while the deploy was stale needs to be merged into its intended group (`UPDATE polls SET group_id = <real> WHERE group_id = <orphan>`, then `DELETE FROM groups WHERE id = <orphan>`).
- **Defensive log when requested `group_id` is unknown.** `_resolve_or_create_group` in `server/routers/polls.py` emits a `WARNING` when `req.group_id` is provided but no matching `groups` row exists. The mint-fresh-group fallback is intentional (per the function's docstring) but a sustained stream of these warnings is a tripwire for: (a) a stale deploy missing a schema migration, (b) the FE sending a stale/cached group_id from before a forget+re-discover cycle, (c) cross-group races. Surface via `bash scripts/remote.sh "docker compose logs --tail 200 api | grep 'group_id'"` when investigating "polls landing in the wrong group" reports.

You do NOT need SSH ŌĆö all server management goes through `scripts/remote.sh`.

**Per-Branch Dev Servers** (automatic on push, hosted on the Mac mini Colima VM):
- Every push to GitHub auto-creates/updates the dev server FOR THE PUSHED BRANCH via the Mac webhook (recreates the container so env/labels are fresh)
- Frontend uses `next dev` with `PYTHON_API_URL` pointing to the in-container API
- API runs via `uv run uvicorn` with `DATABASE_URL` pointing to the per-branch dev database
- Migrations from the branch are auto-applied to the dev database on each update
- **After pushing, wait for the dev server to be ready.** The server takes ~30-60 seconds (longer on first push for a brand-new branch: full git clone + `npm ci` + `uv sync`). Question with `bash scripts/remote-mac.sh "curl -s -o /dev/null -w '%{http_code}' http://localhost:<port>"` until it returns 200, or just hit the public URL.
- URL is derived from the branch name (DNS-label-safe slug): `<branch-slug>.dev.whoeverwants.com`
  - Example: branch `claude/migrate-foo` ŌåÆ `https://claude-migrate-foo.dev.whoeverwants.com`
  - Slug rules: lowercase, non-[a-z0-9-] ŌåÆ `-`, runs collapsed, trimmed, truncated to 50 chars
- URL changes per branch ŌĆö switching branches means a new URL. Bookmarking your CURRENT branch's URL is fine but stale once you cut a new branch.
- The `main` branch is explicitly skipped (it's the prod branch on the droplet; never aged out by 7d-idle, would consume resources forever).
- Author emails are no longer used as a signal; bot-authored pushes get a dev server like any other push.
- Dev servers are fully isolated ŌĆö each has its own container, API, and database.
- **Capacity is `MAX_DEV_SERVERS=15`** (`scripts/mac-mini/dev-server-manager.sh`). When a push would exceed it, `evict_excess_servers` reclaims the least-recently-UPDATED branch's server (container + volume + Postgres DB), so an evicted branch loses its seeded demo data ŌĆö re-upsert + re-seed to bring it back (`dev-server-manager.sh upsert <branch>`). `FRONTEND_PORT_MAX` is DERIVED as `FRONTEND_PORT_START + MAX_DEV_SERVERS - 1` (one published host port per server, range `3001ŌĆō3015`) so the port range can't drift below the server cap. The manager is bind-mounted (`./scripts:/opt/scripts:ro`), so deploying it via `scripts/mac-deploy.sh ... /Users/sccarey/devbox/scripts/dev-server-manager.sh 755` takes effect immediately ŌĆö no rebuild.
- **Lifecycle**: auto-cleaned after 7 days of inactivity, evicted when capacity (15) is exceeded (LRU by last-updated), OR immediately destroyed when the branch is deleted from GitHub (the `delete` event triggers `destroy <branch>`). When the branch is deleted: container + volume + Postgres DB + Caddy snippet are all torn down.
- **Dev-server saturation playbook (sketchy demo links: slow loads, stuck Next.js "rendering", white screens, spontaneous page refreshes).** Diagnosed June 2026. These symptoms are almost always the Mac VM being out of memory, NOT a code bug. Triage from the sandbox: `bash scripts/remote-mac.sh "free -h"` (look for near-zero `available` + `Swap: 0`), `docker stats --no-stream` (each `next dev` container is ~650ŌĆō800 MB), and `dev-server-manager.sh list` (is the box pinned at the 15 cap? is YOUR branch even present, or has it been LRU-evicted?). SymptomŌåÆcause map: slow loads / long "rendering" = `next dev` compile-on-demand thrashing for the last scraps of RAM; white screen = your server was LRU-evicted (link 502s, no upstream) OR a Next.js process got OOM-reaped mid-request (no swap ŌćÆ the kernel kills instead of degrading); spontaneous refresh = HMR full-reload when an OOM-killed `next dev` restarts and the HMR websocket reconnects (the Turbopack-cache-poison reload loop from a route rename looks identical ŌĆö see the `.next`-wipe pitfall in the Dev Server Pitfalls section). **Root cause of the chronic version**: `delete_branch_on_merge` was OFF on the repo, so merging a PR never deleted the branch, so the `delete`ŌåÆ`destroy` webhook never fired ŌĆö merged-branch servers lingered until the slow 7-day idle timer or LRU eviction, keeping the box pinned at the 15 cap and constantly evicting genuinely-active branches. **Fixes applied**: (1) enable repo Settings ŌåÆ General ŌåÆ "Automatically delete head branches" (the `$GITHUB_API_TOKEN` PAT 403s on repo-settings writes ŌĆö must be done in the GitHub UI); (2) bulk-delete stale branches via `DELETE /repos/.../git/refs/heads/<branch>` (Contents scope DOES work ŌĆö deletion fires the `destroy` webhook, reaping container+volume+DB+Caddy snippet; exclude `main`/`production`/`archive/*`/your current branch; with 0 open PRs every branch is merged-or-abandoned so age is a safe "dead" signal); (3) the box's real ceiling was RAM ŌĆö Colima was 12 GB with **zero swap** for 15 servers. Resize from the **Mac host** (NOT reachable via `remote-mac.sh` ŌĆö `colima` is a host process, the cmd-api lives inside the VM): `colima stop -p devbox && colima start -p devbox --memory 24 --cpu 6 --disk 80` (the Mac has 32 GB; pass cpu/disk so they aren't reset; this restarts the VM ŌĆö compose services + per-branch containers auto-restart on the next boot, ~36s). After the resize `free -h` showed `available` 218 MB ŌåÆ 10.3 G.

```bash
# List active dev servers (one row per branch)
bash scripts/remote-mac.sh "bash /opt/scripts/dev-server-manager.sh list"

# Manually trigger a dev server update for a branch
bash scripts/remote-mac.sh "bash /opt/scripts/dev-server-manager.sh upsert claude/my-branch" / 600

# Destroy a dev server by branch name (also drops its DB / volume / Caddy snippet)
bash scripts/remote-mac.sh "bash /opt/scripts/dev-server-manager.sh destroy claude/my-branch"

# Destroy by raw slug (when the branch name is no longer known)
bash scripts/remote-mac.sh "bash /opt/scripts/dev-server-manager.sh destroy-slug claude-my-branch"

# Check dev container logs
bash scripts/remote-mac.sh "docker logs whoeverwants-dev-<slug> --tail 50"

# Check dev API logs (inside the container's /repo volume)
bash scripts/remote-mac.sh "docker exec whoeverwants-dev-<slug> tail -50 /repo/api.log"
```

**Preview Environments** (per-branch API testing):
1. **Push branch** to GitHub
2. **Create preview API**: `bash scripts/deploy-preview.sh` (or manually via `scripts/remote.sh`)
3. Preview APIs are auto-cleaned after 7 days

```bash
# Quick deploy preview for current branch
bash scripts/deploy-preview.sh

# Or manually manage previews on the droplet
bash scripts/remote.sh "bash /root/whoeverwants/scripts/preview-manager.sh list"
bash scripts/remote.sh "bash /root/whoeverwants/scripts/preview-manager.sh destroy <slug>"
```

### Creating Pull Requests

The `gh` CLI is **not available** in this environment. Use the GitHub REST API with `curl` and `$GITHUB_API_TOKEN` instead:

```bash
curl -s -X POST \
  -H "Authorization: token $GITHUB_API_TOKEN" \
  -H "Accept: application/vnd.github+json" \
  https://api.github.com/repos/samcarey/whoeverwants/pulls \
  -d '{
    "title": "PR title here",
    "head": "branch-name",
    "base": "main",
    "body": "## Summary\n- Change 1\n- Change 2\n\n## Test plan\n- [ ] Test item"
  }'
```

The response JSON contains `html_url` with the PR link. Extract it with:

```bash
| python3 -c "import sys,json; print(json.load(sys.stdin)['html_url'])"
```

### Droplet Setup & Provisioning

Full setup documentation is in **[docs/droplet-setup.md](./docs/droplet-setup.md)**. To provision a new droplet from scratch:

```bash
ssh root@<DROPLET_IP> 'bash -s' < scripts/provision-droplet.sh <API_TOKEN>
```

This installs Docker, Caddy, the command execution API, clones the repo, starts all services, and applies database migrations.

### Important Notes
- Each droplet has its own clone of this repo at `/root/whoeverwants`. Never transfer files manually ŌĆö commit here, pull there. Different deploy triggers per tier (push to main vs release published).
- The remote execution API has a configurable timeout (default 120s, max via 3rd arg)
- The API returns stdout, stderr, and exit code for every command

### Latest-Tier Rollout ŌĆö Status

The two-tier deploy is wired end-to-end. Status of each piece:

| Step | What | Status |
|------|------|--------|
| 1 | DNS for `api.latest.whoeverwants.com`, `hooks.api.latest.whoeverwants.com`, `latest.whoeverwants.com` | Ō£ģ done (Route 53) |
| 2 | Vercel project: `productionBranch=production`, `latest.whoeverwants.com` domain with `gitBranch=main` | Ō£ģ done (via undocumented `PATCH /v9/projects/<id>/branch` + `POST /v10/projects/<id>/domains`) |
| 3 | `production` branch on origin (created from current main HEAD) | Ō£ģ done |
| 4 | `.github/workflows/release-to-production.yml` (on `release: published` ŌåÆ force-push tag commit to `production`) | Ō£ģ done |
| 5a | GitHub webhook for the latest droplet (`hooks.api.latest.whoeverwants.com`, push + release events) | Ō£ģ done (user added in GitHub UI) |
| 5b | Existing prod-droplet GitHub webhook (`hooks.api.whoeverwants.com`) ŌĆö confirm subscribed to **Releases** in addition to **Pushes** | ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ manual check ŌĆö the PAT lacks `admin:repo_hook`, so verify in the GitHub UI |
| 6 | Prod droplet cutover (restart `dev-webhook` to pick up label-aware code) | ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ manual ŌĆö after PR merges; see below |

**6. Prod droplet cutover** ŌĆö the prod droplet's `dev-webhook.service` is still running the OLD code (pre-this-PR) which deploys on every push to main. After this branch merges:
1. The prod webhook will deploy main one last time using its old behavior ŌĆö this lands the new `dev-webhook.py` (label-aware) on disk at `/root/whoeverwants/scripts/dev-webhook.py`, but the systemd service is still running the old code in memory.
2. From the dev env: `bash scripts/remote.sh "touch /etc/droplet-label && chmod 644 /etc/droplet-label && systemctl restart dev-webhook"` ŌĆö creates the empty label marker (prod tier = empty string) and restarts the service. From here on, push to main is ignored on prod; only `release: published` events deploy.

### How a release will flow once the cutover is complete

1. Tag a commit on `main` (or wherever) and publish a non-draft / non-prerelease GitHub Release.
2. The `release-to-production.yml` workflow fires ŌåÆ force-pushes the tag's commit to the `production` branch.
3. Vercel sees a push to `production` ŌåÆ builds a production deployment ŌåÆ moves the `whoeverwants.com` alias to it (since `productionBranch=production`, that's the prod alias target).
4. In parallel, the prod droplet's `dev-webhook` receives the `release.published` event from GitHub ŌåÆ `git fetch --tags && git checkout tags/<tag>` ŌåÆ `docker compose up -d --build` ŌåÆ applies pending migrations ŌåÆ `/health` check.
5. The `latest` droplet ignores the release event (its label is `latest`). It only redeploys on push to `main`; this push, the next push, every push.

## Mac Mini Dev Box

The dev-server side of the system runs on a Mac mini at home (`samcarey@mini4`, public IP `65.28.10.210`, Apple M4, 32 GB RAM, macOS 26). Production API stays on the droplet ŌĆö only per-branch dev servers run here.

**Status: dev-server-manager ported + rekeyed to per-branch, end-to-end working.** Running:
- Colima VM (Apple Virtualization Framework, 6 CPU / 24 GB / 80 GB) as Claude's sandbox (raised from 12 GB ŌåÆ 24 GB in June 2026 ŌĆö see the "Dev-server saturation" pitfall below)
- Per-hostname HTTPS at `*.dev.whoeverwants.com` via home-router port forwarding (80/443) ŌåÆ Caddy on Mac ŌåÆ containers in VM
- DDNS (launchd ŌåÆ AWS Route 53) keeping both `mac-test.dev` and the `*.dev` wildcard A records self-healing
- `cmd-api.dev.whoeverwants.com` ŌĆö ClaudeŌåÆVM control endpoint, same model as droplet's cmd-api
- `webhook.dev.whoeverwants.com` ŌĆö GitHub push + delete receiver, HMAC-verified, dispatches to `dev-server-manager.sh`
- `mac-test.dev.whoeverwants.com` ŌĆö placeholder serving nginx
- Postgres 16 in VM (persistent volume, network-only) ŌĆö one DB per branch
- One `whoeverwants-dev-<branch-slug>` container per open branch (Next.js + uvicorn together) spawned by `dev-server-manager.sh`

**Where to look:**
- `docs/mac-mini-setup.md` ŌĆö full reproduction guide
- `docs/mac-mini-next-steps.md` ŌĆö historical record of the deferred decisions; this branch resolves them
- `scripts/mac-mini/` ŌĆö production source files (cmd-api.py, webhook.py, Dockerfiles, ddns, Caddyfile, compose, LaunchAgent plists, dev-server-manager.sh, devserver-entrypoint.sh, caddy-watch.sh, caddy-watchdog.sh + `com.whoeverwants.caddy-watchdog.plist`)
- `scripts/remote-mac.sh` ŌĆö analogous to `scripts/remote.sh`; drives cmd-api over HTTPS
- `scripts/mac-deploy.sh` ŌĆö file-deploy helper (uses cmd-api + colima's `/Users` auto-mount to write `~/devbox/`)

**Calling cmd-api on the Mac mini** (analogous to `bash scripts/remote.sh` for the droplet) ŌĆö set in your shell:
```
export MAC_API_URL=https://cmd-api.dev.whoeverwants.com
export MAC_API_TOKEN=<CMD_API_TOKEN value in ~/devbox/.env on the Mac>
bash scripts/remote-mac.sh "hostname; docker ps"
```

The cmd-api lives in the VM, not on the Mac host. **Mac filesystem access from the VM**: Colima auto-mounts `/Users` into the VM RW via virtiofs, so cmd-api can read/write `~/devbox/` (and `~/Library/LaunchAgents/`) by spawning a sibling container with `-v /Users:/Users`. Anything outside `/Users` (notably `/opt/homebrew/etc/Caddyfile`) is not reachable from the VM and needs a Mac-side action. `scripts/mac-deploy.sh` encapsulates the `/Users` write pattern.

**Per-branch dev server architecture**:
- Each open branch = one Docker container `whoeverwants-dev-<branch-slug>` running Next.js (port 3000) + uvicorn (port 8000) together
- Per-branch Docker volume `whoeverwants-dev-repo-<branch-slug>` mounted at `/repo` preserves node_modules / .venv / .next across restarts within a branch's lifetime
- Per-branch Postgres DB `dev_<branch_slug_underscored>` in the shared `devbox-postgres-1` container; migrations applied by the manager from the branch's checkout
- Container's port 3000 published to VM `127.0.0.1:<3001-3010>`; Colima auto-forwards to Mac `localhost:<same port>`
- Caddy snippet at `~/devbox/caddy.d/<branch-slug>.caddy` routes `<branch-slug>.dev.whoeverwants.com` to that port; the `com.devbox.caddy-watch.plist` LaunchAgent polls the dir every 5s and runs `caddy reload`
- `dev-server-manager.sh` runs inside cmd-api OR webhook (both mount `/host-caddy.d`) and orchestrates the lifecycle. Lives at `~/devbox/scripts/dev-server-manager.sh` on the Mac, mounted at `/opt/scripts/dev-server-manager.sh` inside the containers.
- Webhook receives the GitHub `push` event and calls `bash $MANAGER_CMD upsert <branch>`; receives the GitHub `delete` event (or a `push` payload with `deleted: true`) and calls `bash $MANAGER_CMD destroy <branch>`. Failures are logged + swallowed. The `main` branch is filtered out on both paths (production-only; the manager double-enforces).
- Branch-name slugification (in `branch_to_slug`): lowercase ŌåÆ non-`[a-z0-9-]` ŌåÆ `-` ŌåÆ collapse `-` runs ŌåÆ trim ŌåÆ truncate to 50 chars. So `claude/migrate-foo` becomes `claude-migrate-foo`; the resulting hostname is `claude-migrate-foo.dev.whoeverwants.com`.
- **RESOLVED (container-name clobber in `evict_excess_servers` ŌĆö root cause of dev servers serving under the WRONG container name + getting reclaimed by a sibling branch). Retained as the canonical writeup of the bash dynamic-scope foot-gun.** The original bug: `evict_excess_servers` (`scripts/mac-mini/dev-server-manager.sh`) ran `while IFS= read -r container ...; do ... done <<< "$victims"` with `container` NOT declared `local`. Because bash is dynamically scoped, that loop assigned to `cmd_upsert`'s `container` (set at the top of `cmd_upsert` from the slug). So whenever eviction actually fires (`effective_total > MAX_DEV_SERVERS` ŌĆö i.e. the box is busy with several branches), `cmd_upsert` falls through to `docker run --name "$container"` using the LAST evicted victim's container name instead of the upserted slug's name. The `volume` / `db_name` / `BRANCH` env are separate locals and stay correct, so the launched container serves the RIGHT branch's code + DB but wears a SIBLING slug's name. Blast radius: (1) the `=== Dev server ready ===` summary prints the wrong `Container:` line (the giveaway ŌĆö `Branch`/`Database`/`URL` are correct, `Container` names a different branch); (2) the container is undiscoverable by its own slug (`docker inspect whoeverwants-dev-<slug>` fails) so it's an orphan; (3) the Caddy snippet for the correct slug still points at the right port, so the site works *until* the branch whose name was borrowed gets upserted ŌĆö that branch's `cmd_upsert` does `docker stop/rm whoeverwants-dev-<borrowed-name>` and destroys the mis-named container, 502-ing the victim hostname (and vanishing any static files served into it, e.g. demo screenshots under `public/screenshots/`). Observed 2026-05-25 on `claude/poll-detail-new-options-banner-6NzPz`: its container came up named `whoeverwants-dev-claude-ios-app-title-truncation-jylpb`, then died when that branch was next pushed. **Fix (shipped):** the eviction loop var was renamed to `victim` and declared `local victims victim victim_slug` so it can't alias `cmd_upsert`'s `container`, with the explanatory comment kept inline. The belt-and-suspenders assertion is in place too ŌĆö after `docker run`, `cmd_upsert` checks the launched container's name equals `$(slug_to_container "$slug")` and `docker rm -f`s + fails loudly otherwise. **Audit (shipped):** every other `while read -r container` / `for container in ...` loop in the manager now declares its loop vars `local` (`is_skipped_branch`'s `skip`, `apply_dev_migrations`'s `f`/`basename`, and the `cmd_list` / `cmd_destroy_all` / `cmd_cleanup_old` / `cmd_revive` command paths). The first two run inside `cmd_upsert`'s dynamic scope so the `local` is load-bearing; the four `cmd_*` command paths don't run inside `cmd_upsert` today, but declaring their vars `local` is the belt-and-suspenders that immunizes them against a future refactor that calls them mid-upsert. The lone exception left alone is `find_available_port`'s `while read -r c`, which is inside a `$(... | while ...)` command-substitution subshell so it can't leak regardless. Regression-tested via a stub-`docker` harness that asserts none of the five loop functions clobber a caller's `container`/`slug`/`port` locals (the pre-fix version fails all five; the fixed version passes). **General rule for this file: declare every loop variable `local` ŌĆö bash's dynamic scoping makes an undeclared loop var in any function reachable from `cmd_upsert` a latent clobber of `cmd_upsert`'s `container`/`port`/`slug`/`volume`/`db_name` locals.**

**GitHub webhook subscription**: must include BOTH `push` AND `delete` events. The legacy migration enabled only `push`; the `delete`-event branch teardown only fires when the subscription is widened (Webhooks ŌåÆ Edit ŌåÆ Individual events ŌåÆ "Branch or tag creation/deletion"). Without the subscription update, deleted branches age out via the 7d-idle path instead of being torn down immediately.

**Cutover from per-author keying**: the per-branch manager uses the same container-name prefix (`whoeverwants-dev-`) and same volume prefix (`whoeverwants-dev-repo-`) so legacy per-author entries are visible to `list` / `destroy-all`, but their slugs no longer correspond to any branch. Run once at deploy time to wipe them: `bash scripts/remote-mac.sh "bash /opt/scripts/dev-server-manager.sh destroy-all"`. After that, the next push to each branch repopulates per-branch.

**Operational commands** (via remote-mac.sh):
```bash
bash scripts/remote-mac.sh "bash /opt/scripts/dev-server-manager.sh list"
bash scripts/remote-mac.sh "bash /opt/scripts/dev-server-manager.sh destroy <branch>"          # by branch name
bash scripts/remote-mac.sh "bash /opt/scripts/dev-server-manager.sh destroy-slug <slug>"      # by raw slug
bash scripts/remote-mac.sh "docker logs whoeverwants-dev-<branch-slug> --tail 50"
bash scripts/remote-mac.sh "docker exec devbox-postgres-1 psql -U whoeverwants -c '\\l'"
```

**Pitfalls learned during the port:**
- **Caddy on the Mac host is the single failure surface for ALL three `*.dev.whoeverwants.com` hostnames (`cmd-api`, `webhook`, `mac-test`).** Containers in the devbox VM stay healthy while Caddy is down, but every external request 503s with Envoy `upstream connect error ... connection timeout` (the sandbox egress's signature failure) ŌĆö which looks identical to "Mac is offline." Diagnostic: `bash scripts/remote.sh "hostname"` succeeds (prod droplet reachable, so egress is fine) ŌåÆ DNS resolves to the home IP via Cloudflare DoH (Route 53 healthy) ŌåÆ but `https://mac-test.dev.whoeverwants.com/` times out at TCP. If ALL three Mac hosts time out and DigitalOcean droplets are reachable, the Mac itself (or its router / DDNS / Caddy) is the issue ŌĆö not the wider network. Triage on the Mac: `curl ifconfig.me` (WAN IP matches DNS?) ŌåÆ `colima -p devbox status` (VM up?) ŌåÆ `DOCKER_HOST=unix:///Users/sccarey/.colima/devbox/docker.sock docker ps` (containers up?) ŌåÆ `brew services list | grep caddy` (Caddy service status; "none" = dead). Homebrew's stock `homebrew.mxcl.caddy` plist sets `KeepAlive = { SuccessfulExit: false }` ŌĆö clean SIGTERMs (App Nap, manual stop, system trigger) AND launchd crash-loop throttling both leave Caddy dead with no auto-restart. **Durable fix shipped:** `scripts/mac-mini/caddy-watchdog.sh` + `scripts/mac-mini/com.whoeverwants.caddy-watchdog.plist` ŌĆö a system LaunchDaemon at `/Library/LaunchDaemons/com.whoeverwants.caddy-watchdog.plist` that polls every 60s, checks `pgrep -x caddy && nc -z 127.0.0.1 443`, and `launchctl kickstart -k system/homebrew.mxcl.caddy`s on failure (catches clean exits, throttling, AND hung-but-running where the process exists but the socket is dead). Restart events log to `/var/log/caddy-watchdog.log`; quiet otherwise. Install steps in `docs/mac-mini-setup.md` ┬¦ 9b2. **Pitfall when pasting plists through chat:** chat-clients auto-bracket URLs in heredoc bodies, so a `<!DOCTYPE plist PUBLIC ... "http://...">` line becomes `<!DOCTYPE plist PUBLIC ... "<http://...>">` which breaks XML parsing (`plutil -lint` reports "Unexpected character"). Modern macOS accepts plists without the DOCTYPE; omit it. AND ampersands inside `<string>` bodies (the `&&` and `2>&1` of a shell command) need XML-escaping or break parsing too ŌĆö cleanest workaround is to move the script body to a separate `.sh` file and have ProgramArguments call it.
- **The Colima `devbox` VM is Caddy's upstream and the SECOND single failure surface ŌĆö when it crashes, Caddy stays up and every `*.dev.whoeverwants.com` host 502s (incl. `cmd-api`/`webhook`, so `remote-mac.sh` itself goes unreachable and you can't fix it from the sandbox).** Caddy-up-but-502 (vs a TCP timeout) is the tell that the *upstream* ŌĆö the VM or its containers ŌĆö is down, not Caddy. Observed 2026-06: the VM exited uncleanly, then a plain `colima start -p devbox` failed with `failed to attach disk "colima-devbox", in use by instance "colima-devbox"` ŌĆö a zombie lima/vz process from the unclean exit still held the disk-image lock. The manual recovery (the canonical sequence) is `colima stop -p devbox -f; pkill -f colima-devbox; sleep 3; colima start -p devbox` (the `pkill` releases the lock; the compose services + per-branch dev containers auto-restart on boot). **Root cause + contributing factor:** there was NO VM-level watchdog (caddy-watchdog only restarts Caddy, which was already up ŌĆö its `nc -z 443` passes while the upstream is dead), and the VM ran with **zero swap** (`free -h` ŌåÆ `Swap: 0`) so a memory spike (a push triggering `npm ci` + `next dev` compiles while siblings compile) has no headroom and the macOS host can jetsam the `vz` process ŌĆö the unclean kill that strands the lock. **Durable fix shipped:** `scripts/mac-mini/colima-watchdog.sh` + `scripts/mac-mini/com.whoeverwants.colima-watchdog.plist` ŌĆö the VM-level analog of the caddy watchdog. A system LaunchDaemon running **as the devbox owner** (`UserName=sccarey`, so `colima`/`docker` resolve the per-user VM state under `/Users/sccarey/.colima`) polls every 60s, probing the devbox Docker daemon via `docker ps` over its UNIX socket (the true "dev infra usable?" signal ŌĆö like caddy-watchdog probing :443, not just `pgrep`; a single down container doesn't trip it since Docker still answers); on failure it runs the force-stop + `pkill` + start recovery. Re-probes once after a 5s pause so a transient blip can't bounce a healthy VM; no lock is needed against overlapping recoveries because launchd never double-launches a `StartInterval` job while the prior run is alive (same guarantee caddy-watchdog relies on). Logs only on recovery to `~/Library/Logs/colima-watchdog.log`. Install steps + the swap recommendation in `docs/mac-mini-setup.md` ┬¦ 9b3. **Cannot be installed/tested from the sandbox** ŌĆö colima is a host process, NOT in the VM, so it's unreachable via `remote-mac.sh`/cmd-api (which die with the VM); the one-time `/Library/LaunchDaemons/` install + `launchctl bootstrap` is a Mac-host action the owner runs (same as caddy-watchdog). If VZ refuses to boot headless under a LaunchDaemon, install as a per-user LaunchAgent instead (drop the `<UserName>` key).
- **`docker build` from cmd-api reads context from cmd-api's filesystem, not the daemon's.** The cmd-api container has only `/var/run/docker.sock` mounted ŌĆö no `/Users`. To build images that reference Mac files, spawn an intermediate `docker:cli` sidecar that has BOTH `-v /Users:/Users` and `-v /var/run/docker.sock:/var/run/docker.sock`; build from there. Used in `mac-mini-setup.md` step 8 for the dev-server image build.
- **Bind paths in `docker-compose.yml` are interpreted by the daemon, NOT by the docker CLI's CWD.** When invoking compose from a sidecar with `-v /Users:/Users`, set the sidecar's working directory to the **daemon-visible path** (`-w /Users/sccarey/devbox`), not a remapped one (`-w /devbox`). Otherwise relative `./scripts` resolves to `/devbox/scripts` and the daemon can't find it. `compose config` is the canonical sanity check ŌĆö confirm `source:` fields match real VM paths before running `up -d`.
- **Recreating cmd-api kills the in-flight cmd-api request.** When `docker compose up -d cmd-api` runs from inside cmd-api, the stop step terminates the requesting process mid-flight. Workaround: launch the recreate from a detached sidecar (`docker run -d`) ŌĆö the sidecar is a sibling container and survives cmd-api's restart. Wait ~15s, then verify via `hostname` (returns a fresh container hostname).
- **`docker exec ... --format '{{ ... }}'` quoting through cmd-api eats braces.** When cmd-api hands the cmd to `subprocess.run(cmd, shell=True)`, embedded `{{ }}` survives, but single-quoted Go templates inside single-quoted shell arguments can produce empty stdout (no JSON parse ŌåÆ remote-mac.sh's `json.load` fails on empty body). Workaround: switch the outer quotes to `"` and pass the inner braces literally ŌĆö or use `--format` with no quoting and pipe through `head -c N`.
- **Smoke-test sidecars need the same mounts as cmd-api.** When running `dev-server-manager.sh upsert` from an ad-hoc `docker run` sidecar (for testing), include both `-v /Users:/Users` (so it can read repo state on the Mac) AND `-v /Users/sccarey/devbox/caddy.d:/host-caddy.d` (so caddy snippet writes land in the real Mac-visible dir). The production path goes through cmd-api or webhook which both have these mounts baked in via `docker-compose.yml`.
- **Per-branch volume + bootstrap-marker race on re-upsert.** The manager polls for `/repo/.dev-server-ready` to know when the dev-server is up. If a previous run left the marker file in the per-branch volume, the new run sees it immediately and skips waiting. Today this is harmless because the entrypoint deletes the marker on startup and the manager's downstream steps (caddy snippet write, migration apply) are idempotent. If you add side effects that need actual "this container is up RIGHT NOW", delete the marker via a one-shot `docker run --rm -v $volume:/repo alpine rm -f /repo/.dev-server-ready` BEFORE launching, then wait for it to reappear.
- **Caddy `import` only supports ONE wildcard per glob.** `import /Users/*/devbox/caddy.d/*.caddy` is rejected with `Glob pattern may only contain one wildcard (*), but has others`. Hardcode the user portion: `import /Users/sccarey/devbox/caddy.d/*.caddy`. The username is fixed per Mac install anyway, so no real flexibility lost.
- **Two GitHub webhooks during/after migration: droplet handles prod-deploy, Mac handles dev upserts/destroys.** The droplet's `dev-webhook.service` was patched in-place to short-circuit non-`main` pushes (returns `dev-side-on-mac` JSON, no upsert). The Mac webhook explicitly SKIPS the `main` branch on both push and delete (matching the manager's `SKIP_BRANCHES`) so a push to main doesn't create a `main.dev.whoeverwants.com` dev server alongside production. Both webhooks fire on every push; each handles only its scope. Don't remove the droplet webhook ŌĆö production auto-deploy still runs there. If the patch on the droplet ever drifts (`/root/whoeverwants/scripts/dev-webhook.py`), the patch marker is the `if branch != "main":` early-return block right after `log.info(f"Push to {branch} by {emails}")`.
- **Mac webhook redeploy is split across two surfaces: live-mounted script vs baked-into-image.** `dev-server-manager.sh` is bind-mounted into both cmd-api + webhook via `./scripts:/opt/scripts:ro`, so `bash scripts/mac-deploy.sh scripts/mac-mini/dev-server-manager.sh /Users/sccarey/devbox/scripts/dev-server-manager.sh 755` takes effect immediately ŌĆö no rebuild. `webhook.py` and `devserver-entrypoint.sh`, however, are `COPY`'d at image build time (`Dockerfile.webhook`, `Dockerfile.devserver`); changing them requires deploying to `~/devbox/webhook/webhook.py` / `~/devbox/devserver/devserver-entrypoint.sh` AND rebuilding the image. **Cutover ordering matters when the manager's CLI signature changes** (e.g. per-author ŌåÆ per-branch dropped the `<email>` arg): in the window between deploying the new manager script and rebuilding the webhook image, the still-running webhook calls `upsert <email> <branch>` against a manager that now expects `upsert <branch>` ŌĆö the first positional silently becomes the "branch", spinning up a wrong dev server. Safe sequence: (1) `destroy-all` first (works against the old subcommand), (2) deploy ALL three files (manager + webhook.py + entrypoint), (3) rebuild + recreate the webhook image from a detached sidecar in the same step.
- **One-shot rebuild + recreate of a single compose service from a detached sidecar:** the documented pattern for "recreate cmd-api kills the in-flight request" generalizes to webhook too ŌĆö anytime you need to rebuild + recreate from inside the VM, launch a sibling. The exact recipe (`<service>` = webhook or any other compose service):
  ```
  bash scripts/remote-mac.sh "docker run -d --rm \
    -v /Users:/Users -v /var/run/docker.sock:/var/run/docker.sock \
    -w /Users/sccarey/devbox --name rebuild-sidecar-<n> docker:cli \
    sh -c 'docker compose build <service> && docker compose up -d --force-recreate <service> && echo SIDECAR_OK'" / 60
  bash scripts/remote-mac.sh "until ! docker inspect rebuild-sidecar-<n> >/dev/null 2>&1; do sleep 3; done; echo DONE"
  ```
  The sidecar name must be unique per rebuild attempt (e.g. `webhook-rebuild-sidecar`, `-2`, ...) ŌĆö `docker run --name` rejects duplicates even with `--rm`. Don't skip the `-w /Users/sccarey/devbox` working dir; compose interprets `./` paths relative to the CLI's CWD, and the daemon then needs the path to be Mac-visible via the `/Users` bind mount (per the existing "Bind paths in docker-compose.yml are interpreted by the daemon" pitfall).
- **`sed -E 's/[^a-z0-9-]+/-/g'` does NOT collapse runs of already-allowed `-` characters.** A naive "simplification" of the 3-step slugify (replace non-allowed ŌåÆ collapse hyphen runs ŌåÆ trim) into a single `s/[^a-z0-9-]+/-/g; s/^-+|-+$//g` looks equivalent but isn't: `weird///slash---name` collapses the slashes to one `-` BUT leaves the literal `---` run untouched, producing `weird-slash---name` instead of `weird-slash-name`. The correct one-invocation form is three substitutions on one `sed -E` call: `'s/[^a-z0-9-]+/-/g; s/-+/-/g; s/^-+|-+$//g'`. The second pass is load-bearing because `-` is in the allowed set of the first character class. Same trap applies to any other "allowed-chars-include-the-collapse-target" slugify.

## Tech Stack

| Layer | Technology |
|-------|-----------|
| Framework | Next.js 16.2.0 (App Router, `force-dynamic` routes) |
| UI | React 19.2.4, Tailwind CSS 4, Geist font |
| Language | TypeScript 5 (strict mode, `@/*` path alias) |
| Backend | Python (FastAPI), managed by **uv** |
| Database | PostgreSQL 16 (local, via Docker) |
| Python tooling | **uv** ŌĆö package management, virtual environments, Python version management |
| Unit tests | Vitest 3.2.4, Testing Library, jsdom |
| Python tests | pytest (managed via uv) |
| E2E tests | Playwright 1.55.0 (Chromium, Firefox, WebKit) |
| CI | GitHub Actions (Node 18/20 matrix, lint, coverage) |
| PWA | Service workers, manifest.json, Apple web app support |
| iOS | Capacitor 8 WebView shell (`capacitor.config.ts`), remote-URL loading; built on Mac mini self-hosted runner, distributed via TestFlight |

```
Ōöé   Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ questionCache.ts                # In-memory LRU cache for questions/results/votes/participants
Ōöé   Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ questionId.ts                   # isUuidLike + normalizePath helpers
Ōöé   Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ viewTransitions.ts          # iOS-style slide transitions via View Transitions API
Ōöé   Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ usePageReady.ts             # Hook writing data-page-ready for view transitions
Ōöé   Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ useMeasuredHeight.ts        # Hook measuring an element's offsetHeight via ResizeObserver
Ōöé   Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ useDayTimeWindowsState.ts   # Shared add/remove/edit handlers + removed-day cache for time-question day lists
Ōöé   Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ instant-loading.ts          # Page load optimization
Ōöé   Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ usePageTitle.ts             # Dynamic page title hook
Ōöé   ŌööŌöĆŌöĆ pushoverNotifications.ts    # Push notification integration
Ōöé
Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ database/migrations/            # SQL migration files (001-094, up + down)
Ōöé   Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ 001-015: Core schema (questions, votes, results, ranked choice, RLS)
Ōöé   Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ 016-041: Short IDs, question access, suggestion fields, RLS policies
Ōöé   Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ 042-050: Suggestion question type, vote constraints, editing
Ōöé   Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ 051-063: Participation question machinery (since removed in 094)
Ōöé   Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ 064-093: Cleanup, time question, polls, backfill
Ōöé   ŌööŌöĆŌöĆ 094: Drop participation question type entirely
Ōöé
Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ tests/
Ōöé   Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ __tests__/                  # Vitest unit/integration tests
Ōöé   Ōöé   Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ ranked-choice/          # IRV algorithm tests
Ōöé   Ōöé   Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ ballot-logic/           # Ballot validation tests
Ōöé   Ōöé   Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ voting-algorithms/      # Algorithm correctness tests

Ōöé
Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ social_tests/                   # Social scenario testing framework

Ōöé       Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ test_casual_decisions.py        # Yes/no & suggestion basics; name-required model

Ōöé       Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ test_event_planning.py          # Multi-question polls (atomic batch, partial abstain)
Ōöé       Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ test_time_coordination.py       # Two-phase scheduling, min-availability filter
Ōöé       Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ test_suggestion_collaboration.py # SeedŌåÆcollectŌåÆcutoffŌåÆrank in one poll

    Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ postcss.config.mjs           # Tailwind CSS
    ŌööŌöĆŌöĆ eslint.config.mjs             # ESLint flat config (next/core-web-vitals)
```

## Key Concepts

### Question Types

| Type | Description | Vote Data |
|------|-------------|-----------|
| `yes_no` | Simple binary vote | `{ vote: "yes" \| "no" }` |
| `ranked_choice` | Instant Runoff Voting (IRV) with Borda tiebreak; supports equal/tied rankings; optional suggestion phase | `{ rankings: string[], ranked_choice_tiers?: string[][], suggestions?: string[] }` |
| `time` | Two-phase availability (day/time windows) ŌåÆ preferences (likes/dislikes) | `{ voter_day_time_windows: [...], liked_slots?: string[], disliked_slots?: string[] }` |
| `limited_supply` | First-come, first-served slots: `supply_count` spots, whoever claims first gets them | claim/decline only ŌĆö `is_abstain=false` (claim) or `true` (decline); no choice payload |

### Access Control Model

- **No user accounts** - fully anonymous
- **Browser-based access** via localStorage (`browserQuestionAccess.ts`)
- Question URLs grant access: visiting `/p/[id]` registers access
- Creator authentication via `creator_secret` (stored in localStorage)
- Database-level RLS (Row Level Security) policies on all tables

### Grouped Messaging UI

- **Main page shows groups**, not individual questions. A group is a flat list of polls sharing a `polls.group_id` (Migration 105 retired the `polls.follow_up_to` chain pointer). `lib/groupUtils.ts: buildGroups` groups polls by `group_id` and sorts by `created_at` ŌĆö no chain walking. Sub-questions of one poll are siblings inside the same poll wrapper.
- **Group title** defaults to the deduplicated list of participant names (`creator_name` + `voter_names` from the API). Users can override it via `/g/<id>/edit-title` ŌåÆ `POST /api/groups/<route_id>/title`. The override is stored in `groups.title` (one row per group, single source of truth ŌĆö Migration 105 moved it off `polls.group_title`). `Group.title` reads `latestPoll.group_title` (server surfaces `groups.title` on every poll in the group via JOIN) and falls back to `Group.defaultTitle` (the names string) when NULL. `apiUpdateGroupTitle(routeId, title)` invalidates every poll in the group automatically ŌĆö callers don't have to re-implement the cache cleanup ritual.
- **Group sorting**: groups with unvoted open questions first (by soonest deadline), then groups with no unvoted questions (by most recent activity).
- **Group URLs split path + query.** (Historical: the canonical poll URL is now the PATH form `/g/<groupShortId>/p/<pollShortId>` ŌĆö see the "Poll Cards + Detail Page" section. `?p=<pollShortId>` is legacy-redirect-only; share links, in-app nav, AND notification payloads all emit the path form.) The legacy bullet, for reference: path is the group root's short_id (or root question id when no short_id), query named the poll to auto-expand and scroll to. Empty placeholder is bare `/g/`. Sub-routes `/g/<groupShortId>/info` and `/g/<groupShortId>/edit-title`. Legacy `/p/<id>` URLs (and `/p/<id>/info`, `/p/<id>/edit-title`) live as redirect stubs that resolve the ambiguous id (poll short_id / poll uuid / question uuid) once and `router.replace` into the canonical `/g/...` form ŌĆö see `app/p/[shortId]/_legacyRedirect.tsx`. Three URL-builder helpers in `lib/groupUtils.ts`: `getGroupHref(group)` for the home list (bare `/g/<root>` ŌĆö no auto-expand), `getGroupHrefForPoll(poll)` for "navigate to this poll's group with this poll expanded" (used by FollowUpHeader, GroupCardItem copy-link, /g/ ?id= handler, and the legacy /p/ redirects), and `resolveGroupRootRouteId(poll)` for just the group-root part. The `POLL_QUERY_PARAM` constant in `lib/groupUtils.ts` names the `?p` key.
- **Auto-expand is encoded by the URL itself, not heuristics.** `?p=<id>` present ŌåÆ expand that poll; absent ŌåÆ no expand, page scrolls to bottom (the draft-form area). The old `?group=1` flag and the `suppressExpand` "user has responded to every question" heuristic are gone ŌĆö the URL is the source of truth. URL sync on expand swaps `?p=` via shallow `history.replaceState`, never touching the path; sharing the URL reopens the same expanded card.
- **Home ŌåÆ group lands on the awaiting card (or bottom if all done).** `getGroupHref(group)` returns bare `/g/<root>` and `GroupList`'s tap handler calls `slideToGroup({ href, groupId })`. The group page's initial-scroll layout effect picks the anchor (oldest awaiting question, or bottom for groups with no awaiting work). Tapping a CARD slides to its detail page at `/g/<root>/p/<pollShort>` via `slideToPollDetail` ŌĆö cards no longer expand in place. `isPollOpen(poll, now?)` (not closed AND deadline-not-passed) remains the canonical helper for that rule ŌĆö don't re-inline the `is_closed`/`response_deadline` math.
- **Floating bubble bar auto-follows-up** when on a group page via `document.body.getAttribute('data-group-latest-question-id')` ŌĆö the group page sets this attribute on mount. The home page does NOT render the bubble bar; it has the single new group button instead, which navigates to `/g/` (the empty placeholder). `/g/` shows the bubble bar (since `isGroupRootView` matches it); the user picks a category from there. If the user dismisses the modal without submitting, the empty placeholder remains visible with the bubble bar; tapping back returns to home. On submit from the empty placeholder, the new question has no `follow_up_to` so it becomes its own group root.
- **Shared utilities**: `lib/questionListUtils.ts` (relativeTime, getCategoryIcon, badges), `lib/votedQuestionsStorage.ts` (loadVotedQuestions), `lib/timeUtils.ts:formatCreationTimestamp` (absolute "@ h:mm AM M/D/YY" timestamp used in the tooltip + the expanded card). QuestionList keeps its own full-featured `getResultBadge` with user-specific participation messages.
- **Group list row layout** (`components/GroupListItem.tsx`): NO hairline dividers between rows; the visual structure is avatar-driven, not chrome-driven. Each row is a flex with `[selection checkbox?] [avatar] [text block (flex-1)] [right rail]` (drafts and empty groups pass `hideRespondents={true}`, skipping both the avatar and the right rail). The right rail is a `flex flex-col items-end justify-start self-stretch -ml-[4.224px] gap-0.5` containing two stacked elements that are ALWAYS in fixed positions: the age stamp at top, the countdown / dot indicator below. Either element can be absent independently ŌĆö `createdAt` null hides the age, `unvotedDeadlineKind` undefined hides the indicator ŌĆö but their slot positions are stable so adjacent rows align vertically.
