- Pushes to ANY branch that touch `capacitor.config.ts`, `ios/**`, `package.json`, `package-lock.json`, the workflow file, or `scripts/ios/**`. `main` builds the prod bundle (`com.whoeverwants.app`); every other branch builds the shared `latest` bundle (`com.whoeverwants.app.latest`). Concurrency is keyed on `github.ref` with `cancel-in-progress: true`, so rapid pushes to the same branch only run the latest commit.
- **GitHub Release published** (non-draft, non-prerelease) ŌåÆ builds the prod bundle pinned to the release's tag. Keeps the iOS prod IPA in lockstep with the Vercel + droplet auto-deploys that already fire on the same event. Prereleases are filtered out by an `if:` guard on the job (the `published` action fires for prereleases too).
- Manual via `workflow_dispatch` ŌĆö inputs: `cap_env` (`latest|prod`), `cap_server_url` (explicit URL override), `skip_upload` (bool).

### Universal Links

Tapping a `https://whoeverwants.com/...` URL from iMessage / Mail / Notes opens the installed Capacitor app instead of Safari. Three coupled pieces:

- **AASA file at `/.well-known/apple-app-site-association`** is served by a Next.js route handler (`app/.well-known/apple-app-site-association/route.ts`) returning `{ applinks: { details: [{ appIDs: [...], components: [{ "/": "/*" }] }] }, webcredentials: { apps: [...] } }` with `Content-Type: application/json`. The path has NO `.json` extension; iOS will not follow redirects and will not accept any other content type. `skipTrailingSlashRedirect: true` in `next.config.ts` (already set for API routes) doubles as protection here ŌĆö without it, iOS hitting the bare path would 308-redirect to `/path/` and abort. The `Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store` header on non-`/api`/`_next/static` paths applies and is fine (iOS does its own aggressive caching). Verify both URL forms return 200 directly: `curl -sI https://whoeverwants.com/.well-known/apple-app-site-association` and `.../apple-app-site-association/`. The `appIDs` and `webcredentials.apps` arrays share one `APP_IDS` const (`["479DZ4AZT5.com.whoeverwants.app", "479DZ4AZT5.com.whoeverwants.app.latest"]`) ŌĆö `applinks` powers universal links, `webcredentials` powers passkeys-in-WKWebView (see the Passkeys bullet below).
- **Entitlement** `com.apple.developer.associated-domains` in `ios/App/App/App.entitlements` lists all four (`applinks:` + `webcredentials:` for both hosts) as the committed local-build superset ŌĆö but the SHIPPED artifact is scoped to one host per tier by `ios-build.yml` (see the "AASA at both hosts" bullet above). Both `aps-environment` (push) and `associated-domains` share the same plist now; future capabilities go here too.
- **`webcredentials` is what makes PASSKEYS (WebAuthn) work inside the Capacitor WKWebView.** When JS calls `navigator.credentials.get()/.create()` in a web view, WebKit routes the ceremony through the system AuthenticationServices, which refuses unless the host app is associated with the relying-party domain via the `webcredentials` service ŌĆö the entitlement AND the AASA `webcredentials.apps` array must BOTH list the app. Without it the ceremony fails immediately with `NotAllowedError`, and `lib/passkeys.ts: isCancellation` (correctly, per spec) can't tell that apart from a user dismiss, so `SignInOptions`/`handlePasskeySignIn` clears the loading state silently ŌĆö surfacing as "tap Sign in with a passkey, it briefly attempts, then reverts as if nothing happened." Browser + PWA passkeys do NOT need this association (Safari verifies the RP id against the page origin directly); only the WKWebView path does. The RP id is the host the WebView loads (`latest.whoeverwants.com` for the Latest app, `whoeverwants.com` for prod ŌĆö see `_resolve_rp_id` in `server/routers/auth.py`), so each host needs its own `webcredentials:<host>` entry. Fixed in `claude/ios-passkey-signin-bug-t9FIS`.
- **`appUrlOpen` listener** in `components/UniversalLinksHandler.tsx` (mounted from `app/layout.tsx`, NOT `template.tsx` for the same persist-across-routes reason as `PersistentCreatePollHost`). Delegates to `lib/universalLinks.ts: installUniversalLinksHandler(navigate)` which: (a) short-circuits synchronously via `Capacitor.isNativePlatform()` so browsers/PWA pay zero cost beyond a single boolean check, (b) sets a module-level `installed = true` flag BEFORE the `await import("@capacitor/app")` to defeat the StrictMode-double-mount race, (c) registers `App.addListener("appUrlOpen", ...)`, and (d) calls `pathFromUniversalLinkUrl(event.url)` which re-validates against the known-hosts allowlist before `router.push`-ing. The re-validation is belt-and-braces ŌĆö iOS only hands us URLs matching the entitlement, but cross-origin navigation from this channel would be a high-blast-radius vuln if entitlements ever widen.

**Tier mapping:**
- `whoeverwants.com/...` ŌåÆ prod bundle `com.whoeverwants.app` (loads `whoeverwants.com` in the WebView).
- `latest.whoeverwants.com/...` ŌåÆ latest bundle `com.whoeverwants.app.latest` (loads `latest.whoeverwants.com`). The latest iOS build (`scripts/ios/build.sh --env latest` or any push to a non-main branch) sets `CAP_SERVER_URL=https://latest.whoeverwants.com`.
- Both AASA endpoints (prod + latest) serve the same JSON listing both bundles, but each shipped app's `applinks:` entitlement is scoped to ONLY its own host (by `ios-build.yml`). Net result: a `whoeverwants.com` link opens the prod app, a `latest.whoeverwants.com` link opens the latest app ŌĆö unambiguously, even with BOTH apps installed. A cross-tier link with only the "wrong" app installed opens in Safari. (Before scoping, both bundles claimed both hosts and iOS picked non-deterministically when both were installed ŌĆö the recovery-link-opened-prod-app bug.)

Manual prereqs (must do once per bundle ID, outside this code):
1. **Apple Developer portal ŌåÆ Identifiers ŌåÆ `<bundle>` ŌåÆ check "Associated Domains" ŌåÆ save.** Same UI as Push Notifications; no certificate generation. Without this, the entitlement compiles but iOS silently ignores it. Repeat for every bundle in the AASA `appIDs` list ŌĆö prod (`com.whoeverwants.app`) AND latest (`com.whoeverwants.app.latest`). The SAME "Associated Domains" capability covers both `applinks:` and `webcredentials:` ŌĆö no separate toggle for passkeys, so adding `webcredentials` to an already-applinks-enabled bundle needs no portal change.
2. **iOS aggressively caches AASA.** After deploying an AASA change, existing installs may not pick it up ŌĆö delete + reinstall the app to force a refetch. TestFlight's "Update" button is NOT sufficient on its own. This applies to the `webcredentials` addition too: a passkey fix isn't live on a device until (a) the host the app loads serves the new AASA ŌĆö `latest.whoeverwants.com` only updates on push to main, `whoeverwants.com` only on release ŌĆö (b) a fresh iOS build ships the new entitlement, and (c) the app is deleted + reinstalled.

Pitfalls:
- **Don't put AASA under `public/.well-known/`.** Next.js silently refuses to serve hidden directories from `public/`. Use the `app/` route handler.
- **Static-import `@capacitor/core`, not dynamic.** The chunk is already in every page bundle (via `app/template.tsx` + `lib/pushNotifications.ts`), so `await import("@capacitor/core")` just adds an async hop before the `isNativePlatform()` short-circuit. Same applies to any future Capacitor-conditional code.
- **The validation IS belt-and-braces, not optional.** iOS won't deliver a non-matching URL through `appUrlOpen` today, but a future entitlement widening (e.g. `applinks:*.whoeverwants.com` to cover dev) would expand the surface ŌĆö and the FE has to assume the channel can carry hostile-but-valid-shape payloads (e.g. `https://whoeverwants.com.evil.com/g/foo`, blocked by the `KNOWN_HOSTS` Set check on `.hostname`).
- **WebView already on whoeverwants.com handles deeplinks natively.** If the app is foregrounded and the user taps a same-domain link, iOS lets WKWebView navigate without firing `appUrlOpen`. The listener is primarily a cold-launch / background-resume path. Both flows end up on the same Next.js route ŌĆö don't try to detect "did the listener fire" to gate behavior.

### Helper scripts

- `scripts/ios/build.sh [--env latest|prod] [--skip-upload] [--ref <branch>]` ŌĆö dispatches a workflow run and questions until completion. Requires a `GITHUB_API_TOKEN` with `actions:write`. On failure, calls `logs.sh --failed-only` automatically.
- `scripts/ios/logs.sh [<run_id>] [--failed-only]` ŌĆö fetches and prints CI logs. `--failed-only` hits the per-job logs endpoint (much smaller than the full-run zip).
- `scripts/ios/mac-bootstrap.sh <runner_token>` ŌĆö one-time Mac mini setup (Homebrew, Node, Xcode CLI tools, `xcodebuild -downloadPlatform iOS`, GitHub Actions runner as LaunchAgent).

### Feedback-loop cheat sheet

| Change | Delay | Mechanism |
|---|---|---|
| Web code | ~30 s | Vercel (prod) or dev server (dev); pull-to-refresh on device |
| Native plugin / config | 8ŌĆō20 min | Runner ŌåÆ TestFlight ŌåÆ tap "Update" in TestFlight app |

### Required GitHub repo secrets

- `APP_STORE_CONNECT_API_KEY_ID` ŌĆö Key ID from App Store Connect
- `APP_STORE_CONNECT_API_KEY_ISSUER_ID` ŌĆö Issuer UUID
- `APP_STORE_CONNECT_API_KEY_P8` ŌĆö base64 of the `.p8` file (single-line paste is less brittle via mobile browser than multi-line PEM)
- `APPLE_TEAM_ID` ŌĆö 10-char team ID
- `CI_KEYCHAIN_PASSWORD` ŌĆö password for the dedicated `ci.keychain-db` on the Mac mini

See `docs/ios-setup.md` for the full one-time setup walkthrough.

### Pitfalls learned the hard way

- **API key needs cert-management scope.** The "App Manager" role alone triggers `Cloud signing permission error` + `No signing certificate "iOS Distribution" found` during export. Regenerate the key with **Admin** role (or explicitly enable "Access to Certificates, Identifiers and Profiles"). Apple added this as a separate permission in 2024.
- **Automatic signing ignores command-line `PRODUCT_BUNDLE_IDENTIFIER` overrides.** xcodebuild honors the override for the archive's Info.plist, but the signing phase looks up the profile using the bundle ID baked into `project.pbxproj`. Result: a dev-URL build uploaded under the prod bundle ID. Fix: `sed`-patch `project.pbxproj` before archive and verify the expected number of replacements occurred.
- **Capacitor 8 uses Swift Package Manager, not CocoaPods.** No `Podfile` or `.xcworkspace` ŌĆö there's only `App.xcodeproj`. Don't run `pod install`. Use `-project` (not `-workspace`) with xcodebuild.
- **`xcodebuild` needs a shared scheme.** Capacitor's scaffold doesn't create one; Xcode would on first GUI open, but CI never opens Xcode. Commit `ios/App/App.xcodeproj/xcshareddata/xcschemes/App.xcscheme` to the repo so headless builds find the scheme.
- **Xcode 15+ ships with no platform SDKs.** Run `xcodebuild -downloadPlatform iOS` once on the Mac mini (the bootstrap script does this). Otherwise archives fail with `iOS N.N is not installed`.
- **Self-hosted runner starts from a LaunchAgent.** LaunchAgents don't source `~/.zprofile`, so Homebrew's PATH must be injected explicitly (`echo /opt/homebrew/bin >> "$GITHUB_PATH"` as the first workflow step). Same applies to any brew-installed CLI.
- **LaunchAgent can't access the login keychain reliably over SSH.** Create a dedicated `ci.keychain-db` with a known password (stored as `CI_KEYCHAIN_PASSWORD` secret). The workflow unlocks it at the start of each run. `security set-keychain-settings` fails with "User interaction is not allowed" from SSH sessions ŌĆö run it in the workflow instead (or tolerate the failure; 5-min default timeout is enough for a single build).
- **Mobile Safari corrupts multi-line PEM pastes into GitHub Secrets.** The line wrapping mangles the base64 body, which xcodebuild then rejects with `CryptoKit.CryptoKitASN1Error.invalidPEMDocument`. Paste a single-line base64 string instead (the workflow decodes either form).
- **`altool` exits 0 even when it rejects the upload ŌĆö so the SUCCESS MARKER is the authoritative signal, NOT the presence of an `ERROR:` line.** The "Upload to TestFlight" step passes iff the log contains a success marker (`No errors uploading|UPLOAD SUCCEEDED|successful upload`) and fails on its ABSENCE. Don't trust altool's exit code alone, and don't soften the success-marker check to a warning. **Do NOT re-add a `grep "ERROR:" ŌåÆ fail` pre-check** (the original form did `grep -E "UPLOAD FAILED|^.*ERROR:" ŌåÆ exit 1` BEFORE the success check): altool retries transient Apple-side failures (observed: a mid-upload `RETRIEVE UPLOAD OPERATIONS ... received status code 500; internal server error`) and STILL prints `UPLOAD SUCCEEDED with no errors` afterward, so an `ERROR:` line legitimately co-exists with a completed upload ŌĆö the `ERROR:` pre-check turned that into a red run even though the IPA shipped (cost a confusing "build failed but the app is in TestFlight" cycle on `claude/ios-recovery-email-error-IRD63`). The success-marker-absence rule still catches both genuine failure shapes: the explicit `UPLOAD FAILED` banner, and the silent `ERROR: ... Cannot determine the Apple ID from Bundle ID ... (12)` (bundle not registered in App Store Connect) ŌĆö neither prints a success banner. If you add an extra altool invocation elsewhere, mirror the success-marker-required pattern.
- **`altool --upload-app` MUST pass `--apple-id <numeric ASC app id>` ŌĆö its bundle-id auto-detection PREFIX-matches and mis-routes when bundle ids are nested.** This was the root cause of a multi-hour prod-iOS-upload failure. Without `--apple-id`, altool resolves the target App Store Connect app from the IPA's CFBundleIdentifier via a PREFIX match, not exact. `com.whoeverwants.app` ambiguously matches three sibling apps (`.app`, `.app.latest`, `.app.dev.samcarey`) and altool picks the wrong one ŌĆö prod `.app` IPAs were routed to the `.latest` app record. Symptom is a pair of misleading 409s carrying the WRONG (sibling) app's state: `Validation failed (409) ... The bundle identifier cannot be changed from the current value, 'com.whoeverwants.app.latest'` and `bundle version must be higher than the previously uploaded version: '<canary build #>'` ŌĆö the bundle id + build number in those errors belong to `.latest`, not the `.app` app you're uploading. Canary (`.latest`) uploads worked by luck (no app extends its prefix). Fix: the "Compute bundle identity" step emits a per-tier `apple_id` (`6762459339` = WhoeverWants/`.app`, `6769589158` = WhoeverWants Latest/`.latest`) and the upload step passes `--apple-id "${{ steps.bundle.outputs.apple_id }}"`. The IPA itself (Info.plist, embedded Distribution profile, entitlements, binary `__info_plist`) was provably 100% correct for `.app` the whole time ŌĆö the bug was entirely altool's app resolution. **Decisive diagnostic**: run `xcrun altool --upload-app ... --apple-id <prod numeric id>` manually against the failing IPA on the Mac; it succeeds instantly, proving the IPA is fine and routing is the issue. New tier ŌåÆ get its Apple ID from `GET /v1/apps` on the ASC API or the app's ASC URL (`appstoreconnect.apple.com/apps/<APPLE_ID>/...`) and add a branch to the bundle-identity step.
- **`CFBundleVersion` uses `date +%s` (Unix epoch), NOT `git rev-list --count HEAD`.** Monotonic + unique per build + forward-proof. (Note: the "bundle version must be higher than '861'" error that originally motivated this change was actually a symptom of the altool prefix-mis-routing bug above ŌĆö the `.app` upload was hitting `.latest`'s build history. The epoch scheme is still the right call regardless: `git rev-list --count HEAD` diverges between the canary branch and main, so prod and canary build numbers could legitimately collide or regress; epoch can't.) Apple accepts up to 18 chars for CFBundleVersion; the 10-digit epoch fits. `fetch-depth: 0` is retained for `git log` accuracy in other workflow steps, not for the version counter.
- **`ITSAppUsesNonExemptEncryption=false`** in `Info.plist` skips the TestFlight export-compliance prompt. WhoeverWants only uses standard HTTPS (exempt category).
- **App icon must be 1024├Ś1024 opaque PNG** in `ios/App/App/Assets.xcassets/AppIcon.appiconset/AppIcon-512@2x.png`. Alpha channels cause `Missing required icon file` rejection. `.gitignore` excludes `*.png` except under `public/` and the AppIcon asset catalog ŌĆö preserve both overrides.
- **`CFBundleVersion` monotonicity**: the workflow uses `git rev-list --count HEAD`. Never rewrite history in a way that lowers this count, or TestFlight will reject future uploads.
- **First build auto-scaffolds + commits `ios/`.** Subsequent pulls should include `ios/`. Don't manually `rm -rf ios/` without also rerunning the scaffold flow.
- **`server.url` + App Store review**: App Store review sometimes objects to pure remote-URL apps. Phase 2 switches to bundled assets (requires static export ŌĆö non-trivial with Next.js 16 App Router + `force-dynamic` + `next.config.ts` rewrites). Fine for TestFlight / sideload.
- **`contentInset: 'always'` produces visible black bars at the top and bottom on iPhone X-class devices.** The setting pads the WebView's scroll view away from the safe areas, exposing the configured `backgroundColor` underneath as a solid bar. The web app already handles safe areas itself (`viewport-fit=cover` + `env(safe-area-inset-*)` padding throughout), so the WebView should go edge-to-edge ŌĆö use `contentInset: 'never'` in `capacitor.config.ts`. Pair with `backgroundColor: '#ffffff'` so any brief flash during load matches the page bg in light mode (Capacitor doesn't support theme-aware config values).
- **UIWindow's default `backgroundColor` is black, which leaks as a bottom-of-screen bar if the WebView's frame doesn't fully cover the window.** `CAPBridgeViewController.loadView()` is `final` and assigns `view = webView` ŌĆö you can't restructure the view hierarchy. Defenses: (a) `AppDelegate.didFinishLaunchingWithOptions` sets `window?.backgroundColor = .systemBackground` (window is non-nil here for non-UIScene apps with `UIMainStoryboardFile` in Info.plist), (b) a `MainViewController: CAPBridgeViewController` subclass overrides `viewDidLoad` to set `view.backgroundColor = .systemBackground`. Use `.systemBackground` (not `.white`) so dark-mode users don't see white safe-area zones against a near-black page. Capacitor already writes `webView.backgroundColor` + `scrollView.backgroundColor` from `capacitor.config.ts` (CAPBridgeViewController.swift L308-310) ŌĆö don't redo those in the subclass.
- **Adding a new `.swift` file requires hand-patching `project.pbxproj`.** `npx cap sync ios` doesn't pick up new native files ŌĆö it only syncs web assets and plugins. Xcode's GUI handles file-add via PBXBuildFile + PBXFileReference + group children entries, but the headless CI build has no GUI. For small additions (1ŌĆō2 short classes), colocate inside `ios/App/App/AppDelegate.swift` which is already in the build phase. Reserve new files for non-trivial code where colocation hurts readability.
- **Storyboard `customClass` references use the Xcode target name as `customModule`.** `<viewController customClass="MainViewController" customModule="App" customModuleProvider="target"/>` resolves to the `MainViewController` Swift class in the `App` target. Verify with `grep "name = " ios/App/App.xcodeproj/project.pbxproj` ŌĆö the target name is the source of truth. Capacitor's default scaffold uses `customModule="Capacitor"` because the bridge VC ships from the Capacitor SPM package; subclasses defined in the app target need `customModule="App"` and the `customModuleProvider="target"` attribute.
- **Per-author dev URLs are dead ŌĆö the non-prod iOS tier targets `latest.whoeverwants.com`.** An earlier version of `ios-build.yml` derived `CAP_SERVER_URL` from `head_commit.author.email` (`<slug>.dev.whoeverwants.com`). That worked under per-author dev servers but broke silently when dev servers became per-branch (the `<email-slug>` URL still resolves DNS-wise via the wildcard Caddy frontend, but returns HTTP 503 `upstream connect error` because no upstream container is registered for that slug). The WebView loads the 503, renders nothing visible, and the user sees a white screen (light mode) or black screen (dark mode ŌĆö the `view.backgroundColor = .systemBackground` showing through). Fix in this repo's history: workflow now hardcodes `https://latest.whoeverwants.com` for CAP_ENV=`latest`. If a new tier appears that requires per-bundle URLs again, key on `github.ref` (branch name) NOT email ŌĆö and add a third bundle id rather than reviving the per-actor scheme.
- **TestFlight blank-screen diagnostic workflow.** Symptom: app launches, shows a solid white or black screen (color = light/dark mode default from `view.backgroundColor = .systemBackground`), no content. Before reaching for Safari Web Inspector, run this triage:
  1. Curl the URL the iOS build points at (`https://whoeverwants.com` for prod TestFlight, `https://latest.whoeverwants.com` for the `WhoeverWants Latest` TestFlight). Verify it returns 200 with a valid `<title>` and `<meta name="build-id">`. A 503 / 5xx here is the bug (see the per-author-URL pitfall above for the historical case).
  2. Open the same URL in iPhone Safari on the same device. If Safari renders fine but the WebView is blank, the bug is WebView-specific (CSS / JS / Capacitor bridge) ŌĆö proceed to step 3. If Safari ALSO blanks, the bug is in the web bundle currently served by that tier.
  3. Compare deployed `build-id` between tiers ŌĆö `curl -s https://whoeverwants.com | grep -oE 'build-id" content="[^"]+"'` vs the same against `latest.whoeverwants.com`. If they diverge AND the prod tier is older AND prod TestFlight is the one failing, the most likely fix is "cut a release" to promote the newer (fixed) bundle to prod ŌĆö no new iOS build needed since the WebView reloads its URL on each app open. (Pattern we hit: prod blank screen was an overlay-slide regression in commit `8a60ff0` already fixed in subsequent main commits but never released to prod because the two-tier deploy was set up after the regression and no release had been cut.)
  4. Check client logs on the matching tier (`/api/client-logs?level=error&limit=50`) ŌĆö the forwarder captures unhandled errors and prod-host `warn/error` console output. See the "Client Log Forwarding" section.
- **Cached provisioning profiles persist across workflow runs and bind the wrong bundle to the IPA.** Profiles live OUTSIDE DerivedData (`~/Library/Developer/Xcode/UserData/Provisioning Profiles/` and `~/Library/MobileDevice/Provisioning Profiles/`), so `xcodebuild clean` doesn't touch them. With automatic signing + `-allowProvisioningUpdates`, Xcode SHOULD fetch a fresh profile when the target bundle id changes ŌĆö but in practice it often reuses a cached SIBLING profile (e.g. `com.whoeverwants.app.latest` left over from a canary build, used for a `com.whoeverwants.app` prod build). The resulting IPA has its `Info.plist` CFBundleIdentifier set to the right bundle id but its embedded `.mobileprovision` set to the sibling, and ASC rejects with `Validation failed (409) ... bundle identifier cannot be changed from the current value, '<sibling-bundle>'`. Fix: a workflow step before `Archive` that `rm -rf`'s both profile cache directories, forcing `-allowProvisioningUpdates` to re-fetch from ASC. Costs a few seconds per build for the round-trip. If the new fetch ALSO fails (capabilities mismatch in Apple Developer portal between `.app` and `.latest`, missing entitlements on `.app`, etc.), the failure will be a clearer error from xcodebuild instead of a confusing ASC 409 at upload time.
- **`xcodebuild archive` without `clean` reuses stale embedded CFBundleIdentifier from the App binary.** The Mac self-hosted runner's DerivedData persists across runs. After a canary build (`com.whoeverwants.app.latest`) runs, the next prod build (`com.whoeverwants.app`) re-uses the previously-compiled App.app ŌĆö the outer `App.app/Info.plist` regenerates correctly from the freshly-patched `pbxproj`, but the App binary's Mach-O `__info_plist` segment still carries the previous bundle id baked in at link time. ASC's altool validator reads CFBundleIdentifier from BOTH locations and rejects the upload with `Validation failed (409) This bundle is invalid. The bundle identifier cannot be changed from the current value, 'com.whoeverwants.app.latest'.` Symptom: prod release builds fail at the "Upload to TestFlight" step right after a canary build of the same project succeeded. Fix: pass `clean archive` (both actions) instead of just `archive` to xcodebuild ŌĆö forces full re-link so the binary's embedded plist regenerates from the patched pbxproj. Trade-off: ~30s ŌåÆ ~2min archive time per run; acceptable because the workflow's path filter only triggers iOS builds on native-relevant changes / release publishes / push-to-main. The `clean` action targets the specific scheme/config so SPM caches stay warm. Note that codesign + provisioning profile lookups also benefit from the clean ŌĆö Xcode's per-project profile selection cache lives in DerivedData too. Don't try to fix this with `rm -rf ~/Library/Developer/Xcode/DerivedData/App-*` instead; that nukes SPM caches and triples archive time.
- **The iOS keyboard "input accessory bar" (prev/next chevrons + Done Ō£ō row above the keyboard) is a native WKWebView affordance with NO web removal hook ŌĆö and NO HTML spec controls it.** Reported on the create-poll search box. No input `type`, `inputmode` (other than `none`, which kills the keyboard entirely), `enterkeyhint`, `autocomplete`, taking the input out of a `<form>`, single-field-only, or `contenteditable` removes it ŌĆö it's the WebKit *form assistant*, not part of any web standard (`navigator.virtualKeyboard` is Chromium-only and wouldn't control it anyway). The prev/next chevrons are merely greyed when there's a single focusable field; the Done button always shows. **Removed app-wide (Capacitor only) in `MainViewController` (`ios/App/App/AppDelegate.swift`)**: the accessory view is owned by WebKit's private content view (`scrollView.subviews` whose class name starts with `"WKContent"`), NOT by `WKWebView` ŌĆö so `WKWebView.removeInputAccessoryBar()` dynamically allocates a one-off subclass of that content view whose `inputAccessoryView` getter returns nil (via the colocated `_NoInputAccessoryView` helper) and `object_setClass`es the live instance to it (idempotent; the canonical Cordova/SO swizzle). Applied in `viewDidAppear` (before any tap, so the first focus already has nil) + re-applied via a `keyboardWillShowNotification` observer registered once in `viewDidLoad`. This is the SAME mechanism `@capacitor/keyboard` swizzles internally ŌĆö done by hand to avoid adding a plugin (which would also change keyboard *resize* behavior and disturb the create-poll `visualViewport`/`searchVv` layout). **Critical caveat: this changes ONLY the installed app; plain mobile Safari / PWA has no way (web or native) to remove the bar, a years-old WebKit limitation ŌĆö so a dev-server link in mobile Safari still shows it.** Native-only ŌåÆ not demoable on dev servers; needs a fresh iOS build + reinstall to verify on a real device (Simulator can't validate accessory-bar behavior). Imports added to AppDelegate.swift: `WebKit`, `ObjectiveC`.
- **`plutil -insert KEY -xml "<value>"` corrupts Info.plist on macOS ŌĆö use `/usr/libexec/PlistBuddy` for nested-structure inserts.** When wiring native Google Sign In, an early version of `ios-build.yml`'s "Stamp Info.plist with Google iOS URL scheme" step did `plutil -insert CFBundleURLTypes -xml "<array><dict><key>CFBundleURLSchemes</key>..." Info.plist`. The step exited 0, the next `plutil -extract` was silent (didn't fail), but downstream `xcodebuild archive` failed at `builtin-infoPlistUtility` with `error: contents of file is not a dictionary` ŌĆö the entire root element had been replaced with the inserted `<array>`, blowing away CFBundleDisplayName, the existing plist boilerplate, everything. plutil's `-xml VALUE` typing isn't strict enough to refuse a value that, when applied at the root, would un-dict-ify the file. Switch to `/usr/libexec/PlistBuddy -c "Add :CFBundleURLTypes array" + "Add :CFBundleURLTypes:0 dict" + "Add :CFBundleURLTypes:0:CFBundleURLSchemes array" + "Add :CFBundleURLTypes:0:CFBundleURLSchemes:0 string $REVERSED"` ŌĆö slower, more verbose, but it can't blow up the root because each `Add` is keypath-scoped. Belt-and-braces: end the step with `/usr/libexec/PlistBuddy -c "Print :CFBundleURLTypes"` + `plutil -lint` so any future corruption fails the step at the source instead of two minutes later in xcodebuild.

### Clipboard Link Prompt

On Capacitor iOS app activation (cold launch + every foreground-from-background), `lib/clipboardLinkPrompt.ts` peeks at the system clipboard for a copied web URL; if it holds an `https://whoeverwants.com/...` or `https://latest.whoeverwants.com/...` URL the user isn't already on, `components/ClipboardLinkPrompt.tsx` surfaces a `ConfirmationModal` that `router.push`es into the app. Inert on web/PWA via the `Capacitor.isNativePlatform()` short-circuit.

- **Silent detection via a custom native plugin, NOT `@capacitor/clipboard`.** `Clipboard.read()` (= `UIPasteboard.general.string`) forces iOS's "Pasted from <app>" banner on EVERY call, before JS can inspect the content ŌĆö so the old design prompted on every launch even when the clipboard held a non-app URL or plain text. The fix: `ClipboardUrlPlugin` (colocated in `ios/App/App/AppDelegate.swift`, registered JS-side via `registerPlugin("ClipboardUrl")`) calls `UIPasteboard.general.detectValues(for: [.probableWebURL])` (iOS 16+), which is privacy-preserving and returns the matched URL with NO banner. JS then runs the URL through `pathFromUniversalLinkUrl`'s host allowlist and only surfaces our own modal for actual whoeverwants links. On iOS < 16 `detectValues` is unavailable, so the plugin returns `{supported: false}` and JS skips the auto-check entirely (no banner-triggering fallback ŌĆö iOS 15 just loses the copied-link convenience). **On-device verification of the no-banner behavior is mandatory** ŌĆö headless WebKit / the iOS Simulator can't confirm pasteboard banner behavior; only a real device can. The detection API only inspects the FIRST pasteboard item.
- **`ClipboardUrlPlugin` is a `CAPPlugin, CAPBridgedPlugin` colocated in AppDelegate.swift** (same rationale as `MainViewController`: a new `.swift` file means hand-patching `project.pbxproj` in headless CI). **App-target plugins are NOT auto-discovered ŌĆö they MUST be registered by hand in `MainViewController.capacitorDidLoad()` via `bridge?.registerPluginInstance(...)`.** (Capacitor's runtime auto-discovery only covers plugins shipped in CocoaPods/SPM packages; a `CAPBridgedPlugin` class compiled into the app binary is invisible to it. CLAUDE.md + the Swift comments previously claimed auto-discovery "at runtime, no further change beyond compiling the class" ŌĆö that was WRONG and silently broke all three colocated plugins (`ClipboardUrl`/`AppBadge`/`NativeIdentity`): every JS call rejected with `"<name>" plugin is not implemented on ios`, swallowed by best-effort `catch {}`s, so none was ever device-confirmed and the Phase-3 App Group write never landed. See `MainViewController.capacitorDidLoad()` + the Siri Phase 3 note.) `@capacitor/clipboard` is now unused (still in `package.json`; left installed to avoid churning the SwiftPM graph ŌĆö see the apple-sign-in version-conflict pitfall for why plugin removal is risky). Any change to this plugin needs a fresh iOS build to take effect. **When adding a new colocated `CAPBridgedPlugin`, add a matching `registerPluginInstance(...)` line in `capacitorDidLoad()` ŌĆö compiling the class is not enough.**
- **Cold launch needs an explicit one-shot check** ŌĆö `App.addListener("appStateChange")` doesn't fire on the initial active state. Same shape as `lib/universalLinks.ts`'s "claim `installed` BEFORE await" guard against StrictMode double-mount.
- **Coalesce overlapping detection** via an `if (checking) return; checking = true; try {...} finally { checking = false }` guard so rapid foreground/background cycles don't fire two modals for the same activation.
- **Mark the URL responded BEFORE invoking `onLinkFound`**, not after the user confirms/cancels. Without the early mark, a second `checkClipboard` racing the modal mount can pass the `respondedUrls.has(raw)` check and fire a duplicate `onLinkFound`. The component's confirm/cancel handlers still call `markClipboardUrlResponded` ŌĆö that's idempotent (Set-add).
- **`respondedUrls` is LRU-bounded at 50 entries** ŌĆö a long-running PWA session could otherwise accumulate forever. `Set` preserves insertion order, so the oldest entry is `respondedUrls.values().next().value`. Pattern matches `lib/questionCache.ts: setLru`.
- **Skip-if-already-on-that-path uses `normalizePath` from `lib/questionId.ts`**, not a local helper ŌĆö same single-trailing-slash strip both files need. Don't reintroduce a local `normalisePath` (or any other spelling variant) for path comparison.
- **The component's useEffect mirrors `UniversalLinksHandler.tsx`'s cancellation-race pattern** (`let cleanup; let cancelled; install().then(c => cancelled ? c?.() : cleanup = c); return () => { cancelled = true; cleanup?.(); }`). Two callers is the abstraction threshold ŌĆö keep duplicated for now; if a 3rd "install-once Capacitor listener" component lands, extract a shared `useCapacitorInstaller(install)` hook to eliminate the foot-gun.

### Siri / App Intents (deep-link create-poll ŌĆö Phase 1)

Full phased plan: `docs/siri-integration-plan.md` (working order 1 ŌåÆ 2 ŌåÆ 3 ŌåÆ 4 ŌåÆ 0; Phase 0 = the WWDC-watch gate, moved to the END on 2026-06-04 ŌĆö the early phases are WWDC-resilient). **Phase 1 shipped + DEVICE-VERIFIED (2026-06-04, `latest` TestFlight)** ŌĆö "Hey Siri, create a poll in WhoeverWants" opens the app to the existing create modal with the spoken prompt prefilled as the title. No native poll logic, no auth bridge: the WebView stays the source of truth. Confirmed working end-to-end on a real device by the owner: the phrase triggers the intent, Siri prompts for the prompt text (`requestValueDialog`), the **latest iOS app opens** (NOT Safari ŌĆö see the resolved platform risk below), and the spoken phrase appears prefilled in the title preview.

- **Swift is colocated in `ios/App/App/AppDelegate.swift`** (no pbxproj change ŌĆö `AppIntent` / `AppShortcutsProvider` are auto-discovered, same colocation rule as the plugins): `CreatePollIntent` (`AppIntent`, `openAppWhenRun = true`, required free-text `prompt: String` with `requestValueDialog`) returns `OpensIntent(OpenURLIntent(...))` to a per-tier universal link `https://<host>/g/?create=1&title=<spoken>` (host from `Bundle.main.bundleIdentifier`: prod ŌåÆ `whoeverwants.com`, canary ŌåÆ `latest.whoeverwants.com`, mirroring `capacitor.config.ts`). `WhoeverWantsShortcuts: AppShortcutsProvider` exposes the phrases. Both types are `@available(iOS 18.0, *)` ŌĆö **NOT 16**: `OpenURLIntent` (the loopback-correct opener for the app's own universal link) is iOS 18+, even though App Intents themselves are 16+. (CI caught the original iOS-16 gate ŌĆö the iOS archive failed with "'OpenURLIntent' is only available in iOS 18.0 or newer".) The shortcut is additive, so iOS 16ŌĆō17 users just don't see it; the pre-18 alternatives are worse (`UIApplication.open` of your own universal link opens Safari; a custom scheme adds Info.plist + CI + JS surface ŌĆö that's the documented follow-up if broader reach is needed). `import AppIntents` added.
- **The deep link is consumed by the EXISTING universal-link path** ŌĆö `lib/universalLinks.ts: appUrlOpen` ŌåÆ `pathFromUniversalLinkUrl` already strips the origin and `router.push`es `path+query` for the known hosts, so the new `?title=`/`?category=`/`?create=` params flow through with no change. The mechanism reuses associated-domains routing; nothing new on the JS routing side.
- **Web prefill lives in `app/create-poll/page.tsx`** (the persistent `CreateQuestionContent` host, which reads `useSearchParams`). A new effect ŌĆö mirroring the `?duplicate=` / `?voteFromSuggestion=` auto-open flows ŌĆö fires when `?title=` or `?create=` is present: `applyDraftToState(emptyDraft({category}))` (category via the module-level `normalizePrefillCategory`, which validates against `BUILT_IN_TYPES` values + `custom` and falls back to `custom`), `setTitle(spoken)` + `setIsAutoTitle(false)` (so the auto-title effect doesn't clobber the spoken text; deliberately NOT `loadedTitleRef`, which is the duplicate-snapshot path that can flip back to auto mode), `setIsModalOpen(true)`, then strips the three params via `history.replaceState` so a refresh/back doesn't reopen. The `loadFormState` mount-restore is gated off when `?title=`/`?create=` is present so stale saved state can't overwrite the prefill.
- **Verification needs a real device** (Siri/App Intents can't run in Simulator/headless, like Push/Haptics/Geolocation). The web half is live the moment the branch deploys to its tier host; only the Swift half needs a fresh iOS build. **Platform risk ŌĆö RESOLVED (2026-06-04, device-verified on `latest`):** `OpenURLIntent` of our OWN host opens the app, NOT Safari (as expected, since the `latest` bundle's `applinks:latest.whoeverwants.com` entitlement claims the host). The custom-URL-scheme fallback is therefore NOT needed for Phase 1. The full chain was confirmed on a real device: "create a poll in WhoeverWants" ŌåÆ Siri `requestValueDialog` prompt ŌåÆ spoken title ŌåÆ app opens to the create modal with the title prefilled in the preview (`setTitle(spoken)` + `setIsAutoTitle(false)` holding against the auto-title effect).
- **Phase 2 SHIPPED (native identity bridge, Keychain).** Mirrors the WebView's identity (session bearer token, browser id, display name) into the iOS Keychain so native Swift (and the headless creation App Intent, Phase 3) can call the API *as the user*.
  - **ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ DEVICE-VERIFY FINDING (2026-06-04): the original "plain Keychain, no entitlement (Phase 3 is in-process)" decision was WRONG and broke Phase 3.** The owner reported "quick poll" speaking *"Open WhoeverWants and set your name first"* even with the name set, and **foregrounding the app (which DID run `syncNativeIdentity` and write the Keychain) never fixed it**. Root cause: iOS runs a no-`openAppWhenRun` App Intent in a process SEPARATE from the app, so `QuickPollService.loadIdentity()`'s read landed in the intent's own default access group and never saw the item the foreground app wrote to ITS default group ŌåÆ `loadIdentity()` always nil. Phase 1 ("create a poll") is unaffected because it's a pure deep-link that never reads the Keychain ŌĆö which is exactly why it "didn't get blocked." **Fix shipped: a dedicated shared keychain access group.** `keychain-access-groups` in `App.entitlements` lists entry 0 = the existing default group (`$(AppIdentifierPrefix)$(CFBundleIdentifier)`, kept first so unscoped keychain users ŌĆö e.g. capgo social-login ŌĆö keep their default) + entry 1 = `ŌĆ”$(CFBundleIdentifier).siri`; `NativeIdentityKeychain.baseQuery` now sets `kSecAttrAccessGroup` to the runtime-resolved `479DZ4AZT5.<bundle>.siri` on every write/read/delete, so both contexts target one partition both entitlements list. **Build/portal note:** the entitlement needs "Keychain Sharing" on each App ID; automatic signing (`-allowProvisioningUpdates` + Admin API key) auto-provisions it like the existing aps-environment / applesignin / associated-domains entitlements. The build's "Scope associated-domains entitlement" step is a *targeted* PlistBuddy edit on the associated-domains key only, so it leaves `keychain-access-groups` intact. **Still needs on-device verification** on a fresh `latest` TestFlight build (Keychain/Siri can't be tested in Simulator/headless). If signing ever fails on a Keychain-Sharing capability error, enable it manually on `com.whoeverwants.app` + `com.whoeverwants.app.latest` in the Apple Developer portal (mirrors the one-time steps for Push / Sign In with Apple / Associated Domains).
  - **Storage details:** Pieces:
  - **Swift (`AppDelegate.swift`, colocated):** `NativeIdentityKeychain` (`kSecClassGenericPassword`, service namespaced per bundle id, accessibility `kSecAttrAccessibleAfterFirstUnlockThisDeviceOnly` ŌĆö readable by a background intent after first unlock, NOT iCloud-synced, NOT restore-migrated) + `NativeIdentityPlugin` (`CAPBridgedPlugin`, jsName `NativeIdentity`) with `setIdentity({token, browserId, name})` / `clearIdentity()` / `getIdentity()`. `set` upserts a non-empty value and DELETES on null/`""`, so ONE `setIdentity` call expresses the full triple (sign-out = null token + null name, kept browser id). `import Security`; no `@available` gate (Keychain works on every supported iOS, unlike the iOS-18 `OpenURLIntent`).
  - **JS (`lib/nativeIdentity.ts` + `components/NativeIdentityHost.tsx`):** `syncNativeIdentity()` reads live `getSessionToken` / `getBrowserId` / trimmed `getUserName` and pushes via the plugin; **inert on web/PWA** (`!Capacitor.isNativePlatform()` short-circuit ŌĆö registers a plugin that doesn't exist there is avoided by the early return). `installNativeIdentitySync()` (idempotent module flag like `installSwMessageBridge`, mounted once from `app/layout.tsx` via `<NativeIdentityHost/>`) subscribes to `SESSION_CHANGED_EVENT` + a focus/visibilitychange resync + an initial sync at launch.
  - **Wiring = ONE listener, not per-callsite.** Deliberately did NOT thread `setIdentity` into `saveSession` / `clearSession` / `persistSignIn` ŌĆö that needs a lazy-require to dodge the `session.ts Ōåö nativeIdentity.ts` import cycle. Instead subscribe once to `SESSION_CHANGED_EVENT` (which `saveSession`, `clearSession`, AND `updateCachedSessionUser` all already dispatch); equivalent coverage, no cycle, reads live values at event time. Foreground resync catches a browser id established post-mount + local-only name edits that don't dispatch the event.
  - **Security note:** moving the bearer token from WebView localStorage into the Keychain is a *stronger* at-rest posture (device-only, non-iCloud, encrypted), not a regression. The Keychain-Sharing entitlement (added by the device-verify fix above) shares ONLY the `ŌĆ”ŌĆŗ.siri` group between the app and its OWN intent (same team, two bundles); it does not widen exposure to other apps.
  - **Tests:** `tests/__tests__/native-identity.test.ts` pins gating + payload (Keychain round-trip is device-only). **Not demoable on the dev server** ŌĆö native-iOS-only, no web-visible surface; needs a fresh iOS build + TestFlight to verify on a real device.
- **Phase 3 SHIPPED + HEADLESS DEVICE-VERIFIED (2026-06-05, canary `latest`). WWDC re-check still owed before PROD.** "Hey Siri, quick poll in WhoeverWants" ŌåÆ Siri asks the question. **When the native identity is readable it creates the poll via the API headlessly and opens the app to confirm; when it ISN'T, it falls back to the Phase 1 deep link (opens the create form prefilled).** Either way the user always gets their poll. All colocated in `AppDelegate.swift`.
  - **ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ VERIFIED ON DEVICE (2026-06-05, `latest` TestFlight build carrying #611 + #615): headless creation WORKS end-to-end.** The plugin-registration fix (#611) made the foreground `setIdentity` write land (canary stdout: `[client-log] ŌĆ” [native-identity] setIdentity resolved`), the App Group cross-process read succeeded, and the intent's native `URLSession` `POST /api/polls` returned `201 Created` (confirmed via `bash scripts/remote-latest.sh "docker compose logs ŌĆ” api | grep 'POST /api/polls'"`) with the app un-launched. **Invoked via Spotlight ("Quick poll" ŌåÆ type the prompt), NOT voice** ŌĆö voice routing is a separate, still-flaky layer (see below). The plugin-registration ŌåÆ App-Group-write ŌåÆ headless-read ŌåÆ create chain is now proven; the 5-cycle blocker is closed.
    - **Diagnostic gotcha found + fixed (web-only, `lib/nativeIdentity.ts`).** The one-shot `[native-identity]` log latched on the FIRST `syncNativeIdentity` (the app-launch sync, which on a fresh install runs before localStorage identity exists), so it always read `hasToken=false hasName=false hasBrowserId=false` and SUPPRESSED the later populated write ŌĆö proving the plugin RESOLVES but hiding whether the real identity reached the bridge. Now only a NON-EMPTY resolve latches the log; a rejection still logs immediately. The actual WRITE was always populated (`setIdentity(...)` runs before the log check) ŌĆö which is why headless creation worked despite the misleading empty log.
    - **Success-path UX change (this branch, native): open to the NEW POLL, not bare home.** On device the headless success opened `feHomeURL` (`/`), but the WebView was already mounted on `/`, so `appUrlOpen` ŌåÆ `router.push('/')` was a no-op ŌĆö the home list never re-fetched and the new poll didn't appear until the user navigated away and back. (Also: opening the app suppresses the spoken `dialog`, so via Spotlight there was no confirmation at all; via voice Siri it WOULD speak it.) Fix: `QuickPollService.createPoll` now returns a `CreatedPoll {title, path}` parsed from the response's `group_short_id` + `short_id`, and the success branch opens `feURL(path: "/g/<groupShort>/p/<pollShort>")` ŌĆö the user lands directly ON their freshly-created poll (visual confirmation in every context, and a real navigation so it shows immediately). Both branches still return `OpenURLIntent` (uniform `some` return type); `feHomeURL()` is the parse-failure fallback. Needs a fresh `latest` build + reinstall to test.
    - **Voice trigger still unreliable (separate from headless ŌĆö `CFBundleSpokenName` + iOS re-indexing).** On device, "Hey Siri, quick poll in Whoever Wants" was transcribed as "quick PULL in whoever wants" (pollŌåÆpull speech-to-text miss) and Siri returned the generic "I didn't get that" ŌĆö never reaching the intent. This is the voice-match layer, NOT the headless logic (which Spotlight proved works). Mitigations (owner): **restart the iPhone** to force iOS to rebuild the Siri shortcut index for the new spoken name (#615 has lag after reinstall), try "Post a poll in Whoever Wants", and re-confirm after the `CFBundleSpokenName="Whoever Wants"` build has settled. The Spotlight / Shortcuts-app path is the dependable voice-free trigger meanwhile.
  - **ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ ROOT CAUSE FOUND + FIX SHIPPED to branch (2026-06-05): app-target Capacitor plugins were NEVER registered.** The headless read failed because the `NativeIdentity` App Group came up empty ŌĆö and the App Group is empty because the foreground WRITE never landed, because the colocated `NativeIdentityPlugin` was never registered with the Capacitor bridge. **App-target `CAPBridgedPlugin` classes are NOT auto-discovered** (Capacitor's runtime discovery only covers CocoaPods/SPM-packaged plugins); a class compiled into the app binary must be registered by hand. The Swift comments + CLAUDE.md asserting "auto-discovers at runtime, no change beyond compiling the class" were WRONG and silently broke ALL THREE colocated plugins (`NativeIdentity`/`ClipboardUrl`/`AppBadge` ŌĆö none was ever device-confirmed). **Fix:** `MainViewController.capacitorDidLoad()` now calls `bridge?.registerPluginInstance(...)` for each (the documented Capacitor pattern, capacitorjs.com/docs/ios/custom-code). **Plus a one-shot diagnostic** in `syncNativeIdentity` (`lib/nativeIdentity.ts`) logging the first `setIdentity` outcome (resolve vs reject, presence-flags only ŌĆö no secrets) so the owner can confirm on canary via `/api/client-logs?search=native-identity` that the plugin now resolves. **Owner verification owed (needs the change on `main` + a fresh `latest` iOS build, then a real device):** confirm the log says `setIdentity resolved` (was the silent `"NativeIdentity" plugin is not implemented on ios` reject), then say "Hey Siri, quick poll in WhoeverWants" and confirm it creates HEADLESSLY (app stays closed, "Created your poll: ŌĆ”") instead of the deep-link fallback. Once the App Group write lands, `QuickPollIntent`'s success branch takes over automatically ŌĆö no further intent changes. **Foundation already in place:** App Group + keychain entitlements (provisioned), `NativeIdentityAppGroup` (written in `setIdentity`, read in `loadIdentity`), and the success/fallback `QuickPollIntent` structure ŌĆö only the registration was missing. The earlier device sequence that motivated this: (1) plain Keychain ŌåÆ "set your name first"; (2) dedicated `keychain-access-groups` group ŌåÆ still nil; (3) native spoken diagnostic ŌåÆ `shared no, default no, group set` (intent process can't read the app's Keychain in ANY access group ŌĆö it's isolated); (4) switched to a shared App Group ŌåÆ intent read `appgroup name no` too; (5) ŌåÆ the write-never-lands hypothesis, now confirmed-by-inspection as the missing plugin registration. **Siri voice-trigger reliability ŌĆö SHIPPED (`CFBundleSpokenName`, separate from the headless work).** Two installed apps "Whoever"(prod)+"Whoever ╬▒"(latest) routed ambiguously and the "╬▒" glyph matched poorly when speaking the App Shortcut phrase. Fix: `ios-build.yml`'s display-name stamp step now sets `CFBundleSpokenName="Whoever Wants"` for the **latest** tier ONLY (the phonetic name Siri/VoiceOver use for VOICE matching, distinct from the on-screen `CFBundleDisplayName="Whoever ╬▒"`); **prod is deliberately left WITHOUT a spoken name** so it falls back to "Whoever" ŌĆö keeping the two installed apps' spoken forms DISTINCT ("Whoever" vs "Whoever Wants") so Siri can still route a phrase to the right app when both are installed (a shared spoken name would re-introduce the ambiguity). The committed `ios/App/App/Info.plist` carries no spoken name, so prod/local builds are clean by default; only the latest workflow branch injects it (single source of truth ŌĆö unlike `CFBundleDisplayName`, which has a committed default for local Xcode builds; `CFBundleSpokenName` falls back to the display name when unset, so no committed default is needed). Needs a fresh `latest` iOS build + reinstall to take effect (iOS caches the Siri shortcut index; uninstall/reinstall also forces a re-index, with lag). The deep-link fallback already solves the user-facing problem ("quick poll" opens the app prefilled); this makes the spoken trigger dependable on canary so the headless path can actually be exercised by voice.
  - **Siri tier-name matching gotcha (device-observed):** with BOTH apps installed, Siri fuzzy-matched the spoken "WhoeverWants" to prod's display name "Whoever"; after uninstalling prod (leaving only latest, display name **"Whoever ╬▒"**), Siri stopped responding to the voice command. App Shortcut phrases MUST contain `\(.applicationName)` (Apple requirement), which resolves to the per-tier CFBundleDisplayName ŌĆö and the "╬▒" glyph in the latest name is a poor Siri match. Uninstalling an app also forces a Siri shortcut re-index (lag). Remedies: restart the device (re-index), say the phrase with the actual app name ("Quick poll in Whoever"), and/or set `CFBundleSpokenName` to a Siri-friendly form. **The `CFBundleSpokenName` remedy is now SHIPPED for the latest tier ("Whoever Wants")** ŌĆö see the "Siri voice-trigger reliability ŌĆö SHIPPED" bullet above; on a fresh `latest` build saying "ŌĆ”in Whoever Wants" matches reliably regardless of the on-screen "╬▒".
  - **The fallback design (why both paths open the app):** Swift's opaque `some` return type requires every `return` to share ONE underlying type ŌĆö you CANNOT mix `.result(dialog:)` (headless speak) with `.result(opensIntent:dialog:)` (open) in one `perform()` ([Apple forums 740707 / 738339](https://developer.apple.com/forums/thread/740707)). So to make the failure path open the app, BOTH branches return an `OpenURLIntent`-based result: success ŌåÆ `OpenURLIntent(feHomeURL())` + "Created your poll: X", failure ŌåÆ `OpenURLIntent(CreatePollIntent.createURL(prompt:))` + "Let's finish your pollŌĆ”". Headless `createPoll` is still attempted first (best-effort, `try?`); ANY failure (no readable identity / network / server) silently falls through to the open-the-form branch, so it can never dead-end. The `QuickPollError` path remains only for an empty spoken prompt.
  - **`QuickPollIntent` is now `@available(iOS 18.0, *)`** (was 16): `OpenURLIntent` is iOS 18+. The spoken phrase already required iOS 18 (AppShortcuts), so only manual Shortcuts-app use on iOS 16ŌĆō17 is lost. Still a SECOND `AppShortcut` on the iOS-18 `WhoeverWantsShortcuts` provider with distinct phrases ("Quick poll in ŌĆ”" / "Quickly create a poll in ŌĆ”" / "Post a poll in ŌĆ”", `bolt.fill`) so Siri disambiguates it from the Phase 1 "Create a pollŌĆ”" intent.
  - **`QuickPollService`:** `loadIdentity()` reads `NativeIdentityKeychain` and **gates on the display NAME, NOT the token** ŌĆö `creator_name` is the only hard server requirement (`validate_user_name` 400s a blank); the bearer is optional (an anonymous-but-named user has a browser-keyed auto-account, exactly as for an in-app anonymous create). `createPoll()` POSTs the minimal single-yes/no body (`creator_name` + `title` + one `{question_type: "yes_no", context: prompt}`, mirroring the FE's `draftToQuestionParams` for a single yes_no draft) to the **direct API host** (`apiBase`: prod bundle ŌåÆ `api.whoeverwants.com`, canary ŌåÆ `api.latest.whoeverwants.com` ŌĆö the API host, NOT the FE host the WebView loads), with `Authorization: Bearer <token>` (when present) + `X-Browser-Id`. Returns the server-echoed title.
  - **`QuickPollError` (`CustomLocalizedStringResourceConvertible`):** every failure throws a Siri-speakable sentence (no name ŌåÆ "set your name first"; network ŌåÆ "couldn't reachŌĆ”"; 401 ŌåÆ "sign-in expired"; other non-2xx ŌåÆ "open the app and try there").
  - **`OpensIntent` is now USED (the original "never open, app un-launched" criterion was relaxed).** The plan's "app stays closed" goal is currently unattainable because the headless read is broken (above), and the fallback MUST open the app ŌĆö so quick-poll opens the app on every path today (success ŌåÆ confirm; failure ŌåÆ prefilled form). If the headless read is ever fixed, success still opens (to confirm the created poll) under this design; a truly-closed success path would require splitting the dialog/open cases (not possible under one `some` return ŌĆö see the fallback-design bullet) or a snippet view.
  - **No backend or JS changes.** The native-only changes are: the `keychain-access-groups` entitlement (App.entitlements) + `kSecAttrAccessGroup` in `NativeIdentityKeychain` + the `QuickPollIntent` fallback. The Keychain round-trip + API call are native-iOS-only ŌĆö **not unit-testable in the JS suite, not demoable on the dev server.** A stale bearer degrades to an anonymous browser-keyed create (resolves to the account via the browserŌåÆuser link) rather than 401, so even an expired session keeps working.
- **Phase 4 App Entities FOUNDATION SHIPPED (2026-06-05, owner device-verify owed).** The WWDC-resilient substrate so Siri/Shortcuts/Spotlight can reference the user's polls BY NAME ŌĆö the prerequisite the rest of Phase 4 (vote-by-voice, query-results) reuses for poll disambiguation. All colocated in `AppDelegate.swift`:
  - **`PollEntity` (`AppEntity`, `@available(iOS 16.0, *)`)** ŌĆö `id` = poll short_id (canonical addressable id) + `title` + `groupShortId` + `groupName`; `displayRepresentation` = title with group-name subtitle. `static func fetchAll()` POSTs `/api/groups/mine` (`{include_results:false}`) with the bridged `X-Browser-Id` (Phase 2 App Group; bearer added when present), prefers `questions[0].title` over the display `title` (avoids the group-name-override collapse, same rule the detail-page header uses), sorts newest-first by `created_at` (ISO-8601 lexicographic), caps 50, and **NEVER throws** (returns `[]` on no-identity/network/parse failure ŌåÆ consumer degrades to "no polls to pick").
  - **`PollEntityQuery` (`EntityQuery, EntityStringQuery`, iOS 16+)** ŌĆö `entities(for:)` id-resolve, `entities(matching:)` case-insensitive substring voice-match over title+group name, `suggestedEntities()` for the Spotlight/Shortcuts picker; all delegate to `fetchAll()`.
  - **`OpenPollIntent` (`AppIntent`, `openAppWhenRun`, iOS 18+)** ŌĆö the thin consumer that proves the entity end-to-end: `@Parameter var poll: PollEntity` ŌåÆ opens `/g/<group>/p/<short>` (legacy `/p/<short>` fallback) via the same `OpenURLIntent` loopback as Phase 1/3. Gated iOS 18 ONLY for `OpenURLIntent`; the entity+query are iOS 16 so a future headless iOS-16 intent (e.g. spoken "who's winningŌĆ”") reuses them. Added to `WhoeverWantsShortcuts` ("Open \(\.$poll) in ŌĆ”" / "Show \(\.$poll) in ŌĆ”" / bare "Open a poll in ŌĆ”").
  - **Visibility is BROWSER-SCOPED** (documented limitation, same as Phase 3 headless create): the App Group bridges name + browser id, not the bearer, so `fetchAll` resolves the groups THIS browser is a member of ŌĆö every poll created/joined on this device. Cross-device-only polls won't surface until opened here.
  - **No backend/JS change** (`/api/groups/mine` already returns the needed shape). Native-only ŌĆö not unit-testable in the JS suite or demoable on the dev server (like Phases 2/3); the `IntentDescription` keeps "siri" out per ITMS-90626. When wiring vote-by-voice / query-results, add a `@Parameter var poll: PollEntity` and reuse `PollEntityQuery` ŌĆö don't refetch/re-resolve polls a second way.
- **Phase 4 `GroupEntity` + create-in-group SHIPPED (2026-06-05, owner device-verify owed).** The group-level analog of `PollEntity`, plus a create intent that targets a named group ("Add a poll to the trip group"). All colocated in `AppDelegate.swift`:
  - **`GroupEntity` (`AppEntity`, iOS 16) + `GroupEntityQuery` (`EntityStringQuery`, iOS 16).** `id` = group **short_id** (addressable `/g/<id>`); `groupUuid` = the `groups.id` UUID carried SEPARATELY because the addressable id ŌēĀ the create key for groups (they coincide for polls, where `PollEntity.id` is both). `title` = group name (override ŌåÆ participant-names ŌåÆ "Group", mirroring the FE `buildGroups` default-title incl. dropping the current user via the bridged `identity.name`); `pollCount` drives the subtitle. `fetchAll()` runs `POST /api/groups/mine` (`{include_results:false}`, collapsed by `group_id`) **concurrently** (`async let`) with `POST /api/groups/empty` (membership-only groups), browser-scoped via the bridged `X-Browser-Id` (Phase 2 App Group; bearer added when present); NEVER throws (`[]` on no-identity/network/parse), newest-first by `created_at`, cap 50. Same browser-scoped-visibility limitation as `PollEntity`. The query does id-resolve + case-insensitive title match + `suggestedEntities()` for Spotlight/the Shortcuts picker.
  - **`QuickPollInGroupIntent` (`AppIntent`, iOS 18)** ŌĆö required spoken `prompt` + required `group: GroupEntity` (resolved via `GroupEntityQuery`). Runs the SAME headless-or-fall-back flow as `QuickPollIntent`, factored into the shared `QuickPollService.quickPollOutcome(prompt:group:)` (iOS-18 extension; both intents call it, so the device-verified no-group path is byte-identical ŌĆö only the success dialog gains "ŌĆ” in <group>"). **Headless:** the group UUID rides the create POST's `group_id` (server attaches; unknown id ŌåÆ mint fresh, no 404 ŌĆö so a stale uuid degrades gracefully). **Fallback:** the deep link routes to `/g/<short>?create=1&title=ŌĆ”` (NOT the empty `/g/` placeholder), so the WebView create form attaches via the existing `<body data-group-id>` flow ŌĆö group targeting survives the fallback with zero web changes. Kept a SEPARATE intent (not an optional `group` param on `QuickPollIntent`) to (a) leave the verified no-group path untouched and (b) avoid mixing parameter-bound + bare phrases in one `AppShortcut`. Added to `WhoeverWantsShortcuts` with `\(\.$group)`-bound phrases ("Add a poll to \(\.$group) in ŌĆ”" / "Create a poll for \(\.$group) in ŌĆ”") ŌĆö using "to"/"for" before the group so the app-name "in" suffix doesn't read "in ŌĆ” in ŌĆ”".
  - **No backend/JS change** ŌĆö `/api/groups/mine`, `/api/groups/empty`, the `CreatePollRequest.group_id` field, the `?create=1&title=` deep-link prefill, and the `data-group-id` attribution all already exist (this change only COMBINES them natively). Native-only ŌåÆ not unit-testable/demoable. When wiring a future group-scoped op (e.g. "create in <group>" with richer params), reuse `GroupEntity`/`GroupEntityQuery` + `quickPollOutcome` ŌĆö don't re-fetch groups a second way. Note the short_id-vs-uuid split: use `GroupEntity.groupUuid` for any API call keyed on `group_id`, `GroupEntity.id` for any `/g/<short>` URL.
- **Phase 4+ remaining (backlog):** vote-by-voice (`POST /api/polls/{id}/votes` + `PollEntity` param), query-results (read-only GET, speak the leader, iOS-16 headless), richer creation (multi-question, deadlines). Phase 0 (the deferred WWDC watch) runs last and feeds a re-validation pass over Phases 3ŌĆō4. See the plan doc.

---

## Invite Members (In-App Address Book)

From `/g/<id>/info`, a member taps **"Add people"** (above the members list) to open `/g/<id>/invite-members` ŌĆö a screen that searches the caller's contacts, selects accounts with round checkboxes (whole row tappable), and adds them on **Update** (gated on Ōēź1 selection, behind a `ConfirmationModal`). Added accounts get a push. Shipped on `claude/group-member-invitations-DuZXc` (migration 126).

- **Contacts are an account-to-account address book (migration 126, `user_contacts(owner_user_id, contact_user_id, first_seen_at, last_seen_at)`, PK `(owner, contact)`).** We track ACCOUNTS (user_id), not names ŌĆö the display name is resolved per-account at read time. The relationship is PERSISTED so the invite screen can still surface (and recency-sort) someone the caller no longer shares any group with.
- **`last_seen_at` is the persisted recency watermark; "current shared-group count" is NOT stored ŌĆö it's computed live** in `list_invitable_accounts`. The two power the sort: primary = current shared-group count desc (accounts you're in more groups with float to the top), secondary = `last_seen_at` desc (accounts with 0 current shared groups, most-recently-seen first). The query's `ORDER BY shared_group_count DESC, c.last_seen_at DESC, u.display_name ASC` gives exactly that (0-count rows sort after any positive count automatically).
- **`services/contacts.py: reconcile_contacts(conn, owner_user_id)` is the maintenance primitive** ŌĆö one idempotent upsert of every account the owner CURRENTLY shares a group with, bumping `last_seen_at=NOW()`. It runs on the read paths the owner already hits: inline in the candidates endpoint, AND decoupled (via `reconcile_contacts_safe` as a `BackgroundTasks` task) on `POST /api/groups/mine`. **Reconcile-on-`/mine` is the load-bearing always-running hook** ŌĆö it's what captures the encounter + recency WHILE the owner still shares the group, so a contact survives both of them leaving it later. Reconcile-on-screen-open alone wouldn't suffice (someone who never opens the invite screen would never record contacts). Deliberately NOT wired into the vote/visit/approve/redeem membership-write paths ŌĆö whatever the owner currently shares gets captured on their next home load.
- **Account-aware on both sides.** "The owner's memberships" unions every browser linked to the owner's account (mirroring `load_user_visibility`), and a contact's memberships union every browser linked to the contact's account. Same `browser_id IN (SELECT browser_id FROM user_browsers WHERE user_id = ...)` pattern used everywhere else.
- **Endpoints in `routers/groups.py`** (between the join-request and Phase-G-invite sections):
  - `GET /{route_id}/invitable-accounts` ŌåÆ `InvitableAccountResponse[]` (`{user_id, name, shared_group_count, last_seen_at}`). Reconciles the caller inline, then reads. **Authorization is MEMBERSHIP (`is_caller_member_of_group`), not creator-only** ŌĆö consistent with the existing model where any member can already invite anyone by sharing the group URL. An account-less caller (no resolvable `user_id` via `resolve_actor_user_id`) returns `[]` rather than erroring (they have no contacts). 404 unresolvable route, 403 non-member.
  - `POST /{route_id}/members` body `{user_ids: [...]}` ŌåÆ `{added: N}`. Each id must (a) be a valid uuid (`_is_uuid_like`, skipped silently otherwise ŌĆö NOT 404'd, so one bad id doesn't fail the batch), (b) NOT be the caller, and (c) be in the caller's `user_contacts` (`is_contact`) ŌĆö so a member can't add an arbitrary stranger by guessing user_ids. `add_member_for_user` writes the `group_members` row keyed on the account's earliest-linked browser_id (same pattern as `decide_request`), returning `True` only when a NEW membership was established (already-a-member via any browser ŌåÆ skipped, no dup, no notification). Newly-added accounts get a `fan_out_to_user` push.
- **`fan_out_to_user(group_id, user_id, payload)` in `services/push.py`** is the generic "push one group-scoped notification to one account's browsers" primitive (renamed from `fan_out_member_added` once a third caller ŌĆö plus-ones ŌĆö appeared; callers build their own payloads). Targets `user_browsers WHERE user_id = user_id` (one specific account, not the group at large), gated on the same default-ON `notify_new_poll` pref as `fan_out_join_request` (a fresh member has no pref row ŌåÆ ON). Byte-for-byte the join-request fan-out shape. For the member-added case the payload is: title `Added to <group_phrase>` (via `group_name_phrase`), body `<inviter> added you to the group` (falls back to "You were added to a group" when the inviter has no display_name), `url: /g/<route>` (path form, not `?p=`).
- **FE: new slide-overlay kind `groupInviteMembers`** (`lib/eventChannels.ts` union + `lib/slideOverlay.tsx` `renderForKind` case + `slideToGroupInviteMembers` helper). The route `app/g/[groupShortId]/invite-members/page.tsx` exports the prop-driven `GroupInviteMembersView` (mirrors the `GroupInfoView` split). It is NOT a group-root view (`isGroupRootView` doesn't match it), so it gets the plain `max-w-4xl mx-auto px-4 pb-6` layout like `/info` / `/edit-title`. Back arrow ŌåÆ `slideToGroupInfo({direction:'back'})`.
- **Pitfall: a left-aligned `<h1>` at the top of a subroute collides with the floating `<HeaderPortal>` back/action buttons.** `/info` avoids this because its first content is a CENTERED hero (the buttons float beside it). The invite screen's left-aligned "Add people" title needed `paddingTop: calc(env(safe-area-inset-top, 0px) + 3.5rem)` (vs `/info`'s 1.05rem) to clear the ~40px button row. Any future subroute whose first element is left-aligned text at the top needs the larger top padding, not the hero-page value.
- **Round-checkbox markup is copied from `GroupListItem.tsx`'s selection checkbox** (`w-6 h-6 rounded-full border-2`, blue-fill + white check when selected). Each candidate row is a full-width `<button>` (whole line tappable) containing checkbox + `InitialBubble` avatar + name. Other accounts render initials only (`useMyUserImageUrl` resolves the CURRENT user's photo only ŌĆö cross-user images are out of scope).
- **FE clients in `lib/api/groups.ts`**: `apiGetGroupInvitableAccounts(routeId)` + `apiAddGroupMembers(routeId, userIds)` (+ `InvitableAccount` type), re-exported from `lib/api/index.ts`. Search is purely client-side name filtering over the server-pre-sorted list (order preserved); the list is bounded by "people you share groups with" so no server `?q=` search endpoint was needed.
- **Direct-add semantics (not invite-they-accept).** The added account becomes a member immediately + gets notified ŌĆö there is no pending-acceptance step (that's what Phase F join-requests are for, in the opposite direction). If an accept-first flow is ever wanted, it's a different shape; don't bolt it onto this endpoint.
- Tests: `server/tests/test_invite_members.py` (candidates exclude members + self, count-then-recency sort, member-gate 403, only-own-contacts addable, idempotent add, 404 route). Test setup writes `group_members` rows directly + sets `display_name` via DB rather than driving the full join/name flow.

---

## Group Avatar Images

Groups can have a custom uploaded image avatar that replaces the participant-initials graphic. **Storage**: inline on the `groups` row ŌĆö migration 108 added `image_data BYTEA`, `image_mime_type TEXT`, `image_updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ` columns. Keeping bytes in Postgres (vs filesystem / object storage) means pg_dump captures them automatically, no second storage surface to provision per-branch on the Mac dev infrastructure, and "destroy + recreate dev DB" stays a one-step operation. Trade-off accepted for the current scale.

**API**:
- `POST /api/groups/{route_id}/image` ŌĆö base64 JSON body (`{image_base64, mime_type}`); JPEG/PNG only; 5 MiB cap. No creator-secret check, same trust model as `/title`.
- `DELETE /api/groups/{route_id}/image` ŌĆö idempotent clear; returns 200 even when no image was set.
- `GET /api/groups/by-route-id/{route_id}/image` ŌĆö raw bytes with the stored MIME type and `Cache-Control: public, max-age=31536000, immutable`. The FE's `?v=<image_updated_at>` query string is the cache-buster.

**`image_updated_at` propagates as a wrapper field on every `PollResponse`.** Surfaced via the same `_SELECT_POLLS_WITH_GROUP` JOIN as `group_title` / `group_short_id` (extend the constant when adding a new joined groups field, NOT a parallel SELECT). FE `Poll.group_image_updated_at` flows through `toPoll`; `Group.imageUrl` is derived in `lib/groupUtils.ts: buildGroupImageUrl(routeId, ts)` and consumed by the new `<GroupAvatar>` wrapper.

**`<GroupAvatar imageUrl|names|anonymousCount|sizeClassName>`** in `components/GroupAvatar.tsx` replaces direct `<RespondentCircles>` use at every "this is the group's icon" surface: home list rows, group-page header, /info hero. When `imageUrl` is null, falls through to `RespondentCircles` for the initials graphic ŌĆö same outer dimensions either way, so swapping doesn't shift layout. Both variants render through SVG with a viewBox-100├Ś100 disc of radius `BOUNDING_RADIUS = 41.5` (exported from `RespondentCircles.tsx`, alongside `BOUNDING_DIAMETER = 83` and `BOUNDING_OFFSET = 8.5`). The image branch uses `<image>` with `preserveAspectRatio="xMidYMid slice"` clipped to the same disc; the initials branch packs N circles inside that disc with `LAYOUTS[n]` centers + `diameter`, scaled by `BOUNDING_SCALE[n]`. **`BOUNDING_SCALE` is computed from `LAYOUTS`** (`BOUNDING_RADIUS / max(distance_from_50_50 + r)`) ŌĆö don't hand-tune it; the formula encodes "snug to bounding circle". For multi-name tessellations, the parent SVG draws a `fill-gray-100 dark:fill-gray-800` backdrop circle of the same radius behind the initials so the bounding shape reads as a quiet container; gated `!isPlaceholder` (single-name and empty cases already cover the disc with a colored circle). **The home-list avatar size is `w-[4.8rem]` (76.8px)** ŌĆö bumped from the `w-16` (64px) default by 20% via `sizeClassName` in `components/GroupListItem.tsx`; other surfaces keep their own explicit overrides (`w-28` on /info, `w-[10.5rem]` on /edit-title). The text-column gets `mt-1` to nudge the title baseline toward the avatar's vertical center at the larger size.

**Symmetric `LAYOUTS[n]` is load-bearing for the bounding-disc backdrop.** All centers must be equidistant from (50,50), otherwise uniform scaling leaves child circles at different gaps from the outer ring ŌĆö visibly asymmetric. The original `LAYOUTS[3]` was `[[50, 26], [27, 74], [73, 74]]` (top circle at distance 24, bottom two at 33.24 ŌåÆ top sat further from outer ring after scaling). Replaced with equilateral `[[50, 22.708], [26.364, 63.646], [73.636, 63.646]]` ŌĆö all three at distance 27.292, all pair distances equal. When adding a new `LAYOUTS[n]` row, design it symmetric around (50,50) first; the BOUNDING_SCALE formula then snugs it into the disc with equal gap on every side.

**`<ImageCropModal>`** (`components/ImageCropModal.tsx`) is the drag + pinch-zoom + canvas-export cropper. Several traps learned the hard way:

- **iOS WebKit (Safari + iOS Firefox) silently fails `<img src="data:image/...">` for data URLs over ~1-2 MB.** Phone photos at 5-15 MB produced an empty crop circle. The fix is `URL.createObjectURL` for the displayed source ŌĆö blob URLs have no length limit. FileReader/data URLs are NOT a working substitute on mobile WebKit.
- **Pair `URL.createObjectURL` + `URL.revokeObjectURL` + `setUrl` inside ONE `useEffect`.** First attempt put the URL in `useState(() => createObjectURL(file))` lazy init, assuming React StrictMode would re-run the initializer on the simulated remount. **It doesn't** ŌĆö StrictMode preserves state across the dev mountŌåÆunmountŌåÆmount cycle; only effects re-run. So the cleanup revoked the URL while state kept pointing at it, and the img permanently displayed a dead URL. Pattern that works:
  ```tsx
  const [url, setUrl] = useState<string | null>(null);
  useEffect(() => {
    const u = URL.createObjectURL(file);
    setUrl(u);
    return () => { URL.revokeObjectURL(u); setUrl((prev) => prev === u ? null : prev); };
  }, [file]);
  ```
  The `setUrl(...)` in cleanup is load-bearing ŌĆö without it the img briefly keeps `src=URL_A` after the revoke, fires onError, and sets `loadError` permanently. With it, the img unmounts cleanly between StrictMode mounts.
- **Tailwind preflight ships `img { max-width: 100%; height: auto }` globally.** When the displayed img has explicit `width: 1737px` set inline AND its parent container is 370px, max-width caps the width at 370 BEFORE the transform: scale() runs ŌĆö so the transform downscales an already-clipped width, producing an image rendered at 1/N of the expected width and positioned off-screen. The fix is `maxWidth: 'none'` (and `maxHeight: 'none'` for safety) in the inline style. **This is a browser-agnostic bug**; my Playwright tests only checked `getBoundingClientRect().width > 0`, which was true even for the 78├Ś658-px sliver, so it slipped through. When testing image-sizing fixes, validate the rendered dims match the math.
- **Keep the displayed `<img>` mounted across the loadError ŌåÆ success transition.** Earlier the JSX gated the entire crop container on `!loadError`, so an onError firing for a stale URL_A unmounted the img ŌĆö the subsequent URL_B never got a chance to load. Render the img unconditionally (once `url` is set); show loading/error overlays on top. Successful onLoad sets imageDims AND clears loadError.
- **Don't allocate per-frame in pointermove.** The hot path runs at ~60Hz on touch. Iterate `pointersRef.current.values()` directly (Map iterator) ŌĆö don't `Array.from(...values())`, which allocates a fresh array each frame. Capture first/second pointer in the same loop for pinch math.
- **Canvas export**: 512├Ś512 JPEG at quality 0.9 ŌåÆ ~50-80 KB typically. Drawn from the freshly-loaded blob URL (the modal's URL stays alive until unmount).
- **5MP+ image render limits on iOS**: not actually a hard problem in practice (modern iPhones handle 12+ MP fine). Symptoms that look like image-decode failures on mobile have always traced back to one of the items above, not actual memory limits. Don't pre-resize on the client without evidence; the canvas export already downscales.

**Edit-title flow** (`app/g/[groupShortId]/edit-title/page.tsx`) defers all image + title changes to local state and commits via the Save button:
- Picking + cropping stages a `Blob` in `pendingCroppedBlob` and a derived blob URL in `localImagePreviewUrl` for the preview avatar. No server round-trip.
- Tapping the X badge stages `pendingImageRemoval = true` (and clears any `pendingCroppedBlob`).
- Save runs the staged image action (upload or delete), then the title update if changed, then navigates back. Skips the DELETE entirely when `pendingImageRemoval && !group.imageUrl` (no-op on a group without an image).
- Back checks `hasUnsavedChanges = titleChanged || imageChanged` and shows a `ConfirmationModal` ("Discard your changes?", red Discard button) if anything is staged. Confirm ŌåÆ navigate away without committing; cancel ŌåÆ stay.

The X-badge / camera-badge pattern needs both to be **siblings of the avatar button** inside a single `relative` wrapper ŌĆö NOT children of the same button ŌĆö so their click handlers stay independent (tapping X doesn't open the file picker). The X badge only renders when `effectiveImageUrl` is truthy (no point offering to remove a non-existent image).

**Template `py-6` was retired for sub-routes** (`app/template.tsx`). The page-wrapper used to apply `py-6` (24px top + bottom padding) to every route that wasn't home, settings, or `isGroupLikePage` ŌĆö so `/g/<id>/info` and `/g/<id>/edit-title` got 24px of extra top space ON TOP of their inline `paddingTop: calc(env(safe-area-inset-top, 0px) + 1.05rem)` for floating-button clearance. Changed to `pb-6` (drop top). Other routes in the bucket are redirect stubs where padding is irrelevant.

**(Historical) `accessibleQuestionIds` non-UUID 500 pitfall.** This is moot now: `/api/groups/mine` no longer resolves the `accessible_question_ids` list against the DB (the forget bridge is removed and the field is ignored), and `group_ids_for_question_ids` was deleted. The general lesson still stands ŌĆö when an endpoint casts an FE-supplied array to `uuid[]`, filter through a UUID regex first so one corrupt element can't 500 the whole call (`services/groups.py: require_uuid` / `_is_uuid_like` are the canonical guards for path-param uuids).

**Dev-infra trap (FIXED on `claude/remove-group-dividers-ion0C`)**: `scripts/mac-mini/dev-server-manager.sh`'s `INSERT INTO _migrations (filename) VALUES (:'fname')` line was broken since the script's inception ŌĆö the `:'fname'` psql variable substitution fails with `syntax error at or near ":"` when used inside `psql -c` (`-c` sends SQL to the server with no psql-level variable expansion). So `_migrations` never persisted, every upsert re-ran every migration from scratch, and any non-idempotent rename eventually corrupted the schema. The canonical fingerprint was the three-way `polls` + `multipolls` + `questions` state, caused by migration 092 (`CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS multipolls`) re-running after 097's first-pass rename had already renamed `multipolls ŌåÆ polls`, then 097's second pass failing because `questions` and `polls` both exist and rolling back, leaving subsequent ALTER COLUMNs to land on the wrong tables. Fix: interpolate `$basename` directly into the SQL string (`'$basename'`) ŌĆö the upstream regex check already rejects single quotes, so no injection vector. With `_migrations` actually persisting now, second-and-later upserts skip already-applied migrations and the drift cannot recur. If you encounter the three-way state on a long-lived dev DB created BEFORE this fix, destroy ŌåÆ upsert resolves it cleanly because migrations only run once on the fresh DB.

## User Profile Avatar Images

Users can upload a profile image on the settings page that replaces their initials circle wherever their name renders. **Storage: inline BYTEA on a `user_profiles` row keyed by `user_id` (migration 124 ŌĆö was keyed by `browser_id`, migration 109).** The photo is account data, like `users.display_name`: it follows the user across every signed-in device and **clears on sign-out**.
