- **`Coords` lives in `lib/userProfile.ts`, and `UserLocation extends Coords`.** Don't redefine the lat/lng pair locally ŌĆö import from `userProfile.ts`. The label (city/zip display string) is the only thing `UserLocation` adds on top.
- **Native dispatch uses the dynamic-import-Capacitor-plugin pattern** (`await import("@capacitor/...").catch(() => null)`), matching `lib/pushNotifications.ts: ensureCapacitorPushSubscription` and `lib/universalLinks.ts: installUniversalLinksHandler`. The chunk only loads on the native bundle; web bundles include the chunk but never execute it (the `Capacitor.isNativePlatform()` short-circuit returns false). Don't `import` the plugin statically at module top ŌĆö that pulls it into every web bundle for no benefit.
- **Four plugins now use this pattern** (`geolocation`, `pushNotifications`, `universalLinks`, `clipboardLinkPrompt`). The 5th occurrence triggers the extraction of a shared `loadCapacitorPlugin<T>(name, exportKey)` helper; the current ~4-line repetition is below the abstraction threshold.

## Haptics (Native + Web)

`lib/haptics.ts` is the canonical entry point for "give the user a tactile bump on this action" ŌĆö every callsite must route through `haptic.{light,medium,heavy,success,warning,error}()`, not `navigator.vibrate` directly.

- **`navigator.vibrate` is a no-op on iOS WebKit** ŌĆö Safari mobile, iOS PWA, and (most importantly) the Capacitor `WhoeverWants Latest` / prod WebView all ignore the Vibration API entirely. Apple has never implemented it. The pre-haptics-PR codebase had 4 `navigator.vibrate(N)` calls (long-press ├Ś 2, swipe-threshold, swipe-commit) that worked on Android but were silently dead on every iOS surface, which is the entire user-installed iOS app. Always route through `lib/haptics.ts` so the native-iOS branch fires Capacitor ŌåÆ Core Haptics. Treat any new `navigator.vibrate` in a PR as a bug.
- **Module pattern matches `lib/geolocation.ts` / `lib/pushNotifications.ts`.** Module-level `bridgePromise` caches the dynamic-imported `@capacitor/haptics` bridge; first call resolves it, every subsequent call awaits the same promise. On non-native (`!Capacitor.isNativePlatform()`) the dynamic import never runs and we fall straight through to `navigator.vibrate` (works on Android, no-op on iOS Safari / PWA ŌĆö acceptable, those users have no equivalent affordance).
- **Semantic levels, not raw durations.** Six exported wrappers (`haptic.light` / `.medium` / `.heavy` / `.success` / `.warning` / `.error`) each map to `ImpactStyle.Light/Medium/Heavy` + `NotificationType.Success/Warning/Error` on native, with web-vibrate fallback durations (`10/20/35/30/40/50` ms). Adopt iOS HIG conventions: impact for tap-feedback ("button registered"), notification for action results ("task done / failed"). Don't reach for the raw fallback ms ŌĆö pick the level that names the user-facing concept.
- **Fire at the moment of commit, not after API resolves.** Every instrumented site fires the haptic synchronously at the click handler entry (or at the modal-confirm callback) ŌĆö BEFORE the `await apiFoo(...)` call. Users expect the bump to coincide with the press, not with the network round-trip 500ms later. The `success` notification fires on commit for vote/save/create paths even though that's slightly off-spec (HIG says success = after the task completes); the trade-off is snap-of-feedback over technical correctness. If you ever need true "success after API" semantics, fire `haptic.medium()` on tap PLUS `haptic.success()` after the resolve ŌĆö but no current site does this.
- **Inventory of instrumented sites (commit moments only ŌĆö UI state changes below "form-field threshold" deliberately uninstrumented):**
  - Vote submit: `components/QuestionBallot.tsx: submitVote` (success), `lib/useGroupVoting.ts: confirmPollSubmit` (success), `lib/useGroupVoting.ts: submitYesNoChoice` (success).
  - Poll create: `app/create-poll/page.tsx: handleSubmitClick` (success ŌĆö fires after validation passes, before API call).
  - Confirmation modal confirms (close/reopen/cutoff-suggestions/cutoff-availability/forget): `app/g/[groupShortId]/GroupPage.tsx` `pendingAction` `onConfirm` (single `haptic.medium()` at the top of the handler, BEFORE the per-kind branches so the same feel applies to every action).
  - Bulk-forget confirm: `components/GroupList.tsx: handleConfirmDelete` (medium).
  - Edit-title + group image save: `app/g/[groupShortId]/edit-title/page.tsx: save` (success).
  - Settings profile image save: `app/settings/page.tsx: saveImageChange` (success).
  - Settings main save: `app/settings/page.tsx: handleSave` (success).
  - Notification toggle: `components/NotificationSettingsCard.tsx: onToggle` (medium).
  - new group button: `app/template.tsx: CreateGroupButton.onClick` (medium).
  - Share buttons: `components/GroupShareButton.tsx`, `components/PollShareButton.tsx` (both light ŌĆö share is borderline-significant; light keeps it from feeling like a vote).
  - Long-press ŌåÆ modal open: `app/g/[groupShortId]/GroupCardItem.tsx` (medium ŌĆö migrated from `navigator.vibrate(50)`).
  - Long-press ŌåÆ enter group selection mode: `components/GroupList.tsx: enterSelectionWithGroup` (medium ŌĆö migrated from `navigator.vibrate(50)`).
- **Deliberately NOT instrumented** (below the "above form-field filling out" threshold the user set when this shipped): theme switcher (preference change, no commit semantics), category bubble taps (opens the create modal ŌĆö opening a modal is navigation, not commit), every text input / dropdown / slider in the create-poll modal (filling in fields), the back-arrow on group / info / edit-title (nav). If a future request asks "why doesn't X tap give haptic feedback?" check this list first ŌĆö most omissions are intentional.
- **No new iOS build needed when changing haptic call sites.** `@capacitor/haptics` was already in `package.json` and so was already bundled in every TestFlight build going back to before this PR (it just wasn't called). The native plugin lives in the IPA; the web bundle decides whether to call it. So a new haptic site lands the same way any other web change does: push ŌåÆ deploy to `latest.whoeverwants.com` (or prod release) ŌåÆ next WebView page load picks it up. No need to trigger `ios-build.yml` for haptics changes alone. (Adding a different Capacitor plugin DOES require a fresh build because the native code is per-plugin.)
- **Verifying haptics requires a physical iOS device.** Headless Chromium has no haptics engine; iOS Simulator on a Mac does NOT vibrate (Apple disabled simulator haptics deliberately). The only way to confirm a new haptic site is to install the `WhoeverWants` / `WhoeverWants Latest` TestFlight build on a real iPhone, navigate to the affected surface, and feel for the bump. Dev/canary tier hosts the web code so as soon as the branch deploys to `latest.whoeverwants.com` the existing TestFlight app picks it up ŌĆö no rebuild required.

## App Icons

The ­¤æŗ waving-hand emoji is the canonical app icon, rendered on a black rounded-rect background. Every icon file in the project is a render of the same SVG template ŌĆö keep them in sync when changing the artwork.

### Inventory

| File | Size | Used by |
|---|---|---|
| `app/icon.svg` | viewBox 100├Ś100 | Next.js metadata convention ŌĆö auto-served at `/icon` as the browser favicon. |
| `public/icon-180x180.png` | 180├Ś180 | `<link rel="apple-touch-icon">` in `app/layout.tsx` (iOS Safari "Add to Home Screen"). No SVG source ŌĆö rendered from `public/icon-512x512.svg`. |
| `public/icon-192x192.svg` + `.png` | 192├Ś192 | `<link rel="icon">` in `app/layout.tsx` + PWA manifest (`public/manifest.json`). |
| `public/icon-256x256.svg` + `.png` | 256├Ś256 | PWA manifest only. |
| `public/icon-384x384.svg` + `.png` | 384├Ś384 | PWA manifest only. |
| `public/icon-512x512.svg` + `.png` | 512├Ś512 | `<link rel="icon">` in `app/layout.tsx` + PWA manifest. Also the source for the 180├Ś180 PNG and the iOS app icon. |
| `ios/App/App/Assets.xcassets/AppIcon.appiconset/AppIcon-512@2x.png` | 1024├Ś1024 | iOS Capacitor app icon (loaded by Xcode build into the bundle). Must be **opaque RGB** ŌĆö no alpha channel ŌĆö or TestFlight rejects with `Missing required icon file`. The rounded corners on the source SVG are composited onto a white background to fill them. |

### SVG template

All five `public/icon-*.svg` files (and `app/icon.svg`) share the same body:

```svg
<rect width="100" height="100" fill="#000000" rx="15"/>
<text x="52" y="75" font-size="74" text-anchor="middle" fill="white">­¤æŗ</text>
```

Tuned so that the visible glyph (hand + motion lines) leaves ~12% gap on each side of the frame. The `x=52` (rather than 50) and `y=75` (rather than the line-box-centered ~88) compensate for Noto Color Emoji's ­¤æŗ glyph being slightly off-centered within its em-square.

### Regenerating PNGs

The PNGs are rendered via headless Chromium so they pick up Noto Color Emoji (Apt: `fonts-noto-color-emoji`) ŌĆö that font ships on both the dev droplet and in the GitHub Actions runners, so renders are reproducible. The one-shot script lives in conversation history (search for `regen-icons.mjs`); rerun it whenever the SVG template changes:

1. For each `public/icon-NxN.png` (and the iOS 1024├Ś1024), load the matching SVG into a Chromium page with viewport=N├ŚN.
2. `page.screenshot({ omitBackground: true })` for the public PNGs (preserves rounded-rect transparency).
3. For the iOS PNG, render with white page background and `omitBackground: false` so the corners outside the rounded rect are filled white (then PIL converts RGBAŌåÆRGB).
4. The `public/icon-180x180.png` is rendered from `icon-512x512.svg` at viewport 180├Ś180 (no dedicated 180-size SVG).

Don't render with `librsvg2-bin`'s `rsvg-convert` ŌĆö it doesn't support color emoji and falls back to monochrome glyphs.

## Custom Claude Commands

### /publish
Complete deployment workflow - commit, merge to main, push, and apply database migrations:

```bash
npm run publish
```

This command will:
1. Commit any uncommitted changes (with option to customize message)
2. Push current branch to origin
3. Checkout and pull latest main
4. Merge current branch into main
5. Check for and optionally apply new database migrations to production
6. Push main to origin
7. Optionally delete the feature branch

**Usage:**
- Run from any feature branch (not main)
- Automatically handles git operations with Claude co-authorship
- Tracks which migrations have been applied to production
- Provides interactive prompts for important decisions

## Development Server Access

**The development server runs as a macOS background service and should ALWAYS be running.**

The service is configured via LaunchAgent at `~/Library/LaunchAgents/com.whoeverwants.dev.plist` and:
- Starts automatically on login
- Restarts automatically if it crashes
- Logs to `dev-server.log` and `dev-server-error.log` in the project root

### Access Points
- **Local URL**: http://localhost:3000
- **Tailscale network**: Use Tailscale to access from other devices on your network

### Service Management Commands

```bash
# Check if service is running
launchctl list | grep whoeverwants

# Stop the service
launchctl unload ~/Library/LaunchAgents/com.whoeverwants.dev.plist

# Start the service
launchctl load ~/Library/LaunchAgents/com.whoeverwants.dev.plist

# Restart the service
launchctl unload ~/Library/LaunchAgents/com.whoeverwants.dev.plist && launchctl load ~/Library/LaunchAgents/com.whoeverwants.dev.plist

# View logs
tail -f dev-server.log        # Server output
tail -f dev-server-error.log  # Error logs
```

### Important Notes
- The service **always ensures port 3000 is available** before starting
- If port 3000 is busy, follow the port conflict resolution steps above
- The service runs with your user permissions (not as root)

## Troubleshooting: Development Server Issues

### Problem: Dev Server Not Rendering

#### 1. Port Conflicts
Next.js automatically switches ports when 3000 is busy. Always ensure it's running on port 3000.

```bash
# Check which port Next.js actually started on
lsof -i :3000

# If port 3000 is busy, kill the process and restart the service
kill -9 [PID]
rm -rf .next
launchctl unload ~/Library/LaunchAgents/com.whoeverwants.dev.plist && launchctl load ~/Library/LaunchAgents/com.whoeverwants.dev.plist
```

#### 2. React Hydration Errors
Hydration errors cause the app to show permanent loading spinners.

**Common Cause:** Date/time calculations in render functions
```typescript
// BAD - causes hydration mismatch
const now = new Date();
const openQuestions = questions.filter(question =>
  new Date(question.response_deadline) > now
);
```

**Fix:** Move date logic to `useEffect`
```typescript
// GOOD - avoids hydration issues
const [openQuestions, setOpenQuestions] = useState<Question[]>([]);

useEffect(() => {
  if (typeof window === 'undefined') return;
  const now = new Date();
  const open = questions.filter(question =>
    new Date(question.response_deadline) > now
  );
  setOpenQuestions(open);
}, [questions]);
```

#### 3. Missing JavaScript Build Assets
404 errors for `main-app.js`, `webpack.js` files indicate build corruption.

```bash
rm -rf .next/
npm run dev
```

#### 4. Complete Recovery Steps

1. Clear build cache: `rm -rf .next/`
2. Check for hydration errors in code (search for `new Date()` in render functions)
3. Identify actual port: `lsof -i :3000`
4. Restart dev server service: `launchctl unload ~/Library/LaunchAgents/com.whoeverwants.dev.plist && launchctl load ~/Library/LaunchAgents/com.whoeverwants.dev.plist`
5. Verify URL works: `curl -s -I http://localhost:3000 | head -3`

#### 5. Debug Browser Console
```bash
node scripts/debug-console.cjs
```

**Success Indicators:**
- No hydration warnings in browser console
- "Loading spinner present: false"
- API calls successfully loading data
- Local URL returns HTTP 200

---

## Database Migrations

SQL migration files live in `database/migrations/` (001-064, up + down). All 64 migrations are applied on the production droplet. New migrations are applied manually via `psql` on the droplet:

```bash
# Apply a new migration on the droplet
bash scripts/remote.sh "docker exec -i whoeverwants-db-1 psql -U whoeverwants whoeverwants < /root/whoeverwants/database/migrations/065_description_up.sql" /root/whoeverwants

# Verify migration applied ŌĆö query by FILENAME, not by `_migrations.id`
bash scripts/remote.sh "docker exec whoeverwants-db-1 psql -U whoeverwants -c \"SELECT id, filename FROM _migrations WHERE filename LIKE '065_%'\""
```

- **`_migrations.id` is a serial row counter, not the migration number.** `SELECT id FROM _migrations` returns sequence values like `1, 2, ..., 104` that have nothing to do with the `NNN_` prefix on the filename. Querying for "is migration 092 applied?" by `WHERE id = 92` is wrong (and will silently mislead ŌĆö there *is* always an `id=92` once enough migrations have run). Always check `filename LIKE 'NNN_%'`. The only correct use of `_migrations.id` is `ORDER BY id DESC` to see recently-applied filenames.

- **Historical migrations (091, 099ŌĆō105) reference the legacy `threads` / `thread_members` / `polls.thread_id` schema names.** Migration 107 renamed them to `groups` / `group_members` / `polls.group_id`. The historical files are NOT rewritten ŌĆö their SQL talks about the old names because that's what was on disk at the time. When reading those migrations to understand schema history, mentally substitute `groups` for `threads` etc. CLAUDE.md and `docs/*.md` use the current names throughout.

### Writing New Migrations

1. **Use additive changes**: Add columns with DEFAULT values or allow NULL
2. **Avoid destructive changes**: Don't DROP columns or tables with data
3. **Handle existing data**: Provide migration logic for existing rows

---

## Database Constraint Debugging

### When "Failed to submit vote" Errors Occur

**ALWAYS add comprehensive logging FIRST before attempting fixes:**

1. **Add server-side logging immediately** to capture exact database errors
2. **Check API logs**: `bash scripts/remote.sh "docker compose logs --tail 100" /root/whoeverwants`
3. **Look for constraint violations** - they often "stack" (fixing one reveals another)

### Common Constraint Issues (in order of likelihood):
1. `votes_vote_type_check` - Missing vote type in allowed types
2. `vote_yes_no_valid` - Outdated constraint blocking new vote types
3. `vote_structure_valid` - Structure validation for vote types

### Key Lesson:
**PostgreSQL only reports the FIRST failing constraint.** After fixing one constraint, ALWAYS test again immediately - another constraint may be blocking. The suggestion voting fix required fixing TWO separate constraints that were hiding behind each other.

### Quick Debug Commands:
```bash
# Check API logs on droplet
bash scripts/remote.sh "docker compose logs --tail 100" /root/whoeverwants

# List all check constraints on a table
bash scripts/remote.sh "docker exec whoeverwants-db-1 psql -U whoeverwants -c \"SELECT conname, pg_get_constraintdef(oid) FROM pg_constraint WHERE conrelid = 'votes'::regclass AND contype = 'c';\""
```

**Time-saving tip**: Don't guess at the problem. Add logging, get the exact error, then fix the specific constraint.

### Migration Constraint Naming

- **Use consistent constraint names across migrations.** If migration 043 creates `vote_type_check` and migration 048 drops/recreates `votes_vote_type_check` (different name!), both constraints coexist. New migrations that only update one name leave the other stale. Always `DROP CONSTRAINT IF EXISTS` for ALL known aliases before creating the updated constraint.
- **When adding new enum values to CHECK constraints**, search all migrations for every constraint on that column (names may vary) and drop all of them before adding the new one. Use `SELECT conname FROM pg_constraint WHERE conrelid = 'table'::regclass` to audit.

### Suggestion / Availability Deadline (starts at creation)

> **Migration 118 removed the "deferred until first submission" behavior.** The prephase (suggestion / availability) countdown now starts at poll creation. There is no open-ended "waiting for the first response" phase, and empty cutoffs (deadline passes with zero submissions) are accepted ŌĆö that's the trade-off the user chose for predictable, immediately-ticking timers. The history below describes the retired design; the bullets describe current behavior.

- **The prephase deadline is armed at creation, never on first submission.** `_insert_poll` (`server/routers/polls.py`) resolves a preset `prephase_deadline_minutes` to an absolute `polls.prephase_deadline = now + minutes` at create time, capped to `response_deadline - 1 minute` when a voting deadline exists. A custom absolute `prephase_deadline` passes through unchanged. `prephase_deadline_minutes` is still stored (it's the per-question "this is a suggestion-mode question" signal the FE reads via `question.suggestion_deadline_minutes`) but it's no longer used to defer the deadline.
- **No per-vote arming.** `_submit_vote_to_question` does NOT touch `prephase_deadline` ŌĆö the old `has_deferred_deadline` block (set the deadline on the first suggestion / availability submission) is gone. `_enforce_suggestion_phase_timing` keys solely on `prephase_deadline` (`has_suggestion_phase = suggestion_deadline is not None`); the `suggestion_deadline_minutes`-without-a-deadline branch was removed.
- **`hasSuggestionPhase` / `isInSuggestionPhase` key on the deadline only.** `lib/questionListUtils.ts: isInSuggestionPhase(question, prephaseDeadline)` returns true iff the question is `ranked_choice` AND `prephaseDeadline` is set AND in the future. The retired "`minutes` set but `deadline` null ŌåÆ in phase forever" branch is gone. In `QuestionBallot`, `inSuggestionPhase` is `hasSuggestionPhase && !!effectiveSuggestionDeadline && now < deadline`. `suggestionDeadlineOverride` survives ONLY for the creator-cutoff path (`apiCutoffPollSuggestions` sets it to the now-past wrapper deadline so the UI exits the phase immediately) ŌĆö it's no longer used for optimistic first-submission timer starts.
- **No "pending" prephase UI.** `DeadlineKind` dropped `'prephase-pending'` (the blue dot for "configured but timer not started") in `lib/groupUtils.ts` + `components/GroupListItem.tsx: PENDING_DOT`. The static "Taking Suggestions" / "Collecting Availability" no-countdown labels in `GroupCardItem` and the poll detail page were removed ŌĆö there's always a `prephase_deadline`, so the `<SimpleCountdown>` branch always wins. (The time-availability `"Collecting Availability"` static fallback is kept as a defensive branch for a hypothetical time poll created with no prephase cutoff.) `response-pending` (green dot for "unvoted work, no deadline anywhere") is unrelated and stays.
- **In-flight backfill.** Migration 118 arms any poll left in the old deferred state (`prephase_deadline IS NULL AND prephase_deadline_minutes IS NOT NULL`) with `created_at + minutes` (capped below the voting deadline). The down migration is a no-op ŌĆö the deferred state can't be distinguished from a legitimately-armed deadline after the fact.
- **The optimistic placeholder carries the prephase deadline.** `synthesizePlaceholderPoll` takes a `prephaseDeadline` arg; `app/create-poll/page.tsx` computes it (`prephaseDeadlineIso ?? now + minutes`) so the optimistic card shows the countdown immediately instead of flashing a blank slot until `POLL_HYDRATED`.
- **The group page's `QUESTION_VOTES_CHANGED_EVENT` patcher still carries `prephase_deadline`** through `patchGroupPolls` ŌĆö not because votes arm it (they don't anymore), but so a concurrent creator suggestions/availability cutoff is reflected without a manual refresh.
- **`hasCompletedRanking`** (computed in QuestionBallot) distinguishes "voted with suggestions only" from "voted with rankings". Used to gate preliminary results display and the ranking summary view ŌĆö prevents showing results before the user has ranked.
- **`is_abstain` vs `is_ranking_abstain`**: The `votes` table has two abstain columns. `is_abstain` means "fully abstained" (no suggestions, no rankings) or, in non-suggestion questions, "abstained from voting." `is_ranking_abstain` means "abstained from ranking specifically but has suggestions." In suggestion-phase questions, `is_abstain=true` does NOT mean ranking abstain ŌĆö don't restore `isAbstaining` state or show "Ranking: Abstained" based on `is_abstain` during the suggestion phase. Use `userAbstainedFromRanking` (computed in QuestionBallot) for display checks.
- **Auto-finalization in `get_question`**: When `suggestion_deadline` has passed but `options` is still NULL, the endpoint auto-calls `_finalize_suggestion_options()`. This handles the case where the deadline expires naturally without a manual cutoff.
- **Manual cutoff requires suggestions**: The `cutoff-suggestions` endpoint rejects requests (400) when no suggestions have been submitted, enforced via an EXISTS subquery in the UPDATE.
- **Explain decision OUTCOMES in plain language; fix the empty-brainstorm dead-end.** (Decision from the social-test review, May 2026.) Surface *meaning*, not just *mechanics*. **Actionable parts (a) + (b)-Layer-1 + (b)-Layer-2 are all SHIPPED** (see "Outcome legibility" + "Ranked-choice headline method" bullets below).
  - **(a) Empty-brainstorm cold start ŌĆö SHIPPED.** A suggestion poll with zero suggestions was a dead-end: `cutoff-suggestions` correctly 400s (can't rank nothing), and a prephase deadline reached with zero suggestions auto-finalizes to an empty ballot. Shipped: (1) a blue-text empty-state nudge ("No suggestions yet. Add the first idea below!") in `SuggestionVotingInterface` while the phase is open and `existingSuggestions.length === 0`; (2) an explicit "No suggestions were added, so there was nothing to decide." terminal outcome on the closed-poll results view instead of the misleading "No Voters". (A create-form hint *encouraging* creators to pre-seed `initial_suggestions` was considered and **explicitly declined by the owner (June 2026)** ŌĆö the capability already exists via the Initial Suggestions card, and an extra nudge wasn't wanted. Do NOT re-propose it.)
  - **(b) IRV result is opaque, and may be the wrong method for social groups.** Pure Instant-Runoff (Borda only as tiebreak, then alphabetical) eliminates the option with the FEWEST first-place votes each round ŌĆö so a broadly-liked compromise (everyone's #2, few #1s) is eliminated EARLY and a polarizing plurality wins (documented in `social_tests/tests/test_ranked_preferences.py::test_condorcet_scenario`). For a friend group picking a restaurant, that's often just wrong ŌĆö they usually want "the thing nobody hates," exactly what IRV throws out first. Two layers:
    - **Layer 1 (explain the result) ŌĆö SHIPPED.** See the "Outcome legibility" bullet below ŌĆö every closed poll's result carries a one-line plain-language explanation, surfaced **behind a grey info (Ōōś) icon placed inline right after the result label** ("Final Results" / "Final Round" / "Scheduled Time") ŌĆö owner: "only behind info icon ŌĆ” always grey ŌĆ” inline after the result label", June 2026; never inline prose. For ranked-choice the broadly-acceptable-eliminated-early case is detected via full Borda scores (the gloss text says so; the icon is still grey).
    - **Layer 2 (reconsider the headline aggregation) ŌĆö SHIPPED (migration 135) as a per-poll create-time choice.** The owner reviewed a read-only comparison prototype (`prototypes/aggregation/` ŌĆö runs the documented social-test scenarios through IRV vs Borda vs Condorcet; 4 of 6 agree, the 2 that diverge are the friend-group restaurant/movie cases where Borda AND Condorcet both pick the compromise IRV throws out) and chose the **per-poll "favorite vs consensus" framing** (NOT a silent default change, NOT Borda-vs-Condorcet ŌĆö they agreed in every divergent scenario, so "consensus" is unambiguous). See the "Ranked-choice headline method" bullet below for the implementation.
- **Ranked-choice headline method (favorite vs consensus) ŌĆö SHIPPED (migration 135).** A ranked_choice question carries `questions.winner_method TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'favorite'` (the SQL column default stays `'favorite'` so existing rows + raw-API callers are unchanged; the FE create-form default is `'consensus'`). `'favorite'` = Instant-Runoff. `'consensus'` = Borda (broadest acceptance). **Same ballots either way ŌĆö only which winner becomes the headline differs.** The creator picks at create time via a one-row **"Scoring Algorithm"** dropdown.
  - **Server.** `algorithms/ranked_choice.consensus_winner_from_borda(borda_scores, options)` derives the Borda winner from the already-computed `borda_scores` (no second ballot scan; alphabetical tiebreak mirroring IRV). `_compute_results` (services/questions.py) sets `winner` (the headline) to `consensus_winner` when `winner_method == 'consensus'`, else the IRV winner; it ALWAYS returns `ranked_choice_winner` (the favorite) AND `consensus_winner` so the FE can show "the other lens would've picked Y". `winner_method` threads through `CreateQuestionRequest` ŌåÆ `_insert_poll` ŌåÆ `_row_to_question`/`QuestionResponse` and `QuestionResultsResponse`; validated by `services.validation.validate_winner_method` (only 'favorite'|'consensus'; stored only for ranked_choice, else 'favorite'). Rides every read path because question SELECTs are `SELECT *`/`p.*`. Borda is used (not Condorcet): it's already computed, always produces a clear explainable ranking, and agreed with Condorcet in every divergent prototype scenario.
  - **FE display.** `CompactRankedChoiceResults` early-returns a **`ConsensusResults`** breadth-breakdown (options sorted by Borda score with bars, winner highlighted, "the most first-choice picks went to {favorite}" footnote) when `winner_method === 'consensus'` AND `borda_scores` has entries ŌĆö because the IRV rounds would crown the FAVORITE, contradicting the consensus headline. The compact group-card pill (`CompactRankedChoicePreview`) reads `results.winner` (the headline) so it's correct for free. `rankedChoiceResultGloss` (the grey Ōōś gloss) branches on consensus mode: it explains the method ("ranked highest across the most ballots") instead of the favorite-mode "a compromise lost" warning. Fields wired through `lib/types.ts` (`QuestionResults.consensus_winner` + `winner_method`; `Question.winner_method`) + `toQuestionResults`/`toQuestion` + `groupRefresh` equality.
  - **Create form.** `QuestionDraft.winnerMethod` (default `'consensus'`, NOT remembered per-user ŌĆö the creator opts per-poll) ŌåÆ `draftToQuestionParams` (ranked_choice only) ŌåÆ `CreateQuestionParams.winner_method`. The control is `components/ScoringAlgorithmField.tsx` ŌĆö a one-row `h-12` field (label "Scoring Algorithm" left, the selected method's name right in the standard value font, invisible native `<select>` overlay, same bespoke pattern as `VotingCutoffField`; NOT yet extracted into a shared primitive ŌĆö two inline instances is the codebase's "inline until the abstraction threshold" convention). It lives in the BOTTOM settings card just before "Minimum Votes" (`CompactMinResponsesField`), both gated on `pollHasRankedChoice`. The collapsed value shows only the method name ("Consensus" / "Favorite"); the dropdown options append the algorithm in parens ("Consensus (Borda Score)" / "Favorite (Ranked Choice)"). Wired through persistence (`questionFormState`), the duplicate flow (preserves the source's method via `buildQuestionSnapshot.winner_method`), the vote-from-suggestion flow (resets to the `'consensus'` default), and `synthesizePlaceholderPoll`.
  - **Prototype + demo:** `prototypes/aggregation/` (the read-only IRV-vs-Borda-vs-Condorcet comparison the owner reviewed + `seed_demo.py` which seeds a live favorite/consensus pair with identical ballots). Tests: `server/tests/test_ranked_choice.py::TestConsensusWinner`, `tests/__tests__/ranked-choice/result-gloss.test.ts` (consensus cases). **Demo caveat:** a closed poll is hidden from a fresh viewer (closed-before-join), so screenshot the consensus result via a sign-in link to the creator account, or use an open poll the viewer voted on.
- **Outcome legibility ŌĆö ranked-choice result gloss + empty-suggestion terminal state (shipped).** Implements the actionable parts of the outcomes TODO above.
  - **`borda_scores: dict[str, int] | None` on every ranked-choice result.** The IRV algorithm already computed Borda only for tied last-place candidates; `calculate_ranked_choice_winner` now ALSO computes a full Borda over every option in one pass (`full_borda = _calculate_borda_scores(ballots, options, total_candidates)`) and returns it on `RankedChoiceResult.borda_scores`. `_compute_results` surfaces it as `QuestionResultsResponse.borda_scores` (None for non-ranked-choice / no ranking votes); `toQuestionResults` maps it to `QuestionResults.borda_scores`. Borda rewards breadth (ranked high on many ballots), so it's the signal for "broadly acceptable." This is the data foundation Layer 2 would also build on ŌĆö don't remove it if Layer 1's gloss is ever reworked.
  - **`lib/outcomeExplainer.ts: outcomeExplainer(results)`** is the single pure, unit-tested entry point for the plain-language outcome one-liner across ALL decision types (returns `string | null` ŌĆö no tone, since the icon is always grey). It switches on `question_type`: **yes_no** ŌåÆ "Yes won, 4 to 2." / tie / all-abstain / null on no-votes; **time** ŌåÆ "ŌĆ╣slotŌĆ║ works best ŌĆö N of M can make it, and ŌĆ”" / null when the event was cancelled (the "event's off" banner is self-explanatory) or there's no winner; **ranked_choice** ŌåÆ delegates to `rankedChoiceResultGloss` (below) and returns its `.text`, with a single-round-majority fallback so a decided IRV result always has a sentence; **limited_supply / other** ŌåÆ null (first-come, no "why this won"). Gated on `isQuestionClosed` at every call site (describes the final outcome, never an in-progress tally).
  - **`components/OutcomeInfoButton.tsx`** is the shared grey Ōōś affordance that sits **inline right after a result label** and reveals the explanation in a tap-to-toggle popover (click-outside / Escape to close, `stopPropagation` so the tap doesn't bubble to the result card's round-swipe / tap-to-detail handlers). `align` (`left`/`right`/`center`, default `center`) anchors the popover. **The popover is a block-display `<span>` (not a `<div>`)** so the whole subtree stays valid phrasing content when the button is nested inside the `<p>`/`<h3>` result label ŌĆö a `<div>` there trips the "`<div>` cannot be a descendant of `<p>`" hydration warning. **The explanation is ONLY ever behind this icon ŌĆö never rendered inline** (owner constraint). Wired inline after the label in: `CompactRankedChoiceResults` (after the final-round title, gated on `currentRoundIndex === last`; a single-round majority gets a "Final Results" label to anchor it), `QuestionResults.tsx: YesNoResults` (a new "Final Results" label, since yes/no had no heading ŌĆö non-compact `!hideLoser` branch; compact group-card pills are untouched), and `TimeResults` (after "Scheduled Time"). Tests: `tests/__tests__/outcome-explainer.test.ts`.
  - **`lib/rankedChoiceGloss.ts: rankedChoiceResultGloss(results)`** is the ranked-choice-specific gloss generator that `outcomeExplainer` delegates to (returns `{tone:'warn'|'info', text} | null`). `warn` fires when an *eliminated* option has a STRICTLY higher Borda score than the winner (the strongest such is named) ŌĆö "ŌĆ╣XŌĆ║ was ranked on more ballots than ŌĆ╣winnerŌĆ║ but had fewer first-choice picksŌĆ”". Else, for a Ōēź2-round result, a neutral `info` gloss explains how IRV reached the winner. Single-round majorities and ties/no-winner return null (the single-round case gets a majority one-liner from `outcomeExplainer`). Strictly-greater (not Ōēź) avoids flagging an equal-breadth option. Tests: `tests/__tests__/ranked-choice/result-gloss.test.ts` (FE) + `server/tests/test_ranked_choice.py::TestFullBordaScores` (algorithm).
  - **Empty-suggestion terminal outcome.** A suggestion poll always carries a (possibly empty) `suggestion_counts` array; a fixed-option ranked-choice poll has it `undefined`. So in `CompactRankedChoiceResults`'s empty-rounds branch, `isQuestionClosed && Array.isArray(suggestion_counts) && length === 0 && !options?.length` uniquely identifies "expired with nothing to rank" ŌåÆ renders the explicit terminal message instead of "No Voters". Don't confuse with "suggestions existed but all voters abstained from ranking" (options IS populated there ŌåÆ falls through to "All voters abstained").
- **New options detection uses localStorage**: `storeSeenQuestionOptions(questionId, options)` in `browserQuestionAccess.ts` stores the option set at vote time. On next load, `getSeenQuestionOptions` retrieves it and `newOptions` useMemo computes the diff. Excludes the user's own suggestions (they already know about those) and only fires for users who have already ranked. Cross-device limitation: no baseline on a new device, so no banner ŌĆö acceptable given the app's localStorage-first model.
- **`ClientOnly` wrapper breaks flex row layout** even with `fallback={null}`. `ClientOnly` renders a block-level `<div>` during SSR/initial render which disrupts flex containers. For content guarded by React state that starts empty and populates in `useEffect` (like `questionsWithNewOptions`), skip `ClientOnly` entirely ŌĆö the empty initial state IS the SSR-safe behavior. Only use `ClientOnly` for content that would cause a hydration mismatch if rendered during SSR.

### "Collect Suggestions before Vote" toggle (explicit suggestion-poll mode)

Suggestion mode used to be IMPLICIT: a ranked_choice question with zero options. It's now an EXPLICIT per-question toggle in the create-poll form's top card, under the Context field (`category !== 'yes_no' && category !== 'time'`). Default ON; the last submitted value is remembered per-user (`getUserCollectSuggestions` / `saveUserCollectSuggestions` in `lib/userProfile.ts`, localStorage `whoeverwants_collect_suggestions`, cleared on sign-out alongside the other poll-form prefs).

- **`QuestionDraft.collectSuggestions`** drives everything. `draftIsSuggestionMode(d)` now returns `ranked_choice && d.collectSuggestions` (NOT "zero options" anymore) and is the single source of truth ŌĆö `draftToQuestionParams`, `synthesizePlaceholderPoll`, `anyDraftHasSuggestion`, etc. all route through it. Don't re-derive `ranked_choice && collectSuggestions` inline; call the helper so the API payload and the optimistic placeholder can't diverge (the morph-on-hydration bug the placeholder comments warn about).
- **ON** ŌåÆ options card re-heads to "Initial Suggestions"; `draftToQuestionParams` leaves `options` unset, sets `suggestion_deadline_minutes`, and (when the creator typed options) passes them as `initial_suggestions`. **OFF** ŌåÆ fixed-options poll; `validateRankedChoiceOptions(options, category, collectSuggestions)` requires Ōēź2 distinct options (the old "(leave blank to ask for suggestions)" hint is gone). The `collectSuggestions` param defaults `true` so any other caller keeps suggestion-allowed behavior.
- **Suggestion-poll titles ignore typed options** ŌĆö both `generateTitle` (page.tsx) and `deriveDraftTitle` (helpers) treat `filled = collectSuggestions ? [] : <options>`, so the title is category-based ("Restaurant for Dinner") not "A or B?". Matches the server (which never titles ranked_choice from options).
- **Server: `CreateQuestionRequest.initial_suggestions`** ŌåÆ `create_poll` submits them as the creator's own suggestion-phase vote (`is_ranking_abstain=True`, `voter_name=creator_name`, `browser_id=creator_browser_id`) inside the SAME create transaction. **Gated on an ACTIVE (future) prephase deadline** (`prephase_deadline > now`), NOT merely non-null: a very short voting window caps `prephase_deadline` to `response_deadline - 1min`, which can land in the past ŌĆö seeding then would raise `_submit_vote_to_question`'s "Suggestions cutoff has passed" 400 and roll back the whole create. The gate skips seeding so the create stays atomic AND resilient. (It is NOT best-effort/try-except ŌĆö the gate is what makes the realistic failure path unreachable.)
- **`PollResponse.initial_suggestion_vote_ids` (question_id ŌåÆ vote_id)** rides back on the create response ONLY; `apiCreatePoll` writes `setStoredVoteId` + `setVotedQuestionFlag` so the creating browser OWNS its server-submitted vote. Without this the creator's browser (which never went through the FE vote path) treats them as not-voted: their seeds render as unowned/secondable and a later edit spawns a duplicate vote row.
- **`create_poll` computes the voter roster when (and only when) a seed vote was submitted** ŌĆö a plain create still skips aggregation (`_row_to_poll`'s empty defaults). Without this the create response reports "Viewed (0) / No voters yet" until the first refresh even though the creator just suggested.
- **Pitfall (regression caught in review): the duplicate + vote-from-suggestion flows must set `collectSuggestions` explicitly.** Both load concrete `options` into the form; if `collectSuggestions` is left at the remembered default (often true), `draftToQuestionParams` would convert those concrete options into `initial_suggestions` and re-open a suggestion phase instead of a fixed ballot. The duplicate handler sets it from options-presence (`!dupHasOptions` ŌĆö preserves the pre-toggle "options present = fixed" rule); the vote-from-suggestion handler hard-sets `false` (it always turns a finalized round into a fixed ranking ballot). Any NEW flow that prefills `options` must set `collectSuggestions` too.

### "Ask for Availability before Voting" toggle (time polls)

The time-question analog of the suggestion toggle. A per-question toggle in the create-poll form's top card, under the Context field (gated on `category === 'time'`). Default ON; remembered per-user (`getUserCollectAvailability` / `saveUserCollectAvailability` in `lib/userProfile.ts`, localStorage `whoeverwants_collect_availability`, cleared on sign-out with the other poll-form prefs). ON keeps the existing two-phase availability ŌåÆ preferences flow; OFF skips the availability phase entirely and the poll opens straight into the preference (like/dislike) ballot over the slots derived from the creator's time windows.

- **`QuestionDraft.collectAvailability`** drives it. `draftUsesAvailabilityPhase(d)` = `time && d.collectAvailability` is the single source of truth; `anyDraftUsesAvailabilityPhase` (which replaced `anyDraftIsTime` in page.tsx) and `anyDraftUsesPrephase` route through it so a time question with availability OFF does NOT contribute the poll-level prephase cutoff. Don't re-derive `time && collectAvailability` inline.
- **The FEŌåÆserver signal is the ABSENCE of `suggestion_deadline_minutes`, NOT a new request field** ŌĆö symmetric with how a fixed-options ranked_choice (no suggestion phase) is "options set + no suggestion_deadline". `draftToQuestionParams` sets `suggestion_deadline_minutes` for a time question ONLY when `collectAvailability` is on. `min_availability_percent` + `day_time_windows` + `duration_window` are always sent regardless.
- **Server finalizes slots at create when OFF.** `create_poll` (`server/routers/polls.py`), right after inserting questions, calls `_finalize_time_slots(conn, qid, now)` for every time question whose `suggestion_deadline_minutes is None`, then re-fetches the row so the computed `options` ride back on the create response. With zero votes the min-availability filter is a no-op and `_keep_longest_per_start_time` dedups ŌĆö identical to the cutoff-time finalization. A time question with empty `day_time_windows` derives no slots (finalize is a no-op ŌåÆ `options` stays NULL), so the degenerate "time question, no windows" create is unchanged.
- **No voting-side FE changes were needed.** `isInTimeAvailabilityPhase(question)` (and `QuestionBallot`'s `inAvailabilityPhase`) is purely `!question.options` ŌĆö so once `options` is set the FE treats it as a preference poll automatically. A voter who never submitted availability sees every finalized slot (`preferenceSlotsForVoter` returns all options when `voter_day_time_windows` is empty). `TimeSlotBubbles` already gates its availability badges/legend on `maxAvailability > 0`, so the no-availability-data case renders clean.
- **Results "X of Y available" line is gated on `maxAvail > 0`** (`QuestionResults.tsx: TimeResults`) so a toggle-OFF poll (zero availability data ŌåÆ `max_availability = 0`) doesn't render a meaningless "0 of 0 available".
- **`Minimum Availability` field is hidden when the toggle is OFF** ŌĆö it filters slots by collected availability, which doesn't exist without an availability phase.
- **Duplicate flow copies the creator's NOT-in-the-past time windows + duration, then hard-sets `collectAvailability = true`.** `buildQuestionSnapshot` (`lib/questionCreator.ts`) now captures `day_time_windows` + `duration_window` (both null for non-time questions). The `time` branch of the `?duplicate=` handler in `app/create-poll/page.tsx` filters the copied windows to `day >= formatLocalDateISO(today)` (a poll copied weeks later would otherwise seed dead dates the calendar can't even select ŌĆö past dates render disabled in `DaysSelector`) and applies `duration_window` to the four `durationMin/Max{Value,Enabled}` states. When EVERY day is in the past the filter empties ŌåÆ it falls back to seeding today (a single `DEFAULT_TIME_WINDOW`) so the form isn't left with an empty calendar, matching the non-duplicate init. `collectAvailability` is still forced ON (re-open the two-phase flow); the snapshot doesn't carry the original's availability-toggle state, and ON is the safe default now that the copied windows give it real slots to derive from. The filter is a copy-time transform (a property of "copy this poll", not of the form), so it lives inline in the handler rather than deferring to `DaysSelector.removePastDates` ŌĆö the time-windows list renders rows from `dayTimeWindows` directly and would briefly flash past rows otherwise. The surviving entries are used directly (no defensive copy) since `duplicateData` is freshly `JSON.parse`d local data. (Mirrors the `collectSuggestions` duplicate-flow caution for the options field.)
- Tests: `server/tests/test_time_availability_toggle.py`.

### Plus-Ones (vote on behalf of others) ŌĆö migration 133

One person can submit a single ballot that counts for additional people ("I'm answering for my partner too"). Poll-level toggle, shared-ballot-weighted.

- **`polls.allow_plus_ones BOOLEAN` (migration 133)** ŌĆö poll-level. Default resolved at create in `_insert_poll`: ON when the poll has any `time` question, OFF otherwise; `CreatePollRequest.allow_plus_ones` (bool|None) is the FE override (None ŌåÆ server default). Surfaced on `PollResponse.allow_plus_ones` (and `Poll.allow_plus_ones`, via `toPoll`). The create-poll bottom settings card has a "Allow voting for others (plus-ones)" `SliderSwitch`; FE state `allowPlusOnes: boolean | null` (null = follow `effectiveAllowPlusOnes = allowPlusOnes ?? pollHasTimeQuestion`), persisted in `questionFormState`, reset to null in `discardAndClose`.
- **`votes.plus_one_names JSONB` (migration 133)** ŌĆö array with one entry per represented person ("" = unnamed plus-one). The vote weighs `1 + len(plus_one_names)`. **Poll-level on the wire** (`SubmitPollVotesRequest.plus_one_names`): the batch endpoint writes the SAME value onto every sibling question's row. `_sanitize_plus_one_names` (routers/polls.py) trims + bounds (Ōēż50 people, Ōēż50 chars each, blanks kept) and is CLAMPED to None when `allow_plus_ones` is off ŌĆö a crafted request can't inflate a poll that opted out. Edit path direct-assigns `plus_one_names` (not COALESCE), same as `voter_day_time_windows`, so the FE must always re-send the current list (it does).
- **Weighting is a single helper: `algorithms/weights.py: vote_weight(vote)`** = `1 + len(vote["plus_one_names"] or [])`. Applied in `yes_no.py` (counts), `ranked_choice.py` (each ballot appended `weight` times ŌåÆ IRV tally + majority + Borda all weight), `time_question.py` (`compute_slot_availability` headcount ŌåÆ drives the `min_participants` viability gate, AND like/dislike counts). `_finalize_time_slots`'s vote SELECT was widened to include `plus_one_names` so the cutoff gate is weighted too. Suggestion counts are intentionally NOT weighted (a suggestion is "this option was proposed", binary). Votes feed the algorithms via `SELECT *`, so the column flows automatically.
- **Roster integration (`_compute_poll_voter_data`):** named plus-ones fold into `voter_names` + `voter_name_counts` (deduped per submitter `browser_id` via `DISTINCT ON` ŌĆö each sibling row repeats the array, so unnesting all rows would multiply by question count; the count is per-occurrence so two plus-ones named "Sam" ŌåÆ ├Ś2 ŌåÆ two bubbles via the existing FE expansion). Unnamed plus-ones add to `anonymous_count`. `viewed_total` is bumped by the total plus-one headcount so "voted Ōēż viewed" (the group-card turnout line) stays consistent. The submitter's own vote row is unchanged (plus-ones are NOT separate rows ŌĆö no double-count).
- **Two kinds of plus-one (hybrid model):** a **freeform/unnamed** entry is weighted on the submitter's row (`plus_one_names`, can't be edited later); a **looked-up account** (picked from the contact dropdown ŌåÆ carries `userId`) gets its OWN **seeded, editable vote** attributed to that account so they can change it later. `SubmitPollVotesRequest.plus_one_user_ids` carries the looked-up accounts; `_seed_plus_one_votes` (routers/polls.py) creates one vote per question for each, mirroring the submitter's choice, attributed via the account's earliest browser, voter_name = their `display_name`. **It does NOT auto-add them to the group** ŌĆö instead it mints a single-use **invite** (Phase G `issue_invite`, `target_poll_id` = the poll) and returns a per-account notification spec; `submit_poll_votes` fans those out as pushes (via the generic `fan_out_to_user`, which targets one user's browsers) after the response. The seeded vote counts in the tally immediately even though they're not a member yet; tapping the invite (`/invite/<token>`) lets them join + land on the poll, where the detail page's discovery pass adopts the seeded vote for editing. **Guards:** only the submitter's contacts (`is_contact`), skip self, skip accounts that **already responded** (`user_responded_to_poll` ŌĆö never overwrite their own vote), each seeded once. Anonymous submitters (no account) can't seed (no contacts). Seeded votes weigh 1 (no plus-ones of their own).
- **Candidate lookup: `GET /api/polls/{id}/plus-one-candidates`** ŌåÆ `[{user_id, name, responded}]` (`list_plus_one_candidates` in contacts.py). The caller's contacts (address book; does NOT exclude group members, unlike `list_invitable_accounts` ŌĆö you can vote for a member who hasn't responded), each flagged `responded` (has a vote on this poll via any of their browsers). Reconciles contacts inline. Returns `[]` when the poll doesn't allow plus-ones or the caller has no account. The FE dropdown greys out `responded` candidates with "(responded)" and blocks selection.
- **Seeded-vote recognition (so the represented account can change it later):** the poll detail page runs a one-shot **discovery pass** on mount (gated on `poll.allow_plus_ones`): for each question with no local stored vote id, `apiGetVotes(qid)` (ballot-privacy-scoped to the caller's own rows, so any returned vote IS theirs) ŌåÆ if present, adopt it (`setStoredVoteId` + `setVotedQuestionFlag` + update voted sets + yes/no `userVoteMap`) and dispatch `QUESTION_VOTES_CHANGED_EVENT`. `QuestionBallot` listens for that event and flips `hasVoted` true (so its load-vote effect runs) ŌĆö this is how a seeded account, opening the poll signed-in, sees + edits its vote instead of double-voting. Cross-device caveat: recognition needs the account's browser linked (signed in), since seeded votes attribute to the account's browser.
- **Voting UI: `components/PlusOnesInput.tsx`** ŌĆö rendered on the poll detail page (`PollDetailPage`) when `poll.allow_plus_ones && !isClosed`. Reuses the options-field-card row visual (input + red ├Ś per row) with an explicit **"+ Add a person"** button (blank row = unnamed plus-one). Entries are `{name, userId?}` (`PlusOneEntry`); picking a contact from the dropdown attaches `userId` (ŌåÆ seeded vote), typing freeform keeps it weighted. `useGroupVoting` reads them via a ref-stable `getPlusOnes()` getter ŌåÆ `{names, userIds}` threaded into every `apiSubmitPollVotes` call. Prefill on mount fills the freeform list from the viewer's own vote's `plus_one_names`. The explanatory message ("Your response will be duplicatedŌĆ” If they already have the app, look them up below and they can change their response later.") shows **only once Ōēź1 person is added**; no divider above the section.
- **Submit button shows "for X"** when plus-ones are added: X = 1 (you) + entries. **A single yes/no poll keeps tap-to-submit UNLESS plus-ones are added** ŌĆö `usePollSubmit = isMultiPoll || (allYesNo && allow_plus_ones && plusOnes.length > 0)`, so tapping Yes/No auto-submits when no one's been added, and switches to the staged explicit-Submit flow (button "Submit Vote for X") once Ōēź1 person is added. Multi-question polls always use the staged flow.
- Tests: `server/tests/test_plus_ones.py` (default ON/OFF by type + override, yes/no + unnamed weighting, disallowed-poll clamp, named/duplicate/unnamed roster, edit updates count, **seeded editable vote + responded-flag + edit-by-represented-account, can't-seed-non-contact, skip-already-responded, invite-not-membership**).
- **Known limitations / verification notes (NOT open work ŌĆö these are inherent, kept as the record):**
  - **Notification delivery is untestable in CI** (needs a real push subscription) ŌĆö only recipient-selection + invite minting are covered. This is inherent to push, not a deferred task; verify deliveries on a real device/TestFlight when touching the fan-out.
  - **Cross-device editing requires the represented person be signed in** on the device where they open the invite (the seeded vote attributes to their account's browser; the detail-page discovery pass finds it via the account-scoped `/votes`). Anonymous-on-a-fresh-device can't reach it ŌĆö by design, not a bug.
  - **The per-user push for the plus-one invite uses the generic `fan_out_to_user`** ("notify this one user, gated on the group pref"). This was renamed from `fan_out_member_added` when plus-ones became its third caller (join-request approval, member-add, plus-one invite); callers each build their own payload.
  - **Invites do NOT accumulate per (poll, account) ŌĆö already bounded by the responded-skip, no dedup needed.** `_seed_plus_one_votes` writes the seeded vote BEFORE minting the invite, and skips any account that `user_responded_to_poll` (which the seeded vote satisfies). So on every subsequent submission/edit by the submitter the represented account is skipped ŌåÆ at most ONE seeded vote + ONE invite per (poll, represented-account) is ever minted; re-sending the same `plus_one_user_ids` mints nothing new. (Different accounts / different polls each get their own invite ŌĆö expected, not accumulation.) Locked by `test_plus_ones.py::TestPlusOneInviteNotMembership::test_resubmit_does_not_mint_duplicate_invite`. The earlier "mints a fresh invite every submission, a dedup is a possible tidy-up" worry was overstated ŌĆö building explicit invite-dedup would solve a non-problem.
  - **Public-group redundancy**: for a public group the invite is somewhat redundant (the recipient would auto-join on visit anyway) ŌĆö harmless, the deep link still works.

### Document Scroll Architecture

- **The document (body/html) is the scroller.** `body` has no `overflow: hidden`; top/bottom bars are `position: fixed` and overlay the scrolling content. The previous "fixed viewport + inner `.safari-scroll-container`" layout was removed ŌĆö don't reintroduce inner `overflow-auto` wrappers for page content. Modal sheets and autocomplete dropdowns may have their own internal scroll, but page chrome must not.
- **Pull-to-refresh is the browser's native behavior.** We no longer ship a custom touch-driven PTR implementation ŌĆö an earlier version caused visible oscillation when approaching the top of the page (body-transform fighting momentum-scroll). The browser's native PTR gesture (Chrome mobile, Safari mobile) handles refresh. Consequence: `overscroll-behavior` is NOT set to `none` on html/body ŌĆö leaving it at the default enables native PTR and the iOS rubber-band bounce, which is fine.
- **Never use UA sniffing (`/iPad|iPhone|iPod/`) to detect iOS.** Since iOS 26, Apple froze the OS version in the UA string. Worse, modern iPhones (17+) and iPads report `Macintosh; Intel Mac OS X 10_15_7` ŌĆö identical to desktop Safari. In PWA standalone mode, "Safari" and "Mobile" tokens are also stripped, making the UA completely indistinguishable from a Mac. Use `navigator.standalone` (WebKit-only property): `undefined` = not Apple, `false` = Safari browser, `true` = standalone PWA.
- **NEVER use `e.preventDefault()` in touchmove on a scrollable element.** On iOS, calling `preventDefault()` on even a 1px touchmove causes the browser to classify the entire gesture as non-scrollable, permanently blocking scroll for that touch sequence. Any touch listeners on scrollable elements must be `{ passive: true }`.
- **`transform: scale(1)` is NOT a no-op on iOS.** Any CSS `transform` (even identity) creates a containing block that can break momentum scrolling in child `overflow: auto` elements. The `responsive-scaling-container` omits `transform` on mobile ŌĆö desktop media queries apply the actual scaling transforms.
- **Modal body-lock uses `position: fixed; top: -scrollY`** to freeze scroll without `overflow: hidden` (which doesn't reliably block iOS native PTR). The create-question modal in `template.tsx` saves `window.scrollY` on open and restores it with `window.scrollTo(0, scrollY)` on close.
- **Don't use `env(safe-area-inset-bottom)` in layout-affecting properties that feed `scrollHeight`.** On iOS Safari browser mode the value is dynamic ŌĆö `0` when the URL bar is visible (it occludes the home-indicator area), `~34px` when the URL bar hides. If a page's `padding-bottom` uses `calc(X + env(safe-area-inset-bottom))`, the document height animates in lockstep with the URL bar, making `max-scrollable` a moving target and producing a visible scrollY clamp during momentum near the bottom edge. Use a static value for content padding; reserve `env(safe-area-inset-bottom)` for the positioning of truly fixed elements (e.g., the new group button, the floating `BubbleBarPanel`) where it doesn't affect flow. The home-page padding is `6rem` flat (clearing the new group button); group-like pages reserve `var(--bubble-bar-panel-height, 12rem)` for the floating bubble panel ŌĆö see the BubbleBarPanel section below.
- **Group-page bottom padding is `var(--bubble-bar-panel-height, 12rem)`** ŌĆö a CSS variable set by the floating `BubbleBarPanel`'s ResizeObserver. The cards-wrapper inside `GroupContent` reserves exactly the panel's measured height so the last card sits flush against the panel's top edge at scroll-bottom. The `12rem` fallback (192px) is a generous upper bound for the single-row bubble bar (one ~40px button row + 34px safe-area inset) used during the first paint before the observer fires; the observer collapses it to the real ~75px on the next tick. The template wrapper at `app/template.tsx` no longer adds a `paddingBottom: '0.5rem'` for `isGroupLikePage` ŌĆö that buffer was for the OLD in-flow bubble bar and surfaced as an 8px gap below the last card once the bar floated. `slideOverlay`'s group-kind `innerStyle` and `GroupBackdropHost`'s wrapper similarly dropped their 0.5rem so the overlay ŌåÆ real-route handoff doesn't shift content. Historical: an earlier in-flow bubble bar set padding to 0.5rem flat; an even earlier iteration set it to 4.5rem (72px) as iOS Safari URL bar clearance but read as a layout bug on every other surface.
- **Per-second `setState` in a countdown component causes Firefox iOS scroll jitter at scroll edges.** When ~15+ countdown spans each re-render every second via `setTimeLeft(...)`, Firefox iOS momentum scrolling near the top edge compensates scrollY by +200-230px in a single frame (a single-frame snap, not a smooth bounce). The React reconciliation pass triggered by the setState ŌĆö even if the DOM diff is just a text-node swap ŌĆö trips a layout event that FxiOS treats as reason to adjust `scrollY`. Fix: update countdown text imperatively via a ref (`span.textContent = ...` inside `setInterval`) so React never re-renders. Both `components/GroupList.tsx` and the inner `SimpleCountdown` in `app/group/[groupId]/page.tsx` use this pattern. Safari iOS doesn't exhibit the bug, but the ref-based approach is also more efficient.
- **Diagnosing weird scroll behavior: instrument scrollY with a client-log tracer.** When user-reported "jitter" doesn't reproduce in Playwright (chromium + touch simulation can't replicate iOS momentum + URL-bar physics), add a temporary `window.addEventListener('scroll', () => console.log(...))` that records `scrollY`, `scrollHeight`, and `innerHeight` with timestamps via the existing client log forwarder. The user reproduces the issue once on their real device; the buffer captures the per-frame numbers. Finding a single-frame `dy > 100` with stable `scrollHeight`/`innerHeight` ŌåÆ something's programmatically adjusting scrollY (anchoring, max-clamp, browser compensation). `dy` tracking scrollHeight/innerHeight changes ŌåÆ layout-driven. This is how both the iOS Safari URL-bar bug and the FxiOS countdown-setState bug were nailed down ŌĆö without the tracer, both looked identical visually.

### BubbleBarHost + BubbleBarPanel (Floating Bubble Bar)

> **UPDATE (June 2026, `claude/poll-creation-interface-8x3rD`): the bubble-button bar was REPLACED by a search-box poll creator.** The horizontally-scrolling category buttons (`BUBBLE_BUTTON_CLASS` / `BUBBLE_BUTTON_STYLE` / `BUBBLE_ICON_STYLE` / `BUBBLE_TITLE_STYLE` / `BUBBLE_*_PX` constants) are DELETED; the rounded-rectangle bubble description below is HISTORICAL. The bar is now an always-visible pill **text input** (`pollSearchBar` in `app/create-poll/page.tsx`) pinned to the bottom (NO hide-on-scroll ŌĆö the panel's scroll-hide subsystem was removed). Tapping it raises the keyboard and expands a full-screen, keyboard-aware suggestion list ABOVE the bar:
>   - **Keyboard-aware layout**: the focused container is `position: fixed` pinned to the visual viewport (`top: vv.offsetTop; height: vv.height`) so its bottom edge lands flush on the keyboard's top and the input bar (its last child) sits just above it. ONE `<input>` (never reparented across the focus toggle) so focus/keyboard survive. `searchVv` tracked via a `visualViewport` resize/scroll listener that's attached **only while focused** (the component is layout-persistent, so an always-on listener would re-render on every scroll on every page). The unfocused container is bottom-anchored `{bottom:0}` auto-height (just the pill).
>   - **Bottom-anchored, best match nearest the bar**: the list `flex-col` + an inner `mt-auto` wrapper stacks rows UP from just above the bar (collapses to 0 on overflow so the top stays scrollable); an effect re-pins scroll to the bottom on focus / suggestion change / vv change. Order topŌåÆbottom: **Yes/No** (frames the literal text as a yes/no question), **filtered categories** (built-ins filtered by typed-token prefix match, reversed so the best match is at the bottom of the group), **Options** (when the text parses into Ōēź2 comma/"or"-delimited options ŌåÆ fixed-options poll), **Context** (`{category:'custom', forField:<typed text>}` ŌåÆ "Options for &lt;text&gt;?", interpreting the input as the poll's CONTEXT rather than its category; shown ONLY when the raw text has no standalone "for" yet ŌĆö guard is `!/\bfor\b/i.test(raw)`, NOT `!context`, since "Birthday for" yields empty context but must still suppress the row; sits just ABOVE Custom), **Custom** (bottom, next to the bar ŌĆö a custom-category poll named after the typed text, tagged "custom"). A trailing **"for ŌĆ”"** clause sets the context (`forField`) on every suggestion (shown as a muted "for ŌĆ”" suffix); the yes/no row keeps the literal text as its prompt. Helpers `parseForContext` / `parseOptionsFromText` (module scope) + the `searchSuggestions` useMemo.
>   - **Segment labelling (`claude/poll-suggestion-labels-jTjOh`)**: each suggestion's text is split into typed `SuggestionSegment[]` (module-level type + `contextSegments(context)` helper, both above `CreateQuestionContent`) so the words that get PREFILLED show a tiny uppercase label over the left edge + a matching-color underline (`border-b-2`). Fixed palette (module consts, literal Tailwind class strings so JIT keeps them): **green** `SEG_CATEGORY`, **purple** `SEG_CONTEXT`, and a cycling `OPTION_SEG_COLORS` (red/blue/gold/pink/teal/orange) one per option. Colors are softened (`text-{c}-500/80 dark:text-{c}-400/80` + `border-{c}-400/50`). Per type: yes/no ŌåÆ one plain unlabeled segment (the text becomes the TITLE, not a bucket); category ŌåÆ `[{label:Category}, ...contextSegments]`; options ŌåÆ one `{label:Option}` per parsed option (cycling color) interleaved with muted `┬Ę` + `...contextSegments`; custom ŌåÆ `[{label:Category subject}, ...contextSegments]` or a bare unlabeled `New Poll`. Connectives (`for`, `┬Ę`) are `muted` (gray, no label). Render: the segments `<span>` is `relative ... overflow-hidden whitespace-nowrap` with `pt-3` ONLY when a labeled segment is present; each labeled segment is `relative inline-block` with the label `absolute left-0 bottom-full` (sits inside the `pt-3` zone so overflow-hidden, which clips long text on the right, doesn't clip it). `segments` is the SOLE render source ŌĆö the suggestion objects no longer carry `primary`/`context` (the aria-label derives from `segments.map(s=>s.text).join('')`). Palette is intentionally NOT lifted to `lib/` (single consumer; the codebase uses ad-hoc color strings everywhere).
>   - **Selecting a row** ŌåÆ `chooseSuggestion(overrides)` ŌåÆ name-gate (stashes a retry THUNK in `pendingSearchAction` for `AccountGateModal`, since suggestions carry a full draft prefill ŌĆö title/options/context ŌĆö not just a category) ŌåÆ `openModalWithDraft(overrides)` which layers the overrides over `emptyDraft()` and opens the new-poll modal prefilled. `openModalFor`/`handleBubbleClick`/`pendingBubbleCategory` (category-only) were retired in favor of these.
>   - **The Ō£Ģ on the left of the bar** (`dismissSearch`) collapses back to the bottom pill; tapping outside / blurring the input also collapses.
>   - **Body scroll is locked while the bar is focused (`useBodyScrollLock(isModalOpen || searchFocused, false)`).** Focusing the input raises the soft keyboard / shrinks the visual viewport, which drifts the underlying group page's document scroll even though the picker is `position: fixed` ŌĆö so cancelling left the group scrolled away from where it was (reported bug). The lock snapshots `scrollY` on focus and restores it via `window.scrollTo` on dismiss. `locked` stays true across the focus ŌåÆ modal-open transition (`searchFocused` flips false as `isModalOpen` flips true in the same render batch), so picking a suggestion doesn't teardown/restore-flicker the scroll. Don't gate the lock on `isModalOpen` alone ŌĆö the focused-but-no-modal picker state needs it too.
>   - **Input caret**: the input carries `style={{ lineHeight: 'normal' }}` (NOT Tailwind `text-base`'s 1.5rem, NOT `leading-none`) ŌĆö iOS Safari draws the caret on the font's natural metrics, so a custom line-height desyncs the caret from the placeholder/text (caret sat too low). `normal` makes them share metrics (default-input behavior).
>   - **Access gating (`lib/groupAccessState.ts`)**: the bar must NOT appear on the "Private Group / no access" wall. A module store (subscribe/`useSyncExternalStore`, mirrors `useHomeBackdropActive`) records the route id of the most recently loaded-with-access group; `GroupContent` calls `setGroupAccessGranted(groupId)` once it's loaded WITHOUT error (the wall ŌĆö `error || !group` ŌĆö never reaches that). `BubbleBarHost` shows the bar on `/g/<id>` (id via `extractGroupRouteId`) only when access is granted for THAT id (default hidden-until-confirmed avoids a flash on walls + stale-grant leaks across groups); the bare `/g` placeholder (no id) is always allowed. No unmount cleanup of the store (same overlay-double-mount reasoning as `data-group-id`); staleness handled by the route-id match.
>   - `BubbleBarPanel` is now a trivial portal-target div (`<div id={DRAFT_POLL_PORTAL_ID}/>`, NO transform so the portaled `fixed` bar is viewport-relative); it still exports `PANEL_HEIGHT_VAR` (the cards-wrapper bottom padding) which `CreateQuestionContent` writes from the measured unfocused bar height. `PANEL_OFFSET_VAR` was deleted (nothing read it after the down scroll-arrow was retired).
>   - **UPDATE (June 2026, `claude/poll-suggestion-text-box-GpJHt`): suggestions render the REAL auto-title; the bottom bar is split into a circular +/Ō£Ģ button + a separate text box; recently-posted poll titles are offered as reuse suggestions; the right-side pill chips and the empty "New Poll" row are GONE.** Specifics superseding the two bullets above:
>     - **Every row's text IS the title the poll would land on**, derived from the same `overrides` the row prefills ŌĆö so the displayed text can never drift from the created poll. The single source of truth is `draftTitleSegments(d)` in `createPollHelpers.ts` (`deriveDraftTitle` is now literally `draftTitleSegments(d).map(s=>s.text).join('')`, proven byte-identical to the old generator across 1440 cases): it returns typed `TitleSegment[]` (`kind: 'plain'|'category'|'context'|'option'`, `muted?`, `optionIndex?`). `page.tsx: overridesToSegments(overrides)` fills a minimal `TitleDraft` from a row's overrides ŌåÆ `draftTitleSegments` ŌåÆ `annotateSegments` (maps `kind`ŌåÆthe `SEG_CATEGORY`/`SEG_CONTEXT`/`OPTION_SEG_COLORS` UI spans; muted glue greys out; plain prompt is bare). The old per-type inline segment building + `contextSegments` helper + the `┬Ę ` option separator are REPLACED ŌĆö options now read as the actual or-list ("Dune, Oppenheimer, or Barbie for movie night?") via `orListSegments` (mirrors `buildOrList`'s truncation, minus the trailing "?"). When adding a category to `draftTitleSegments`, the suggestion rows pick it up automatically.
>     - **Recently-posted poll titles** (annotated) sit at the bottom of the list, just above the bar. `pollToRecentEntry(poll)` reconstructs `overrides` + the annotated `titleText` from a poll's question (SINGLE-question polls only ŌĆö multi-question titles can't be cleanly annotated from one section; yes_no special-cased to its prompt; icon via the shared `getCategoryIcon(q)`). A `recentEntries` useState is snapshotted from `getCachedAccessiblePolls()` in an effect keyed on `[searchFocused]` (re-read on every open, e.g. after creating a poll; cleared on close), sorted newest-LAST so the most recent sits nearest the bar. The `searchSuggestions` memo filters them by the same `matchesTokens` token-prefix predicate as the category rows. Requires the viewer to be a member of a group whose polls are warm in the accessible cache (loaded by visiting the group).
>     - **Split bar**: a standalone circular `<button>` (the `+`/`Ō£Ģ`) + a separate text-box pill, no inner `+`. `+` (unfocused) opens a blank poll via `chooseSuggestion({ category: 'custom' })`; `Ō£Ģ` (focused) `dismissSearch`. **It MUST be ONE persistent button toggling its `onClick` on `searchFocused`, with `onMouseDown={(e)=>e.preventDefault()}` ŌĆö NOT two conditionally-rendered buttons.** The preventDefault is load-bearing: without it, tapping `Ō£Ģ` blurs the input ŌåÆ `onBlur` flips `searchFocused` false ŌåÆ the click then runs the `+` branch (opens the modal instead of cancelling). preventDefault keeps focus stable so the ternary reads the correct state at click time (same pattern the suggestion rows use). Two separate buttons are WORSE ŌĆö the focused `Ō£Ģ` would unmount mid-click when blur re-renders, dropping the click entirely.
>     - The empty-text "New Poll" suggestion row is removed (the `+` button replaces it); a custom-category row still appears only when a non-empty subject is typed. `SEARCH_ROW_CLASS` dropped its `border-b` dividers and halved the inter-row vertical padding (`py-3.5`ŌåÆ`py-[7px]`, `min-h-[3.5rem]`ŌåÆ`min-h-[1.75rem]`); the right-side `tag` pill field + its render were deleted.
>     - **UPDATE (`claude/poll-option-annotations-blue-NrU8C`): option annotations are all blue; yes/no + limited-supply rows are annotated with the category NAME; yes/no titles get a "?"; a Limited Supply suggestion row was added.** Specifics:
>       - **Options are a single blue palette, not a cycling set.** `OPTION_SEG_COLORS` (the 6-color red/blue/gold/pink/teal/orange array) was replaced by one `SEG_OPTION` const (blue). `TitleSegment.optionIndex` (the cycling index) went with it ŌĆö every option annotation is now blue regardless of position.
>       - **UPDATE (`claude/poll-textbox-annotations-ZbuwX`): only the FIRST option carries the "Options" label; every option is still underlined individually.** `annotateSegments` (page.tsx) tracks an `optionLabelled` flag and tags only the first `kind: 'option'` segment with `label: 'Options'` (plural); 2nd+ options get the bare `SEG_OPTION` (blue `colorText`/`colorBorder`) with no label. The render branch in `searchSuggestions` now keys the labelled/underlined branch on **`seg.colorBorder`** (not `seg.label`), and renders the label span conditionally (`{seg.label && ...}`) ŌĆö so an unlabelled-but-coloured segment still gets its `border-b-2` underline. The `pt-3` label-room reservation stays gated on `s.segments.some((seg) => seg.label)` (the first option + category/context still carry labels). When adding a future segment kind that should underline without a label, give it a `colorBorder` and omit `label`.
>       - **yes/no + limited_supply titles annotate the WHOLE title with the category.** `draftTitleSegments` emits the typed prompt/item as `kind: 'category'` with a per-segment `label` override (`TitleSegment.label?: string`), so the suggestion row shows a **YES/NO** / **LIMITED SUPPLY** label + underline over the whole title (like the custom-category row, but with the specific category name instead of the generic "CATEGORY"). **UPDATE (`claude/poll-annotation-styling-sfEgO`): these whole-title category-NAME annotations are FADED GREY, not green.** Only the rows whose label IS a specific category name spanning the entire typed title (yes/no, limited_supply) use the faded `SEG_WHOLE_TITLE` const (`text-gray-400/80 dark:text-gray-500/80` label + `border-gray-300/60 dark:border-gray-600/60` underline); the generic green `SEG_CATEGORY` is kept for bare built-in category words (Place, Movie, Restaurant, Time, ...) and the custom CATEGORY row. `annotateSegments` (page.tsx) keys on the override: `if (s.label) return {...SEG_WHOLE_TITLE, label: s.label}` else green `SEG_CATEGORY`. The label string comes from `labelForCategory('yes_no'|'limited_supply')` ŌĆö NOT hardcoded ŌĆö so it stays in lockstep with `_CATEGORY_LABELS`. When adding another category whose whole title should carry a specific (faded) label, set `kind:'category'` + `label: labelForCategory(cat)` in its `draftTitleSegments` branch. (A broader "fade ANY category that spans the whole line" rule ŌĆö keyed on the absence of context/option segments ŌĆö was tried and reverted: it also drained the built-in category rows' green, which the owner wanted kept.)
>       - **yes/no titles end with "?".** `yesNoTitleText(prompt)` / `yesNoNeedsQuestionMark(prompt)` append "?" unless the prompt already ends with terminal punctuation (`?`/`!`/`.`). Applied in ALL THREE yes/no title paths to preserve the "suggestion ŌēĪ persisted title" invariant: `draftTitleSegments` (the "?" is a trailing MUTED plain segment, so it greys like other rows' "?"), `draftPollPreview` (string), and the submit handler's `wrapperTitle` (gated on `draftDbQuestionType === 'yes_no'`, so limited_supply item names stay "?"-free). limited_supply gets NO "?" (item name, not a question).
>       - **Limited Supply suggestion row** sits next to the Yes/No row at the top of `searchSuggestions` (`row('limited', '­¤Ä¤’ĖÅ', { category: 'limited_supply', title: raw, isAutoTitle: false })`) ŌĆö frames the typed text as the item name, mirroring how Yes/No frames it as the prompt.
>       - **Title-required categories (`yes_no`, `limited_supply`) are EXCLUDED from the default category-suggestion loop** (the `cats = orderedBubbleEntries.filter(...)` in `searchSuggestions`). A default category row renders the category NAME as the title via `draftTitleSegments`' whole-title annotation ŌĆö which for these two categories is exactly what the user-typed title is supposed to override (so the row would show "Yes/No" / "Limited Supply" AS the title, the reported bug). They stay creatable via their dedicated top rows (the `row('yesno', ...)` / `row('limited', ...)` calls, which frame the TYPED TEXT as the title), and their RECENT polls still surface in the `recentEntries` loop (those carry real user-typed titles, so showing them is correct). When adding a future category whose title must be user-typed, add its `value` to this filter's exclusion list AND give it a dedicated top row.
>     - **UPDATE (`claude/poll-suggestion-spacing-fUm7Q`): suggestion-row spacing + icon/text vertical alignment.** `SEARCH_ROW_CLASS` inter-row spacing was tightened to 25% of the prior baseline (`py-[7px]`ŌåÆ`py-[1.75px]`, `min-h-[1.75rem]`ŌåÆ`min-h-[0.4375rem]`); the icon's flanking spacing was cut 30% (`px-5`ŌåÆ`pl-[14px] pr-5` for the left, `gap-4`ŌåÆ`gap-[11.2px]` for the iconŌåÆtext gap ŌĆö the row's *right* edge padding stays `pr-5` since that's after the text, not beside the icon). The annotation label sits flush above its text via `bottom-full`; the small remaining gap is the text line-box half-leading (~3px measured) and is nudged via `translate-y-[ŌĆ”px]` on the label span (currently `1.368px`). **Icon/text vertical alignment is load-bearing and non-obvious:** the text wrapper carries `pt-3` (label-clearance room), so with the row's `items-center` the icon centered against the *taller padded box* and the visible text glyphs ended up ~6.5px lower. Fix = mirror the SAME conditional `pt-3` onto the icon span (gated on `hasLabel = s.segments.some(seg => seg.label)`, hoisted once per row) so icon and text boxes are equal height (both 36px) and their glyph lines align. **Don't measure alignment by the icon span's bounding-box center** ŌĆö that box includes the empty `pt-3` label zone on top, so it reads ~6px high; the visible emoji sits in the box's bottom line region. Verify with a screenshot, not `getBoundingClientRect()` on the padded span. Sub-pixel `translate-y` / `py` tweaks below ~1px are imperceptible ŌĆö the icon glyph height (`text-2xl`) floors the row pitch once padding shrinks past it.

The HISTORICAL bubble-button description follows.

The create-poll bubble bar is mounted **ONCE at the layout level** by `<BubbleBarHost>` (`components/BubbleBarHost.tsx`, rendered in `app/layout.tsx`). It is NOT rendered per-route inside `GroupContent` / `EmptyPlaceholder` anymore. The host decides *whether* the bar is shown; `components/BubbleBarPanel.tsx` is the fixed-bottom chrome + the `#draft-poll-portal` target + the scroll-hide logic. The bar's JSX (the buttons) is still owned by `CreateQuestionContent` (`PersistentCreatePollHost`, also layout-level), which portals into `#draft-poll-portal`. The panel auto-hides on scroll-down and reappears on scroll-up or at the document edges.

- **Why layout-level (the slide-flicker saga).** When the bar lived in `GroupContent` it was rendered in BOTH the slide overlay's GroupContent and the real route's during a pollŌåÆgroup back slide, so the two copies met at the slide seam with mismatched horizontal offsets ŌĆö a jumbled/**doubled** bar (confirmed on prod: 14 buttons mid-slide instead of 7). Single-rendering it (only the real route) killed the doubling but then the bar had to wait for the heavy GroupContent to commit ŌĆö **measured 1ŌĆō3.5s on the dev server** ŌĆö before appearing. Both are structurally impossible with a single layout-level instance that isn't gated on the group render.
- **Behavior: no bar DURING the transition, then slide it up AFTER.** `BubbleBarHost` shows the bar iff `isGroupRootView(pathname) && !slideActive && !homeBackdrop`. `slideActive` (`useIsSlideOverlayGroupActive()`) is true while a group-arrival slide overlay is mounted, so the bar is withheld for the whole transition and mounts only once the overlay unmounts on the settled group route. `BubbleBarPanel` mounts **hidden** (`visible` starts `false` ŌåÆ `translateY(100%)`) and slides up via the existing `transition-transform`. Net UX: the page transition plays with no bar, then the bar slides up from the bottom. Direct group-page loads (no slide, `slideActive` already false) mount + slide up immediately. This sidesteps the seam entirely ŌĆö the bar is never on screen during the slide.
