- **Slide-up entrance needs a DOUBLE rAF.** A dedicated mount effect flips `visible=true` after `requestAnimationFrame(() => requestAnimationFrame(...))`. A single rAF batches with the mount commit so the `translateY(100%)` frame never paints and the transition is optimized away (the bar pops in). Same lesson as the slide overlay's enterŌåÆshown handoff. The scroll-visibility effect deliberately does NOT call its initial `schedule()` anymore ŌĆö that would set `visible=true` on a single rAF and pre-empt the entrance; scroll-restore / bottom-pin still drive `evaluate()` via the scroll events they fire, so the `isScrollRestoring()` force-visible path is unaffected.
- **`useHomeBackdropActive()` (`lib/useHomeBackdropActive.ts`) is the shared SHOW/HIDE_HOME_BACKDROP_EVENT listener.** During a groupŌåÆhome swipe-back the group route is still the current path (until the gesture commits), so `isGroupRootView` would keep the bar on ŌĆö floating it over the revealed home page. `BubbleBarHost` gates on `!homeBackdrop` so the bar hides for the duration of that gesture. The hook is shared by all three components that react to the backdrop (`HomeBackdropHost`, `CreateGroupButtonHost`, `BubbleBarHost`) ŌĆö don't re-inline the addEventListener/removeEventListener boilerplate.
- **Behavior change vs the old per-route bar (swipe-back-from-group):** the old bar was a `useSwipeBackGesture.extraTargets` member, so it translated horizontally WITH the page during a groupŌåÆhome swipe. The layout-level bar instead **hides** at swipe-start (via `homeBackdrop`) and is gone by commit. Accepted trade-off ŌĆö a fixed bar that vanishes as you leave reads fine and avoids a bar floating over home; it's an unreported gesture and not the pollŌåÆgroup path that motivated the work. If you want slide-with-page back, you'd need to re-anchor the bar into the swipe transform, which the layout-level single-instance model can't do cleanly.
- **Visibility rule (scroll-hide):** `visible = atTop || atBottom || lastDirection === 'up' || !userInteracted`. The `atTop` clause is load-bearing on iOS: rubber-band at the top edge produces a synthetic positive scrollY delta on snap-back, which would otherwise flip the direction to `'down'` and hide the panel. The `!userInteracted` clause keeps programmatic scrolls (back-nav restore, bottom-pin, iOS scroll-anchoring) from hiding the bar ŌĆö only a real pointer/wheel/keydown-driven scroll-down hides it.
- **Two-layer DOM structure** (outer **shell** `position: fixed z-30` + touch-stop handlers, inner **panel** with bg/border/safe-area-padding + the visibility `translateY`). The shell is no longer a swipe transform target (the bar isn't in `GroupContent`'s swipe wrapper), but the split is kept: the shell owns positioning + `onTouchStart/Move/End/Cancel` `stopPropagation` (so a horizontal drag on the bubble row can't initiate a page swipe), and the inner panel owns the visibility transform. `z-30` always ŌĆö the bar is never on-screen during a slide so it no longer elevates above the overlay.
- **CSS vars `PANEL_HEIGHT_VAR` / `PANEL_OFFSET_VAR`** are exported from `components/BubbleBarPanel.tsx`. The cards-wrapper in `GroupContent` reserves `var(${PANEL_HEIGHT_VAR}, 12rem)` of `padding-bottom` so the last card sits flush against the panel at scroll-bottom; the down scroll-helper arrow uses `bottom: calc(... + var(${PANEL_OFFSET_VAR}, 0px))` so it floats above the panel when visible and reclaims the space when it auto-hides. Don't hand-write the CSS var names ŌĆö import the constants so a rename is grep-safe.
- **Measurement via `useMeasuredHeight`** (`lib/useMeasuredHeight.ts`) on the inner panel. **No initial seed** ŌĆö see "Empty-write guard" pitfall below for why. A `vvCounter` state is bumped on every `visualViewport.resize` and passed as the hook's deps ŌĆö that re-attaches the ResizeObserver and reads a fresh `offsetHeight`. iOS browsers resolve `env(safe-area-inset-bottom)` differently depending on URL-bar / toolbar visibility, but the env-driven size change isn't always picked up by ResizeObserver on those browsers; the deps bump catches the shift without reimplementing measurement.
- **Empty-write guard + `:root` CSS defaults.** The bubble bar JSX is portaled in by `CreateQuestionContent` asynchronously (its MutationObserver fires after BubbleBarPanel mounts), so for a few rAF ticks after each BubbleBarPanel mount the `#draft-poll-portal` div is empty and the panel's `offsetHeight` is only its border + `env(safe-area-inset-bottom)` ŌĆö 1px on browsers without safe-area, ~35px on iPhone X-class. Writing that small value to `--bubble-bar-panel-offset` pulls the down scroll-helper arrow to the viewport bottom; when content lands and the panel resizes to ~130px the arrow's `transition: bottom 200ms ease-out` then visibly animates it up ŌĆö surfacing to users as "the arrow repositions itself after the slide completes". Two-part fix in this file + `app/globals.css`: (a) `:root { --bubble-bar-panel-height: 192px; --bubble-bar-panel-offset: 192px; }` so consumers (cards-wrapper padding-bottom, down arrow's `bottom`) have a sensible default before any panel mounts; (b) BubbleBarPanel's CSS var writer skips when `visible && heightPx < MIN_MEANINGFUL_PANEL_HEIGHT` (50px) ŌĆö comfortably above max-empty (35px) and below min-populated (~88px on wide desktop, ~130px+ on phones). The seed value passed to `useMeasuredHeight` was also removed; with the seed at 192 (Ōēź threshold), Render 1's useEffect closure could fire with `panelHeight=192` and write 192 to the var, briefly snapping the arrow back to the default before the measurement-driven write of 129 ŌĆö sequence visible in the trace as `192 ŌåÆ 129 ŌåÆ 192 ŌåÆ 129` during the slide. Default-0 panelHeight + threshold guard catches that path too. Trace evidence: with the fix, the var transitions `192px ŌåÆ 129px` exactly once per slide (matching ResizeObserver's first real measurement after content portal); without the fix, the var oscillates `(empty) ŌåÆ 1px ŌåÆ 129px ŌåÆ 1px ŌåÆ 129px` across the overlayŌåÆreal-route handoff.
- **Cached scrollHeight.** Reading `document.documentElement.scrollHeight` on every scroll tick forces a synchronous layout flush ŌĆö on long group pages that's the hottest cost in the visibility loop. The component caches it via a one-shot `ResizeObserver(documentElement)` that updates a ref; the scroll evaluator uses the cached value.
- **Change-detection guard on CSS-var writes.** `style.setProperty` on `:root` invalidates style on every element reading the var (the cards-wrapper and the down arrow here). The write effect compares the new `(height, visible)` tuple against `lastWrittenRef` and skips no-ops ŌĆö important because `visualViewport.resize` can fire many times per URL-bar transition with the same `offsetHeight`.
- **Single instance ŌĆö no dual-portal anymore.** With the bar at the layout level there is exactly one `BubbleBarPanel` / one `#draft-poll-portal` at any time. The old "two instances coexist during a slide-overlay handoff" concern is gone (it was the source of the doubling). The CSS vars are still deliberately NOT cleared on unmount ŌĆö when the bar hides (leaving a group route) a sibling group route may be about to mount and the host padding shouldn't flash to 0.
- **Transitions: the bar does not slide WITH the page ŌĆö it's withheld then slides up.** There is no per-transition "panel translates with the page" behavior to maintain anymore (that was the per-route + extraTarget model). Every group arrival = no bar during the slide, then a slide-up on the settled route (see the "no bar DURING the transition" bullet above). The groupŌåÆhome swipe-back hides the bar via `homeBackdrop`; the groupŌåÆhome View-Transitions back button removes it when `pathname` leaves the group route.
- **Pitfall: rubber-band at scroll-top can flip direction to `'down'`** on iOS. Without the `atTop` clause, the snap-back from a pull-down gesture (scrollY goes negative briefly, then snaps back to 0 with a positive delta > threshold) flips `lastDirection` to `'down'` and hides the panel even though the user is at the top. The `atTop = currentY <= 2` check defeats this.
- **Pitfall: env(safe-area-inset-bottom) changes can be silent to ResizeObserver on iOS.** The `vvCounter`-driven remeasure is what catches them. If you remove the `visualViewport.resize` listener, expect iOS Firefox / iOS Safari to ship a stale panel height on URL-bar toggles, sliding content under the panel at scroll-bottom.

### Voter Availability: Split Slots + Ghost Re-add (`DayTimeWindowsInput` voter form)

The voter availability form (rendered by `TimeBallotSection` ŌåÆ `TimeQuestionFields` ŌåÆ `DayTimeWindowsInput` with `questionWindows` set, i.e. `isVoterForm`) lets a voter carve a creator's day window into multiple disconnected segments. Model (replaces the old per-window enabled-checkbox toggle, which is gone):

- **All ballot slots are deletable** (delete `├Ś` button), exactly like the creation form, and the `+` button (`pickVoterSplitWindow`) adds another ŌĆö dropped into the largest free gap inside the creator's allowed windows, with a 15-min margin off any edge that abuts an existing slot so it isn't born orange. Voters may delete every slot in a day (the creation form keeps its "can't delete the last slot" rule; voter form does not ŌĆö re-add via a ghost).
- **Ghost rows.** For each original (creator) window that NO current ballot slot overlaps (`windowsOverlap`), a muted row with an empty checkbox is rendered (`handleRestoreWindow` re-adds the full window on check). Ghosts are merged with real rows in start-time order, and **suppressed when `disabled`** (the read-only post-vote summary) ŌĆö there they'd read as "options you forgot".
- **Soft validation, not a hard clamp.** The old per-index `constraintMin/Max` clamp on the edit `TimeGridModal` was REMOVED (it mapped windows to the wrong question window once a split re-sorted the list). A voter window is invalid when it's outside every creator window (`isWindowWithinQuestionWindows`) OR touches/overlaps its sorted predecessor (`win.min <= prev.max`); invalid slots get the orange `intersecting` pill variant AND block submit.
- **`hasInvalidVoterWindows(voterDays, questionDays)` (`lib/timeUtils.ts`) is the single submit-gate predicate**, mirroring the per-pill orange flags so the highlight and the block can't drift. It's checked in THREE places that must stay in lockstep: `buildVoteData` (`voteDataBuilders.ts`, returns `{ok:false}` ŌĆö covers the batch/wrapper path), `QuestionBallot.handleVoteClick` (early-return BEFORE opening the confirm modal ŌĆö the detail page's wrapper Submit routes through `handleVoteClick`, so without this a voter would open the confirm modal and only get bounced on confirm), and `TimeBallotSection` (disables its own Submit button + shows the amber notice).
- **Card-less day rows.** `TimeQuestionFields` renders the day list as borderless `DayTimeWindowsInput` rows inside a `divide-y divide-gray-200 dark:divide-gray-700` (no per-day card). Because the pills then sit directly on the availability card (`POLL_SUBCARD_CLASS` = `bg-gray-100/900`), the filled pill / `+` button backgrounds are `bg-gray-200 dark:bg-gray-700` (one step darker than the surface) ŌĆö also legible on the create-poll white/`gray-800` card. Don't drop them back to `gray-100` or they vanish on the voter card in light mode.
- **`handleEditApply` spreads the existing window (`{...w, min, max}`)** so an edit preserves other fields rather than replacing the object. The vestigial `enabled` field is still defensively honored by the `voteDataBuilders` cleaning filter + the submit gate (`w.enabled !== false`), but nothing sets it false anymore.
- Composes cleanly with #515 (voters can't add/remove DAYS ŌĆö no day-picker in the voter `TimeQuestionFields`) since this feature is about within-day SLOTS, and with #516's drag-select which lives in the preferences phase, not availability.

### Constrained Time Wheel Pickers (Voter Response)

- **(Historical for the day-window editor) Voter time ranges as strict subsets via clamping is RETIRED for `DayTimeWindowsInput`** ŌĆö see "Voter Availability: Split Slots" above; containment is now soft-validated (orange + block), not clamped. The wheel-picker notes below still describe `TimeCounterInput` / `TimeGridModal` internals.
- **Voter time ranges must be strict subsets of the question creator's window.** For non-cross-midnight question windows (e.g., 9AMŌĆō5PM), enforce `voter_min < voter_max` ŌĆö never allow cross-midnight voter ranges. For cross-midnight question windows, only exclude exact equality (`min !== max`, which would be 24h). The `isValidVsSibling()` function in `TimeCounterInput.tsx` implements this.
- **Filter wheel items, don't clamp after the fact.** Clamping after scroll causes visible snap-back. Instead, compute the valid hour/minute sets upfront so invalid values are never shown.
- **Each picker must know the other picker's value** (`siblingValue` prop) to dynamically filter its options. The min picker shows only times strictly less than the current max, and vice versa. Hours with no valid minutes are hidden entirely.
- **The AM/PM wheel in constrained mode is non-interactive** ŌĆö wrapped in `pointerEvents: 'none'`, it auto-follows the selected hour via `selectedIndex`. This keeps hours in chronological order across AM/PM boundaries.
- **When an hour change invalidates the current minute**, auto-select the minute giving the smallest positive duration to/from the sibling (Ōēł1 increment gap). This avoids jarring jumps to arbitrary times.

### Cross-Midnight Time Windows

- **Time windows where `max <= min` represent cross-midnight ranges** (e.g., 10 PMŌĆō2 AM). Equal start/end means a full 24-hour window. Use `<=` consistently in all cross-midnight detection ŌĆö `<` misses the equal-times-as-24h case.
- **String comparison works for HH:MM cross-midnight detection** only because the format is always zero-padded. `"02:00" < "22:00"` is correct lexicographically. If the format ever loses zero-padding (e.g., `"2:00"`), all comparisons silently break.
- **`_window_effective_end()` in `time_slots.py`** is the canonical backend helper ŌĆö it adds 1440 minutes when `w_end <= w_start`. The frontend has no shared utility yet; cross-midnight checks are inline in `DayTimeWindowsInput` and `TimeGridModal`.
- **Looping scroll wheels must scroll to the nearest occurrence** of the target index, not the center repetition. Otherwise wraparound (12ŌåÆ1) causes the wheel to scroll the long way around through all values.
- **ScrollWheel's `suppressScrollHandler` flag can get permanently stuck.** `recenterLoop()` sets the flag and schedules an rAF to clear it, but `correctPosition()` runs synchronously right after and bails out because the flag is still set. If a touch interaction then overwrites `scrollTimeout`, the clearing rAF/timeout is lost and the flag stays true forever ŌĆö silencing all `onChange` calls. Fix: defer `correctPosition` via rAF when suppression is active, and add a safety timeout (500ms) that guarantees the flag gets cleared.
- **Use refs (not render-scope variables) for state that multiple scroll events may read/write within a single React render cycle.** `handleHourChange` in `TimeCounterInput` captured `periodIndex` from the render scope. When two scroll events crossed the AM/PM boundary before React re-rendered, the second event used the stale value and emitted the wrong time. Track such state in a `useRef` and update it immediately in the handler.

### Limited Supply Question Type

A first-come, first-served signup: the creator sets `supply_count` slots for something (tickets, leftover food, a carpool seat, a volunteer shift) and whoever **claims first** gets them. Later claimants are **waitlisted** in order. Shipped on migration 131 (type + `questions.supply_count`) + migration 132 (`questions.reveal_claimant_names`).

- **Vote shape: a claim carries NO payload.** `vote_type='limited_supply'` with `is_abstain=false` is a CLAIM, `is_abstain=true` is a DECLINE ("No thanks"). `yes_no_choice`/`ranked_choices`/`suggestions` are all NULL (enforced by the `vote_structure_valid` CHECK). No new vote columns ŌĆö claim order is just `votes.created_at`.
- **Resolution is ordering, weighted by plus-ones** (`server/algorithms/limited_supply.py: calculate_limited_supply_result`): take non-abstain votes, sort by `created_at`, then **expand each claim into one entry per represented person** ŌĆö `vote_weight(vote)` = `1 + len(plus_one_names)` (submitter first, then each named/unnamed plus-one, all sharing the claim's `created_at`). The first `supply_count` person-entries are **secured**, the rest **waitlisted**. Because slots are awarded per-head, a single claim can **straddle** the boundary (a "me + 2 friends" claim with 2 spots left secures 2, waitlists the 3rd ŌĆö first-come per person, no wasted spots). Declines take no slot, so when a secured claimant edits to a decline the next waitlister is promoted automatically (results recompute from the ordered claim list ŌĆö there's no stored "secured" flag). `claim_count` / `secured_count` / `waitlist_count` are now **people** counts (not vote-row counts). `_compute_results` returns `supply_count` / `secured_count` / `waitlist_count` / `claims[]` (`{name, secured, position, created_at}` ŌĆö one per person). Empty-string plus-ones collapse to `name=None` (FE shows the "Spot taken"/"Waiting" placeholder). A pre-migration-130 row with no `plus_one_names` weighs exactly 1.
- **The title IS the item** ("2 spare tickets"), like a yes_no prompt: the create form shows the Title field + a "Number Available" `CompactNumberRow`, NOT options/category/context (`category` stays `custom`; the bubble sets `question_type=limited_supply`). `isAutoTitle` is false. `_category_for_title` / `getQuestionLabel` / `QUESTION_TYPE_SYMBOLS` special-case `limited_supply` ŌåÆ ­¤Ä¤’ĖÅ, same convention as `time`.
- **Create-form bottom-card settings are gated so only the relevant ones show + use "claiming" wording.** The ranked-choice / suggestion settings (Suggestion Cutoff, Scoring Algorithm, Minimum Votes, Show-Results-After-Min-Votes, Allow-voting-before-options) are hidden because `isSuggestionMode` AND `inlineFormIsRankedChoice` both exclude `limited_supply` (alongside `yes_no` + `time`) ŌĆö otherwise a limited-supply category slips through (it's `!== yes_no && !== time`) and surfaces all of them. So the bottom card shows only **Claiming Cutoff** + **Allow claiming for others (plus-ones)** + the (now-shown) emoji picker. The "claiming" relabel is driven by `pollIsLimitedSupply` (= every question is limited_supply; mixed polls keep "voting"): `VotingCutoffField` takes a `label` prop ("Claiming Cutoff" vs default "Voting Cutoff"), and the plus-ones row swaps "voting"ŌåÆ"claiming". When adding a new bottom-card setting that's ranked-choice/suggestion-specific, gate it on `pollHasRankedChoice`/`pollHasPrephase` (both already exclude limited_supply) ŌĆö don't gate on a bare `category !== 'yes_no' && category !== 'time'`, which re-introduces the limited-supply leak.
- **Multi-slot claims ride the plus-ones mechanism ŌĆö `allow_plus_ones` defaults ON for limited_supply.** A voter claims N spots by adding N-1 people in the poll-level `PlusOnesInput` (the same "respond for others" feature used by time/yes-no); the claim's `plus_one_names`/`plus_one_user_ids` ride the submit and the server weights it (above). The default is set in BOTH `routers/polls.py: create_poll` (server) and `app/create-poll/page.tsx: effectiveAllowPlusOnes` (the create-form toggle's displayed state) ŌĆö keep them in sync, same as the time-question default. There is NO bespoke quantity-stepper / per-claim quantity column; plus-ones IS the multi-slot mechanism.
- **Two submit modes, picked by `PollDetailPage`:**
  - **Self-submit (no plus-ones added):** "Claim a spot" / "No thanks" post immediately via QuestionBallot's `submitVote` (speed matters ŌĆö one tap), using the `pendingSupplySubmit` deferred-submit pattern (mirrors binary-RC tap). `wrapperHandlesSubmit` is false; it's in `SELF_SUBMIT_TYPES` and `prepareBatchVoteItem` returns `{skip}` so a multi-question wrapper Submit can't double-claim.
  - **Staged (Ōēź1 plus-one added, single-question poll):** `limitedSupplyStaged` (in `PollDetailPage`) flips `useWrapperSubmit` true ŌåÆ `wrapperHandlesSubmit` true ŌåÆ QuestionBallot's `supplySelectionMode`. The tap now only SELECTS claim-vs-decline (no submit); the ballot renders the two as a selector (claim selected by default) and the wrapper renders an explicit **"Claim N spots"** / **"Decline"** Submit that commits with the plus-ones attached. Mirrors the yes/no-with-plus-ones staging precedent. `handleVoteClick` routes limited_supply to immediate `submitVote()` (no confirm modal ŌĆö the wrapper Submit IS the confirmation, like time). The name gate runs at the wrapper Submit (`gateOnName`), so the selection tap doesn't gate. After committing, the ballot shows the outcome + a "Change my response" affordance (`onEdit` ŌåÆ `setIsEditingVote(true)`) that re-reveals the Submit. The count for the label comes from a reactive `plusOnesCount` prop (distinct from the `getPlusOnes` getter read at submit time); `wrapperSubmitLabel` bakes the head count in ("Claim 3 spots"), so the wrapper SKIPS its generic " for N" suffix for limited_supply.
  - **`getPlusOnes` is threaded into QuestionBallot's `submitVote`** so the self-submit/single-question-wrapper paths carry plus-ones on the atomic POST (multi-question polls carry them via the wrapper's own `confirmPollSubmit`). This also fixed a latent gap where single-question non-yes_no polls (e.g. a single time poll) dropped plus-ones on the wrapper-Submit path.
  - The ballot shows live "N of M spots left" / "Full ┬Ę K waitlisted", the viewer's own secured/waitlist status (matched by their own vote's `created_at` against the roster), and the signup roster (one row per person, including plus-ones). The committed-status JSX is factored into one `committedStatus` const shared by the staged-post-vote, self-submit-claim, and self-submit-decline branches.
- **Name visibility is a per-question toggle** ("Show who claimed", `reveal_claimant_names`, default true). When OFF, only the creator sees names; other viewers get an anonymized roster (positions/counts, "Spot taken"/"Waiting", own row ŌåÆ "You"). Enforced **server-side**: `_compute_results(..., reveal_names=)` nulls each claim's `name` + sets `names_hidden=true`; `get_results` (per-question) and `polls_for_poll_ids` (bulk/warm-cache) both compute `reveal_names = reveal_claimant_names OR viewer_user_id == poll.creator_user_id`. `created_at` is kept even when hidden so the FE can still identify the viewer's OWN row. `_SELECT_QUESTION_FULL` surfaces `poll_creator_user_id` for this check.
- **Group-card pill** (`CompactSupplyPreview`): "N/M claimed" or "Full" (green when full/closed). Uses counts only ŌĆö names are never on the card ŌĆö so the name toggle doesn't affect it. Falls back to `question.supply_count` when no results have loaded so a fresh poll still reads "0/N".
- **Not auto-closed when full** (deliberate ŌĆö the waitlist keeps collecting so drops can promote). Tests: `server/tests/test_limited_supply.py`.
- **OPEN QUESTIONS ŌĆö RESOLVED (owner confirmed June 2026: keep current behavior on all of them):** (a) **keep collecting a waitlist when full** (does NOT auto-close ŌĆö so dropped/declined claims promote the next waitlister); (b) **keep the explicit "No thanks" decline** (non-claim is not treated as an implicit decline); (d) **name-visibility toggle defaults to visible** (`reveal_claimant_names` default true). **(c) per-person multi-slot claims ŌĆö RESOLVED earlier:** done via plus-ones (see the "Multi-slot claims" + "Two submit modes" bullets above); not a quantity stepper. The whole limited-supply spec is now locked ŌĆö no open design questions remain.
- **Name gate (SHIPPED):** a nameless user tapping a self-submitting ballot (limited_supply Claim/Decline, OR a binary 2-option ranked-choice card) would otherwise hit the server's `400 "name is required"` (surfaced as a raw vote error). These taps auto-submit and bypass the wrapper-Submit name gate, so `QuestionBallot` takes an optional `onRequireName?: (retry) => boolean` prop that `handleSupplyClaim`/`handleSupplyDecline` AND `handleBinaryChoiceTap` (first-time auto-submit only ŌĆö the edit case stages through the gated wrapper Submit) consult before firing the deferred submit; `PollDetailPage` passes its `gateOnName` to **every** ballot (not scoped to a type ŌĆö the prop is only consumed by the self-submitting tap paths, so it's a no-op elsewhere; yes/no's self-submit is gated separately via `dispatchYesNoTap`). The gate stashes the tap as a retry and replays it once `AccountGateModal` saves a name ŌĆö `submitVote`'s existing `getUserName()` fallback then picks up the freshly-saved name. The prop is the canonical hook for any future self-submitting ballot type that needs the name gate; don't re-inline a getUserName check in the handler, and pass `gateOnName` unconditionally rather than re-adding a per-type ternary. **Pitfall fixed (private-browser "Failed to submit vote"):** the binary RC tap path was originally missed ŌĆö `handleBinaryChoiceTap` never called `onRequireName` and `PollDetailPage` scoped the prop to `limited_supply` only, so an anonymous viewer with no saved name (e.g. opening a shared link in a private browser) auto-submitted with `voter_name: null` and got the 400.

### Showtime Question Type (migration 140)

A `showtime` poll behaves like a `time` poll but the options are **concrete movie showtimes** (curated by the creator from real Alamo Drafthouse data) instead of generated 15-minute slots. Voters mark each curated showtime **want / neutral / can't-attend** (a time-preference ballot where red = "can't attend"); winner = **max attendance (fewest can't-attend) ŌåÆ max likes (want) ŌåÆ earliest**. Full spec: `docs/showtime-poll-plan.md`. Scope: Alamo only, no self-healing (v1).

- **Vote storage REUSES the time shape ŌĆö NO new columns.** Migration 140 only adds `'showtime'` to the 3 CHECK constraints (`questions_question_type_check`, `votes_vote_type_check`, `vote_structure_valid` ŌĆö the showtime vote branch is just `yes_no_choice IS NULL`, mirroring `time`). Reactions live in the existing `votes.liked_slots` ("want") / `disliked_slots` ("can't"). No availability phase, no slot generation, no min-participants/exclusion machinery ŌĆö options arrive pre-finalized at create time. `_insert_question` already gates the time-only columns (`day_time_windows`, `min_availability_percent`, etc.) on `== time`, so showtime gets them None/0 for free; `_finalize_time_slots` in `create_poll` is gated on `== time` so showtime skips it. **`allow_plus_ones` defaults ON** for showtime (group outings), like time ŌĆö set in BOTH `routers/polls.py: create_poll` AND `app/create-poll/page.tsx: pollHasPlusOneDefaultType` (keep in sync).
- **Winner reuses `_pick_winner_from_reactions` verbatim** ŌĆö `algorithms/showtime.py: calculate_showtime_results(options, votes)` returns `{winner, like_counts, dislike_counts, attendance_counts}` where `attendance_counts[opt] = total preference-respondent weight ŌłÆ dislike weight` (attendance-max ŌēĪ dislike-min). Plus-one weighting flows through `vote_weight`. `_compute_results` has a `showtime` branch; `vote_validation` accepts showtime like time. `QuestionResultsResponse.attendance_counts` is the only new results field.
- **Option-key format = the time slot key** `"YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM-HH:MM"` (end = start + runtime) so `parse_slot_key` + `lib/timeUtils.ts` parsers/sorters work unchanged. Rich data (cinema, format, seats, poster, session_id, sales_url) lives in `options_metadata[key]`.
  - **Cross-cinema key collisions are real and MUST be disambiguated** ŌĆö two cinemas showing the same movie at the same start time + runtime produce the identical key (the format omits cinema/format on purpose so the shared parsers work), which both crashes React (duplicate key) and collides in `options_metadata`/vote refs. `alamo.py: group_by_film` ŌåÆ `_disambiguate_keys` nudges the END minute (+1m, mod 24h) per collision: the START + date (which drive the chronological winner sort + the displayed time) stay exact; only the rarely-shown end/runtime label shifts a minute. `ShowtimeBubbles` also keys React on `${key}#${idx}` as defense-in-depth. Don't append a space/`@`/`-` suffix to the key ŌĆö it breaks `parse_slot_key`'s `split(" ")` / `split("-")` / `_time_to_minutes`.
- **Data layer = `server/services/showtimes/` + `server/data/alamo_cinemas.json`.** Alamo has no official API; two unauthenticated JSON feeds are joined + a static cinema directory (coords/tz ŌĆö neither feed carries coordinates):
  - **Sessions (legacy)** `feeds.drafthouse.com/adcService/showtimes.svc/market/{marketId}/` (NOTE trailing slash ŌĆö bare path 307-redirects) ŌåÆ `MarketŌåÆDatesŌåÆCinemasŌåÆFilmsŌåÆSeriesŌåÆFormatsŌåÆSessions`; carries runtime, seats, format names, cinema names. Forward window is ~60 days for populated markets (NOT the ~2 days the plan feared).
  - **Catalog (modern)** `drafthouse.com/s/mother/v2/schedule/market/{marketSlug}` ŌåÆ posters (joined on the film slug); catalog also carries sessions but we take posters only. `SessionSalesURL` is usually empty ŌåÆ derive `https://drafthouse.com/ticketing/{SessionId}` (verified 200).
  - **Directory** (`alamo_cinemas.json`): `{cinema_id, slug, name, market_id, market_slug, lat, lng, timezone}`. The `cinema_id` is `00xx` for Austin (market `0000`), `07xx` for DFW (market `0700`, slug `dfw`). **Market IDs are NOT sequential** ŌĆö most numeric ids return `null`; enumerate by probing (the legacy feed's `Market.MarketName/MarketSlug` confirms). **Adding a metro = drop its cinemas into this JSON** (the legacy feed gives id/name/slug/tz; lat/lng are the only manual part). `ShowtimeSource` protocol (`alamo.py`) is the seam for other chains later ŌĆö don't build them now.
  - `cache.py` ŌĆö per-(market, fetch_date) TTL disk+memory cache mirroring `search.py`'s favicon cache (atomic `NamedTemporaryFile`+`os.replace`); `SHOWTIME_CACHE_PATH` env. Ōēż1 upstream fetch/day/market. `_haversine_miles` (from `routers/search.py`) is the radius filter against the directory.
- **`GET /api/showtimes/nearby?lat&lng&radius&days=21`** (`routers/showtimes.py`, dedicated router ŌĆö heavy cached catalog, not a per-keystroke proxy; identity-free like `/preview`). Resolves in-radius cinemas ŌåÆ fetches their distinct markets **concurrently** (`asyncio.gather`) ŌåÆ filters to in-radius + horizon ŌåÆ groups by film. Returns `{reference, horizon_days, cinemas:[{cinema_id,name,slug,distance_miles,has_sessions}] (distance-sorted), films:[{film_id,name,year,rating,runtime,poster_url,sessions:[{key,session_id,cinema_id,cinema_name,cinema_slug,date,time,datetime,format,seats_left,sales_url}]}]}`. The FE loads it ONCE then filters/curates client-side. Rewrites added in `next.config.ts`. `lib/api/showtimes.ts: apiShowtimesNearby`.
- **Create flow = `app/create-poll/ShowtimeCreateFlow.tsx`** (rendered in the create-poll modal top card when `category === 'showtime'`): reference location + radius gate ŌåÆ **theater-selection step** (the in-radius `cinemas` list, nearest-first, distance in blue, round checkboxes; Ōēź1 must be selected) ŌåÆ filterable movie picker (only films playing at selected theaters; counts update with selection) ŌåÆ `DaysSelector inline compact allowedDays` ŌåÆ per-day `ShowtimeBubbles` curation (filtered to selected theaters). Writes back `options` (curated keys) + `options_metadata` + `forField` (= film name ŌåÆ "Showtime for {Film}" auto-title). `selectedCinemas`/`selectedFilmId`/curated are ephemeral component state (catalog re-fetched on reopen; `QuestionDraft.showtimeFilmId` persists the pick). **The create-form inline gates exclude showtime** (`isSuggestionMode`, `inlineFormIsRankedChoice`, `showOptionsCard`, the Context/Collect-Suggestions rows) AND **include it** in `pollHasPlusOneDefaultType` ŌĆö so the bottom card shows only Voting Cutoff + plus-ones (ON) + Emoji, like limited_supply. When adding a new bottom-card setting, gate it on `pollHasRankedChoice`/`pollHasPrephase` (both exclude showtime) ŌĆö don't gate on a bare `category !== 'yes_no'` exclusion list.
- **Ballot = `components/QuestionBallot/ShowtimeBallotSection.tsx`** (early-return branch in `QuestionBallot`, like limited_supply): single-phase tri-state over `question.options` via `ShowtimeBubbles mode="vote"`, want/neutral/can't, wrapper Submit + name gate + plus-ones (showtime is NOT in `SELF_SUBMIT_TYPES`, so it's wrapper-owned like time/ranked_choice). `voteDataBuilders.ts` has a `showtime` case (liked/disliked, `vote_type:'showtime'`). `submitVote` commits immediately (no confirm modal, like time). Committed reactions restore on edit (the `showtime` branch in the vote-data restore effect). Results fetch gate includes showtime.
- **`ShowtimeBubbles` (`components/ShowtimeBubbles.tsx`)** ŌĆö day-grouped flex-wrap of arbitrary-minute bubbles (time + format┬Ęcinema + seats), deliberately NOT routed through `expandHourRowsToQuarters` (that snaps to :00/:15/:30/:45; real showtimes aren't on 15-min boundaries). Two modes share the layout: `curate` (2-state include/exclude) + `vote` (3-state want/neutral/can't, with a legend). `disabled` = read-only. Tap-cycling only ŌĆö the lasso drag-to-select range from `TimeSlotBubbles` is NOT reused (deliberate v1 simplification). `slotsFromOptions(options, metadata)` (exported here) is the shared builder for `options + options_metadata ŌåÆ ShowtimeSlot[]` used by the ballot + results.
- **Results = `ShowtimeResults` (closed: winner showtime + cinema/format + "N can attend ┬Ę M want" + ticketing link, then the disabled bubble grid) + `CompactShowtimePreview` (group-card winner-time pill, green closed / blue open)** in `QuestionResults.tsx`; wired into `GroupCardItem.plainResultForQuestion`. `­¤Ä¼` icon via `QUESTION_TYPE_SYMBOLS.showtime` + `getQuestionLabel` ("Showtime") + `_QUESTION_TYPE_SYMBOLS`/`_CATEGORY_LABELS` (server). Showtime is a `BUILT_IN_TYPES` entry (­¤Ä¼), gated OUT of `isAutocompleteCategory` (catalog-sourced picker, not per-option Nominatim).
- **Demo caveat:** a CLOSED showtime poll is hidden from a fresh viewer by the closed-before-join filter (a screenshot browser "joins now"), so demo with OPEN polls or a sign-in link to the creator. Push delivery / results-as-anonymous can't be screenshot; the winner math is covered by `test_showtime_poll.py`. Tests: `server/tests/test_showtimes_adapter.py` (adapter join/dedup/radius against a real-payload fixture, no live network) + `test_showtime_poll.py` (algorithm + create/vote/winner over the DB).

### Time Question Type

- **Two-phase flow**: availability phase (voters submit `voter_day_time_windows`) ŌåÆ preferences phase (voters submit `liked_slots`/`disliked_slots` after cutoff). When the poll wrapper has `allow_pre_ranking !== false` (the default), the preferences phase opens for each voter as soon as they've submitted availability ŌĆö they don't wait for the cutoff. See "Pre-ranking for time polls" below.
- **Time ballots submit immediately on Submit ŌĆö NO confirmation modal (both phases).** `QuestionBallot.handleVoteClick` short-circuits to `void submitVote()` for `question_type === 'time'` (after all validation, including the availability-window overlap check) instead of opening `showVoteConfirmModal`. Yes/No and ranked-choice keep their confirm modal. **Pitfall this exposed (fixed):** removing the modal removed the incidental render cycle that let the wrapper's `externalVoterName` prop catch up. The wrapper (`PollDetailPage`) computes `savedUserName = getUserName()` at render time and passes it as `externalVoterName`; when a nameless user submits, `AccountGateModal.onSubmit` `saveUserName`s then SYNCHRONOUSLY replays the submit via `triggerSubmit()` ŌåÆ `handleVoteClick` ŌåÆ `submitVote()` before React re-renders, so the prop is still the stale `""` ŌåÆ server 400 "Voter name is required". Fix: `submitVote`'s `trimmedVoterName` falls back to `getUserName()?.trim()` when the prop-derived `voterName` is empty (the same source the name-gate verified). Any future "submit synchronously right after a localStorage write" path that reads a render-time-snapshotted prop needs the same fresh-read fallback ŌĆö the prop won't reflect the write until the next render.
- **Slot finalization at cutoff**: `_finalize_time_slots()` runs at availability cutoff, applies the **"Minimum Participants" viability gate** (`filter_slots_by_min_participants()` ŌĆö keeps slots that at least `time_min_participants` people can attend, default 2), deduplicates via `_keep_longest_per_start_time()`, and writes the surviving slots to `question.options`. When availability WAS collected but no slot met the gate it instead sets `options='[]'` + `time_event_cancelled=true` ("event's off"). The shared `_compute_candidate_time_slots(question, votes) ŌåÆ (slots, has_availability)` (in `server/services/questions.py`) is used both here AND for the pre-ranking tentative-slots path; the returned `has_availability` bool is what lets `_finalize_time_slots` distinguish "no slot cleared the bar ŌåÆ cancel" from "nobody submitted availability yet ŌåÆ don't cancel, keep all creator slots" without re-scanning votes. See "Minimum Participants" below for the full model. (The legacy relative `filter_slots_by_min_availability()` / `min_availability_percent` column survive for back-compat but no longer drive finalization for new polls.)
- **Pre-ranking for time polls (`allow_pre_ranking` on `polls`).** When set (default true), voters can react to candidate slots before the availability cutoff. `_compute_results` returns the dynamically-computed candidate list as `options` with `options_are_tentative=true`; the FE `questionResults.options_are_tentative` flag drives the new `isAvailabilitySubmission` derived state in `QuestionBallot.tsx`. Voter UX is sequential: availability form ŌåÆ submit ŌåÆ bubble UI with tentative slots ŌåÆ submit preferences ŌåÆ summary. The slot list shifts as more voters submit availability; likes/dislikes the voter cast on slots that subsequently get eliminated remain in their vote row but are silently ignored by the winner algorithm (only slots in `question.options` after finalization count). To edit availability after submitting, voters Forget the question and redo (no separate "Edit availability" affordance in this iteration). Disable the toggle to restore the old "wait for cutoff" behavior. Three load-bearing pieces of plumbing:
  - **`include_tentative_time_options` kwarg on `_compute_results`** (`server/services/questions.py`) ŌĆö defaults `True` (per-question results endpoint), but the bulk `polls_for_poll_ids` path (`/api/groups/mine` + `/by-route-id/{id}`, on a 5s page refresh tick) passes `False` to skip the slot-generation pass. Without this gate, every active group tab with N time polls triggers `_compute_candidate_time_slots` for each poll twice every 5s ŌĆö the algorithm is O(days ├Ś windows ├Ś durations ├Ś starts ├Ś voters) and dominates server CPU on the hot loop. The per-question `/api/questions/<id>/results` call still populates tentative options for the ballot UI; `QuestionBallot`'s `apiGetQuestionResults` cache write merges in.
  - **`isAvailabilitySubmission` vs `inAvailabilityPhase`** (`QuestionBallot.tsx`) ŌĆö pair of distinct concepts that USED to be one boolean. `inAvailabilityPhase` is the wrapper-level "slots aren't finalized yet" gate that drives the "Collecting Availability" status label and the tentative-slots amber notice. `isAvailabilitySubmission` is the per-voter active-form gate: true while filling the availability inputs, false while reacting to tentative bubbles. Both flow through to `TimeBallotSection`; the summary header label, the input-vs-bubble JSX fork, and `voteDataBuilders` all switch on `isAvailabilitySubmission`. `BallotInputs.isAvailabilitySubmission` in `voteDataBuilders.ts` is the renamed field (was `inAvailabilityPhase`) ŌĆö keeps the wire-format decision local to the builder.
  - **Inline `setUserVoteData(v)` on first-time submits, not just edits** (`QuestionBallot.tsx: submitVote` + `prepareBatchVoteItem.commit`). Was `if (isEditing) setUserVoteData(v)`. Pre-ranking time flow reads `userVoteData.voter_day_time_windows` synchronously to derive `hasSubmittedAvailability`, which feeds `isAvailabilitySubmission`. Without the inline write, the first-time-submit path leaves `userVoteData` null until the loadVoteData useEffect re-fetches ŌĆö causing a one-cycle flash through the "Your availability:" summary before the bubble UI lands. The companion `await fetchQuestionResults()` after submission (gated on `time + inAvailabilityPhase + allow_pre_ranking !== false`) lands the tentative options in the same paint cycle.
- **`components/TimeQuestionFields.tsx` is now exclusively voter-facing and renders NO day-picker.** The create-poll form inlines `DayTimeWindowsInput`/`DaysSelector` directly (the creator defines the days); `TimeQuestionFields` is only mounted by `QuestionBallot/TimeBallotSection.tsx` (active availability form + the read-only submitted-availability summary). A voter replies *within* the creator-defined days, so the old "Select Days / Add/Remove Days" button + its `DaysSelector` were removed ŌĆö voters toggle availability via the per-window checkboxes (`isVoterForm` branch in `DayTimeWindowsInput`, gated on a truthy `questionWindows`) but can't add or remove days. The `highlightDaysButton` prop went with it; `renderDaysSection` still gates the label + day rows. Don't reintroduce a day-picker here ŌĆö if a creator-side embedded use ever returns, render the picker at that call site, not inside the voter component.
- **`TimeWindow.enabled?: boolean`** in `lib/types.ts` is the per-window "on/off" toggle the voter form writes. **The availability algorithms (FE `isVoterAvailableForSlot` + server `_voter_available_at`) do NOT read it.** Disabled windows must be stripped before submission, AND the day must be dropped if all its windows are disabled ŌĆö leaving an empty `windows` array on a day means "all day available" per the helper's contract, which silently inverts the voter's "I'm NOT available" intent. The `voteDataBuilders.ts` time-availability branch handles both filters; mirror the pattern in any future direct-submit path. Submit-button disabled-state gating also reads `w.enabled !== false` so an all-unchecked state surfaces as a disabled CTA rather than silently sending null availability.
- **"Minimum Participants" viability gate (migration 129) ŌĆö RESOLVES the old min-availability-model TODO.** Replaces the relative `min_availability_percent` % filter with a single, intuitive per-slot **viability gate**: a time slot counts only if at least `time_min_participants` people are available for it (default **2**). At the availability cutoff, slots below the threshold are dropped; if NO slot clears the bar the poll resolves to an explicit **"event's off"** terminal state (`time_event_cancelled=true`, `options=[]`) rather than a thin/empty ballot. The owner converged on this (the per-slot viability-gate interpretation, plain absolute count, explicit cancel) after comparing three prototype variants on separate dev servers (split filter+gate / single headcount / min-max range ŌĆö all retired). Wiring:
  - **Schema (migration 129):** `questions.time_min_participants INTEGER` + `questions.time_event_cancelled BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT false`. The old `min_availability_percent` column + `filter_slots_by_min_availability()` survive for back-compat but no longer drive new-poll finalization.
  - **Gate only applies once availability is collected.** `_compute_candidate_time_slots` skips the gate (keeps all creator slots) when no vote carries `voter_day_time_windows` ŌĆö otherwise an availability-phase-off poll (finalized at create with zero votes) or a phase that closed empty would cancel everything (every count is 0 < 2). This rule lives in ONE place: the function returns `(slots, has_availability)` so `_finalize_time_slots` cancels iff `has_availability and not slots` without re-scanning.
  - **Display: results-level flag only.** `time_event_cancelled` rides `QuestionResultsResponse` (+ `toQuestionResults` + FE `QuestionResults`); `TimeResults` shows a "No time works ŌĆö the event's off" banner and `CompactTimePreview` shows an "Event's off" pill. It is deliberately NOT surfaced on the per-question read path (`QuestionResponse`/`Question`) ŌĆö nothing consumes it there; `time_min_participants` IS on the question read path (duplicate-restore). The results branch reads `time_event_cancelled` straight off the question DB row (`p.*`), independent of `QuestionResponse`.
  - **FE create form:** a single "Minimum Participants" row (`<CompactNumberRow>`) in the bottom settings card, in the same slot "Minimum Votes" occupies for ranked_choice, gated on `showTimeFields && collectAvailability`. Draft field `QuestionDraft.minParticipants` (default 2) ŌåÆ API `min_participants` (`server/models.py: CreateQuestionRequest.min_participants: int = 2`) ŌåÆ `questions.time_min_participants`. The old "Minimum Availability %" card + `MinimumParticipationModal` are deleted.
  - **`<CompactNumberRow>` (`components/CompactNumberRow.tsx`)** is the shared label-+-tap-to-edit-number settings row, used by BOTH "Minimum Votes" (`CompactMinResponsesField`, which adds the "Show Results After Min Votes" toggle below it) and "Minimum Participants". Reuse it for any new numeric settings row rather than re-inlining the isEditing/inputRef edit-toggle.
  - **Auto-closed on cancel (SHIPPED).** When a poll's ENTIRE content is a cancelled time event, it auto-closes (`close_reason='cancelled'`) so the closed-gated "event's off" banner (`TimeResults`) surfaces. `services/questions.py: _maybe_close_cancelled_event_poll(conn, poll_id, now)` is the shared primitive ŌĆö it closes iff every question is a `time` question AND every one is `time_event_cancelled` (so a multi-question poll with any non-time or uncancelled-time section stays open; the single-question time poll, the common case, closes). Called from BOTH the inline `cutoff-availability` endpoint (fires the poll-CLOSED push inline, sets `close_notified=true`, instead of a "voting is open" transition push) AND the cron tick's transition pass (excludes the cancelled poll from the transition-push loop; its close push fires the NEXT tick via step 2's un-notified-close claim, since the cancel-close happens after step 2 already ran that tick). `close_reason='cancelled'` is a new value stored on `polls.close_reason` (plain TEXT, no CHECK constraint; the FE treats `close_reason` as `string | null` and only switches on `manual`/`max_capacity`/`deadline`, so `cancelled` falls through harmlessly). The legacy per-question GET-read finalize path (`routers/questions.py`) is deliberately NOT auto-closed ŌĆö closing as a side effect of a read would be surprising + inconsistent (only the tick + cutoff endpoint are deadline actors). Tests: `test_notification_events.py::test_cutoff_availability_cancels_unviable_event` + `::test_tick_cancels_unviable_time_event`. (The compact "Event's off" pill shows regardless of closed.)
  - **Seeding a time-poll demo via API (lesson):** the availability phase needs BOTH the poll-level `prephase_deadline_minutes` (arms the clock) AND the question-level `suggestion_deadline_minutes` (marks the question as having a phase) ŌĆö sending only the question-level one makes `cutoff-availability` 400 with "No availability phase to cut off" (mirrors `social_tests/conftest.py: create_poll`, which injects the poll-level value when a question carries the per-question one). To demonstrate "event's off": give the creator one wide window + duration, then have several voters each available at DISJOINT single slots so no slot reaches 2.
  - **Tests:** `server/tests/test_time_poll.py: TestFilterSlotsByMinParticipants`.
- **"Attendance Leeway" (exclusion tolerance, migration 138).** Creator-set integer (default **0**) controlling how many fewer attendees than the best-attended slot a time may have and still reach the preference phase. A slot survives iff `max_attendance ŌłÆ slot_attendance Ōēż tolerance`. Tolerance 0 ŌåÆ only the best-attended slot(s) are offered for preference voting (so the flexible-majority's availability decides, and preferences just break ties among the best slots ŌĆö this is what makes "everyone marks availability, nobody bothers with preferences" produce the best-attended time instead of the *earliest* one, which was the old `_pick_winner_from_reactions` failure mode). Raising it widens the field so a slightly-less-attended-but-otherwise-preferable slot can stay in the running. Wiring:
  - **Schema (migration 138):** `questions.exclusion_tolerance INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0`. Rides every question read path (`p.*` ŌåÆ `_row_to_question` ŌåÆ `QuestionResponse.exclusion_tolerance` ŌåÆ `toQuestion` ŌåÆ FE `Question.exclusion_tolerance`); set on INSERT in `routers/polls.py` (clamped `max(0, ŌĆ”)`, 0 for non-time questions to satisfy NOT NULL).
  - **Algorithm:** `filter_slots_by_exclusion_tolerance(slots, availability_counts, tolerance)` (`algorithms/time_question.py`), applied in `_compute_candidate_time_slots` **AFTER** `filter_slots_by_min_participants` ŌĆö the absolute viability gate decides whether the event happens at all (and "event's off"); leeway only *narrows* the surviving field. The best slot always survives (`max ŌłÆ max = 0 Ōēż tolerance`), so it never empties a non-empty list. Because `_compute_candidate_time_slots` feeds BOTH `_finalize_time_slots` (persists `options`) and the pre-ranking tentative-slots path, the filter applies live + at cutoff with no extra code.
  - **FE create form:** a second `<CompactNumberRow label="Attendance Leeway">` directly under "Minimum Participants", same `showTimeFields && collectAvailability` gate, `min={0}`. Draft field `QuestionDraft.exclusionTolerance` (default 0) ŌåÆ `draftToQuestionParams` ŌåÆ API `exclusion_tolerance`. Persisted in `questionFormState`; carried through the duplicate flow (`buildQuestionSnapshot` now also includes it AND `time_min_participants` ŌĆö the latter was a pre-existing dead read fixed in passing).
  - **Inline Ōōś via `CompactNumberRow.labelInfo` (new prop).** `CompactNumberRow` gained an optional `labelInfo?: ReactNode` rendered as a **sibling of** the `<label>` (not a child ŌĆö so the info button's own click never triggers the labelŌåÆinput association). The leeway row passes `<OutcomeInfoButton align="left" text="ŌĆ”" />` (the codebase's existing grey inline-info popover, reused rather than a bespoke modal).
  - **Display: orange "excludes N" badge is ABSOLUTE, not relative.** Per slot the badge shows how many availability respondents that slot leaves out ŌĆö `availability_respondents ŌłÆ availability_counts[slot]` ŌĆö so **even the best-attended slot shows its real exclusion** (the owner's explicit requirement: "indicate that the best slot still excludes n people"). Both the preference ballot (`TimeSlotBubbles.excludedCount`) and the results page (`QuestionResults: TimeResults`, per-cell `unavailable` + the "X of Y available" winner line) use the respondent total as the denominator. **`QuestionResults.availability_respondents`** (new field, migration-free) = the weighted headcount of everyone who submitted availability (submitter + plus-ones); computed in `calculate_time_question_results`, rides `QuestionResultsResponse` ŌåÆ `toQuestionResults` ŌåÆ FE `QuestionResults`. Both renderers fall back to `max_availability` (the old relative baseline) when the field is absent (pre-deploy cached results). NOTE: because the badge is absolute, it is NO LONGER equal to the configured leeway value ŌĆö leeway gates which slots *survive* (relative, `max ŌłÆ count Ōēż tolerance`), the badge *displays* absolute exclusion (`respondents ŌłÆ count`); the two are intentionally different numbers.
  - **Tests:** `server/tests/test_time_poll.py: TestFilterSlotsByExclusionTolerance`.
- **Per-voter "minimum participants" = conditional attendance (migration 130).** A time RESPONDENT can attach a personal turnout threshold to their availability ("only count me for a slot if at least N people total are available"). It's the per-voter mirror of the creator's gate above and composes with it. The owner chose the "conditional attendance" semantics over an aggregated-preference or informational-only reading.
  - **Algorithm: `compute_slot_availability` returns EFFECTIVE counts** (`server/algorithms/time_question.py`). For each slot it gathers the available voters' thresholds (`_voter_threshold`, default **1** = no constraint) and resolves a fixed point via **`_effective_attendance(thresholds)`** = the largest k such that Ōēź k voters have a threshold Ōēż k (sort ascending; max k where `s[k-1] <= k`). Dropping a voter from a slot lowers the count, which can push another voter below their threshold, cascading ŌĆö this is the closed-form of the greedy-removal fixed point (verified against a brute-force reference over 20k random cases in `TestEffectiveAttendance`). All-default thresholds (1) reduce to the prior raw count, so existing polls are unaffected. The creator's viability gate (`filter_slots_by_min_participants`) then runs against these effective counts, so the two compose; and the displayed "X of Y available" + winner use effective counts. The like/dislike winner tiebreak is intentionally NOT changed (a dropped voter's preference on a surviving slot still counts ŌĆö v1 scope; the threshold drives viability/availability, not the preference aggregation).
  - **Schema (migration 130):** `votes.voter_min_participants INTEGER` (nullable; NULL = no constraint). Threaded through `SubmitVoteRequest`/`EditVoteRequest`/`PollVoteItem`/`VoteResponse`, the insert/edit SQL (written directly, NOT COALESCEd ŌĆö the preferences-phase edit re-sends it from `userVoteData`, same reasoning as `voter_day_time_windows`), `_row_to_vote`, the `_finalize_time_slots` votes SELECT (must list it explicitly ŌĆö that query doesn't `SELECT *`), and the `_vote_item_to_{submit,edit}_req` converters. All time votes go through `apiSubmitPollVotes`, so the builders in `voteDataBuilders.ts` are the single FE emit point.
  - **FE: NO on/off toggle.** A `<CompactNumberRow>` "Minimum people for me to come" in the availability ballot (`TimeBallotSection`). The value itself encodes the constraint (the owner rejected a `SliderSwitch` as redundant). **Floored at the creator's poll minimum** (`time_min_participants`, "the original min") ŌĆö a personal min below that is meaningless since the slot already requires it. `QuestionBallot` computes `pollMinParticipants = Math.max(1, question.time_min_participants ?? 2)`, seeds the field default to it, passes it as the field `min` (`voterMinParticipantsFloor`), and **sends `voter_min_participants` only when the value is strictly above the floor** (else null = no extra constraint). Persisted in the ballot draft (`voterMinParticipantsValue`) and restored from the committed vote (only when `> floor`).
- **`<CompactNumberRow>` can be backspaced to empty while editing.** The edit input holds a local string `draft` (seeded from `value` on edit-start) so it can sit empty mid-type without snapping back to the old number ŌĆö valid in-range values live-commit via `setValue`, but an empty / below-`min` draft leaves the committed value alone until **`commit()` (blur / Enter) clamps it UP to `min`**. This is the canonical "clear-and-retype + auto-correct-to-floor" behavior and applies to every `CompactNumberRow` (creator Minimum Votes / Minimum Participants too). Don't reintroduce the old "controlled `value={value}` number input that ignores empty onChange" form ŌĆö it made the field impossible to clear.
- **Preference-phase bubbles must be filtered per-voter by their availability.** A voter who said they can't attend a slot in the availability phase should not see (or be able to react to) that slot in the preferences phase. `preferenceSlotsForVoter` in `QuestionBallot.tsx` runs `isVoterAvailableForSlot()` (from `lib/timeUtils.ts`) against the loaded `userVoteData.voter_day_time_windows` and passes the filtered list to `TimeSlotBubbles`. Voters who never submitted availability see every finalized slot.
- **`null` vs `[]` semantics for liked/disliked slots**: `null` = voter hasn't submitted preferences yet; `[]` = submitted with all bubbles neutral. The frontend uses this distinction to show an implicit edit prompt (hasNotReactedYet).
- **Preferences-phase vote edits MUST re-send `voter_day_time_windows` + `voter_duration`.** `_edit_vote_on_question` writes both columns directly (not `COALESCE`d), because the same NULL-on-the-wire value carries two different meanings: in the availability phase it means "clear my availability" (abstain edit), but in the preferences phase the FE just leaves the field out of its UI. Symptom of forgetting: a voter who submits availability in phase 1, then submits preferences in phase 2, ends up with `voter_day_time_windows = NULL` because the phase-2 edit overwrote it ŌĆö `compute_slot_availability` then returns 0 for every slot (winner is still picked from likes/dislikes, but the displayed "X of Y available" reads "0 of 0"). The fix lives in the FE: `voteDataBuilders.ts` preferences-phase branch reads `state.userVoteData?.voter_day_time_windows` / `voter_duration` and passes them through, so the SQL UPDATE writes the existing values back (effective no-op). Don't try to fix this with `COALESCE` server-side ŌĆö that breaks the legitimate availability-phase abstain flow.
- **`TimeBallotSection` post-submit summary must skip the `hasVoted && !isEditingVote` branch when the voter has not reacted yet.** A voter who submitted availability in phase 1 transitions into phase 2 with `hasVoted=true` but `liked_slots/disliked_slots` still `null`. Without an explicit gate, the post-submit summary's ternary chain falls through to `null` ŌĆö leaving `"Your preferences:"` sitting above the wrapper Submit with nothing in between. The gate is `const hasNotReactedYet = !inAvailabilityPhase && hasVoted && userVoteData?.liked_slots === null && userVoteData?.disliked_slots === null && !userVoteData?.is_abstain;` and `if (hasVoted && !isEditingVote && !hasNotReactedYet) { ...summary... }`. Falling through renders the active preferences form so the voter can mark slots. Mirrors the parent's `hasNotReactedYet` in `QuestionBallot.tsx:780` (which feeds `canImplicitlyEdit` for the wrapper Submit visibility).
- **Submitted availability is shown by re-rendering `TimeQuestionFields` with `disabled={true}`**, populated from `userVoteData.voter_day_time_windows` and `userVoteData.voter_duration` rather than the active form state (which may have been reset post-submit). Pattern used in the post-submit summary in `components/QuestionBallot/TimeBallotSection.tsx`. Duration callbacks are spread conditionally on `userVoteData.voter_duration` truthiness ŌĆö when the voter didn't constrain duration, omit all four `onDurationXxx` handlers so `TimeQuestionFields`'s "render the duration block only when all callbacks are provided" gate hides it instead of showing `0ŌĆō0` defaults.
- **Submitted PREFERENCES are shown by re-rendering `<TimeSlotBubbles disabled={true}>`, NOT a text list.** The post-vote "Your preferences:" summary (the `hasVoted && !isEditingVote && !hasNotReactedYet` block in `TimeBallotSection.tsx`) renders the same bubble grid the voter used, greyed out, so they see their actual ballot (green/red bubbles + legend) instead of a "Liked: ŌĆ” / Disliked: ŌĆ”" sentence. Tapping the existing `editVoteButton` flips `isEditingVote` ŌåÆ falls through to the interactive instance below. Props mirror the active form EXCEPT: `onToggle={() => {}}` (no-op), `disabled={true}`, and liked/disliked are sourced from the COMMITTED `userVoteData.liked_slots`/`disliked_slots` (the active form sources from in-flight `likedSlots`/`dislikedSlots` state) ŌĆö that divergence is intentional, the two instances render in mutually-exclusive view states. `disabled` mode in `TimeSlotBubbles` already gates every interactive bit (pointer-down returns early, no window listeners, the range-toolbar `ModalPortal` is gated on `!disabled`), so the heavier component is cheap to render read-only. This deliberately parallels the availability-summary pattern above (re-render the real ballot disabled, don't paraphrase it as text). The two `<TimeSlotBubbles>` render sites (disabled summary / enabled form) are kept separate, NOT unified behind a computed `disabled` prop ŌĆö they sit in structurally different branches with different surrounding chrome (header + edit button vs "Mark Your Preferences" + abstain + submit).
- **Closed-state `TimeBallotSection` returns `null` unless the voter abstained.** The parent's closed-state block in `QuestionBallot.tsx:1244-1261` already renders `QuestionResultsDisplay` (the candidate slots) plus loading + "unable to load" fallbacks ŌĆö so `TimeBallotSection`'s own closed branch only needs to add the "You Abstained" badge. An earlier version wrapped its (mostly empty) inner content in `py-6`, leaving ~48px of dead space below the candidate slots whenever the voter wasn't abstaining. When adding new closed-state content for a question type, audit whether the parent already handles it before adding a wrapping section.
- **Time results: heading is "Start Options" (no count) and the slot list is collapsed-by-default with fade + chevron.** `components/QuestionResults.tsx: TimeResults` wraps the day-rows divider div in `<CollapsibleStartOptions>`, which delegates to the shared `<CollapsibleFadeSection>` primitive (collapsed at 80px, 28px fade band). The legend (liked / disliked / unavail.) renders in the always-visible header next to the heading; only the rows themselves collapse. Same UX as the Notes field on a poll card.
- **Winner algorithm**: fewest dislikes ŌåÆ most likes ŌåÆ earliest slot key (chronological tiebreak). Implemented in `_pick_winner_from_reactions()` in `server/algorithms/time_question.py`.
- **Category "Time" in create form**: selecting it from the category dropdown keeps the standard form and injects `ParticipationConditions` + threshold slider + availability cutoff in place of options. Uses a single `{(questionType === 'time' || (questionType === 'question' && category === 'time'))}` condition ŌĆö do NOT add a separate duplicate block for each case.
- **`formatDayLabel(dateStr)`** is the canonical day-label formatter in `lib/timeUtils.ts`. Use it in all time-related components instead of local copies.
- **Shared time-slot helpers** in `lib/timeUtils.ts`: `parseSlotStart`, `parseSlotDate`, `groupSlotsByDay`, `getBubbleLabel` (predecessor-aware compact label returning `{time, period}` ŌĆö see "Time bubble grid layout" below for the case table), `expandHourRowsToQuarters` (pads each hour-row to four `:00/:15/:30/:45` `SlotCell { slot, available }` entries ŌĆö synthetic ghost cells for missing positions use a slot-key WITHOUT an end time, e.g. `${date} 10:00`, distinct from real keys so liked/disliked Set lookups never collide), `periodColorClass(period)` (Tailwind class for AM=orange / PM=purple, used by `TimeSlotBubbles`, `QuestionResults`, AND `DayTimeWindowsInput`'s time-window pills ŌĆö extract before introducing a 5th call site), `formatStackedDayLabel` (stacked weekday / month+day for the bubble grid row label), and `formatTimeSlot` (full "Mon, Apr 28 ŌĆó 10:00 AM ŌĆō 10:30 AM (30m)" label). `TimeSlotBubbles.tsx` (voting ballot) and `QuestionResults.tsx` (results view) both use these ŌĆö never re-implement slot formatting locally.
- **Time bubble grid layout** (`components/TimeSlotBubbles.tsx` + the `QuestionResults` results-view start-options panel). Each day renders three columns: stacked day label (left, `w-12`) | period column (`w-7`, AM/PM badge, orange/purple via `periodColorClass`, empty when this row continues the previous period) | bubble grid (a 2-col CSS grid where col 1 holds the hour-anchor bubble and col 2 holds a `flex flex-wrap` of the minute bubbles, so col-2 wraps stay indented past col 1). One row per hour. Every row carries all four quarter-hour positions; missing positions render at the same `min-w-12 h-8 px-2` footprint but with no border/background + faded text (`text-gray-300 dark:text-gray-600`, `select-none`, `aria-hidden`) ŌĆö ghost cells, so the columns line up vertically across rows. Bubble text uses Geist Mono (`font-mono` Tailwind class ŌåÆ `--font-geist-mono`); single-digit hours are NBSP-padded in `getBubbleLabel` (e.g. `┬Ā 1:00`) so the digit/colon/minute aligns column-by-column with `10:00`/`11:00`/`12:00`. **NBSP, not a regular space**: `white-space: nowrap` still collapses leading regular spaces; NBSP survives. `getBubbleLabel` cases: `:MM` for same-hour-different-minute, `H:MM` for same-period-different-hour, `H:MM` + non-null `period` for first-of-row / period-change. Hour-anchor labels always include `:00` (no bare-hour form) so the format is uniform across the grid. Row-level `period` is read off the first cell's `getBubbleLabel(firstSlot, prevSlot).period`, where `prevSlot` is the previous hour-row's last cell's slot key (use `hourRows[rowIdx-1].at(-1).slot`, NOT a flat-array index ŌĆö the old `hourRows.flat() + flatIdx + cellsWithPrev` orchestration was retired). The shared `SLOT_CELL_SIZE` string lives at module scope inside each consumer so the ghost branch + real branch agree on dimensions. **Per-day `useMemo`** wraps the `groupSlotsByDay + formatStackedDayLabel + expandHourRowsToQuarters` chain keyed on `[options]` ŌĆö keep new transformations inside the same memo rather than re-running per render tick.
- **Slot keys `"YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM-HH:MM"` arrive from the backend already in chronological order.** Consumers that just group by day (`groupSlotsByDay`) do NOT need to re-sort the list first; the old list view only sorted because it reordered by dislikes/likes.
- **Drag-to-select range voting (preferences phase, `components/TimeSlotBubbles.tsx`).** A plain tap still cycles ONE bubble (neutral ŌåÆ liked ŌåÆ disliked ŌåÆ neutral); a DRAG across bubbles selects a contiguous **chronological** range (`options.slice(lo, hi+1)` via an `optionIndex` Map ŌĆö the visual 2D grid is irrelevant, range is by slot order). A drag is distinguished from a tap by an 8px `DRAG_THRESHOLD`. While Ōēź1 slot is selected, a fixed bottom-center toolbar (portaled via `ModalPortal`, so it never reflows the page) offers Like / Dislike / Neutral + a cancel ├Ś; pressing one applies that state to every selected slot (loops the existing `onToggle`) and clears the selection. Selected bubbles get a flush `ring-2 ring-blue-500` (NO `ring-offset` ŌĆö the outline hugs the bubble edge). Key mechanics:
  - **Gesture runs on POINTER events via window listeners, not React handlers.** `onPointerDown` on a bubble records an anchor + adds `window` `pointermove`/`pointerup`/`pointercancel` listeners; touch implicitly captures the pointer to the bubble but the events still bubble to `window`, and `document.elementFromPoint(x,y).closest('[data-slot-available="true"]')` maps the finger position to the hovered bubble (no `setPointerCapture` needed ŌĆö works for mouse + touch). `onClick` was REMOVED; a no-drag `pointerup` calls `handleTap` (keyboard handled separately via `onKeyDown` Enter/Space) ŌĆö so a drag never also fires a stray tap-cycle.
  - **Tap vs drag selection: `setSelection((prev) => prev.size === 0 ? prev : new Set())` on pointerdown** clears any prior selection without a redundant re-render when already empty.
  - **`effectiveSelection = options.filter(s => selection.has(s))`** intersects the live options so a stale selection (slots that vanished as tentative availability shifted) silently drops out; the toolbar gate + apply both read it. After dropping the "N selected" count text, `effectiveSelection` is still load-bearing (gate + apply) ŌĆö don't delete it.
  - **Scroll + swipe-back blocking is scoped to the AVAILABLE bubbles only, not the grid/labels/ghosts.** Each available bubble `<button>` carries `touch-none` (`touch-action: none` ŌåÆ browser won't pan/scroll) AND `onTouchStart/Move/End/Cancel={e => e.stopPropagation()}` (keeps the ancestor `useSwipeBackGesture` React `onTouch*` handlers on PollDetail's `.touch-pan-y` wrapper from seeing the drag ŌåÆ no page-transition). Touch events target the element where the touch STARTED for the whole gesture, so blocking only on the bubble fully covers any drag begun there. Day labels, gaps, the grid container, and greyed-out ghost cells keep `touch-action: auto` so they scroll/swipe normally ŌĆö verified via computed `touch-action` (`none` on bubbles, `auto` elsewhere) + a CDP touch test (rightward drag on a bubble leaves the swipe wrapper `transform: none`; the same drag on a ghost cell produces `translate3d(...)`). `touch-action` alone can't stop the JS swipe handler (it only governs the browser's native pan); the `stopPropagation` is what blocks the gesture, so BOTH are required.
- **Cap-height text centering for bubble labels**: time-slot bubble labels are pure cap-height text (digits, uppercase letters, colons ŌĆö no descenders like g/j/y). `flex items-center` on a `leading-none` line box positions the **line box** at the bubble center, but the visible glyphs sit in the UPPER half of that line box because the space below the baseline is reserved for descenders that never appear ŌĆö so the text looks "too high". Fix: use the modern CSS properties `text-box-trim: trim-both` + `text-box-edge: cap alphabetic` to shrink the text box to exactly the cap-height range, so flex centering aligns the visible glyphs instead of the padded line box. The shared `.cap-height-text` utility class in `app/globals.css` encapsulates the rule; use it on any `<span>` wrapping single-line, descender-free labels inside a centered container. Supported in Chromium 133+ / Safari 18.2+.
- **Availability cutoff requires `suggestion_deadline_minutes` to be set** on the question ŌĆö the endpoint enforces `suggestion_deadline IS NULL AND suggestion_deadline_minutes IS NOT NULL`. Questions created without this field will fail the cutoff endpoint with 400.
- **`ChunkLoadError` after new builds**: the browser has stale cached chunks from the previous build. The lazy `CreateQuestionContent` import and the global `unhandledrejection` handler in `template.tsx` both auto-reload the page when this happens. The service worker uses network-first for JS chunks so new builds take effect immediately.
- **Autotitle convention**: time questions use `"Time?"` as the autotitle (matching the `BUILT_IN_TYPES` label), not a bespoke prompt like "When works?". Every branch of `generateTitle()` in `app/create-question/page.tsx` must call `appendFor(...)` on its return value so the "for X" suffix gets appended ŌĆö the standalone `questionType === 'time'` fallback originally returned a raw string and silently dropped `forSuffix`.

### Day-Time-Windows Input (Creator Form)

- **The `+` button does NOT open the time-grid modal**; it appends a slot in place via `pickNextTimeWindow(targetDay, allDays)` (in `lib/timeUtils.ts`). The algorithm walks chronologically-previous days first (each day's slots tried latest-start first; the first one that doesn't overlap any existing slot on the target day wins), then chronologically-following days under the same rule, then falls back to `DEFAULT_TIME_WINDOW` (`08:00ŌĆō17:00`). The `TimeGridModal` is now an **edit-only** surface ŌĆö `handleEditApply` only handles the `editingIndex !== null` path. The `+ Time` amber-pill fallback for empty days is also gone since new days always inherit windows; if an empty-windows day ever happens, the always-on `+` column adds one.
- **`useDayTimeWindowsState.onWindowsChange` always sorts by start time.** Sorting is the single source of truth for "slots are in chronological order"; every consumer (the per-pill `intersectsPrev` validation, the `+ button`'s smart pick) trusts this. Don't store slots out-of-order anywhere ŌĆö the sort lives in the hook so any new mutation that funnels through `onChange` is covered.
- **`useDayTimeWindowsState.onDaysSelected` inheritance**: a newly-added day's windows come from (1) the in-memory removed-day cache (re-adding a day restores its previous windows), else (2) the chronologically-previous day in the working list (deep-copied so edits don't propagate backward), else (3) `DEFAULT_TIME_WINDOW`. The auto-added "today" entry from `emptyDraft({category: 'time'})` and the parallel path in `app/create-poll/page.tsx` also seed with `DEFAULT_TIME_WINDOW` so the "first day" rule lands even when the day was auto-added.
- **`intersectsPrev` is per-pill validation, not a global error.** The styling is a soft orange outline (`border-orange-400 dark:border-orange-500`) on an otherwise-normal pill ŌĆö read as a hint, not a blocker. Submission is not blocked. The duration-too-short check is a separate, harder error state (`bg-red-50` + red border + red text). Two separate flags fold into a single `pillVariant` selector keyed against `PILL_STATE_CLASSES` (`disabled | tooShort | intersecting | normal`).
- **Layout-stable pill borders: `PILL_BASE` always sets `border` (1 px reserved) + exactly one border-color class appended per pill via `pillBorderClass(variant, isVoterForm)`.** `PILL_STATE_CLASSES` carries ONLY bg/text/hover now ŌĆö NO border-color ŌĆö because the border color is form-aware: `tooShort`/`intersecting` keep their warning colors (red/orange) regardless of form; neutral pills (`normal`/`disabled`) are `border-transparent` in the **creator** form (borderless, composes into the create-poll `divide-y` card) but `border-gray-300 dark:border-gray-600` (a thin outline) in the **voter** form. The voter outline replaces the removed "Select time slots to fine-tune" hint ŌĆö it signals the time-slot bubbles are tappable. **Don't fold the border color back into `PILL_STATE_CLASSES`**: a class string containing both `border-transparent` and `border-gray-300` hits Tailwind's source-order precedence (later-generated class wins, NOT class-attribute order), so the override is unreliable ŌĆö exactly-one-border-color-per-pill is the invariant that avoids it. `pillVariant` only ever returns `normal`/`tooShort`/`intersecting`; the `disabled` variant is applied directly (not via `pillVariant`) by the voter form's **ghost re-add rows** (`PILL_STATE_CLASSES.disabled` + `pillBorderClass('disabled', isVoterForm)`), so its gray outline + `opacity-50` reads as a faded "tap to re-add this removed window" affordance. Switching states never shifts layout by ┬▒1 px because the `border` width is constant.
- **Date column is fixed at `w-[88px]`** so the `+` button column to its right lands at the same X position on every row, regardless of how short any individual row's date / relative-day label is. The width is sized to the upper bound of label widths in Geist Sans: longest date line "Wed, Sep 30" Ōēł 81 px, longest abbreviated relative-day "23mo away" Ōēł 50 px. If labels ever exceed 88 px, either widen the column or compact the labels further.
- **Relative-day labels use abbreviated units with no space between number and unit**: `Today`, `Tomorrow`, `5d away`, `2w away`, `3mo away`, `1y away`. Matches the `compactDurationSince` convention in `lib/questionListUtils.ts`. Bucket thresholds: <14 days ŌåÆ `Nd`, <8 weeks ŌåÆ `Nw`, <24 months ŌåÆ `Nmo`, else `Ny`.
- **The `+ button` is in its own flex column, `self-start` aligned**, so its center sits at the same Y as the topmost pill's center regardless of how many pills the day has. `shrink-0` keeps it a perfect 34 px circle even when delete controls appear in the slot column and pressure the row. Diameter 34 px = pill height (text-sm line + py-1.5 + 1 px border each side).
- **Delete control hides when only one slot remains.** Two-or-more-slot days show a red `├Ś` icon (no trash can) to the left of each pill; one-slot days show no `├Ś` so the day can never drop to zero windows. To remove the entire day, use the day picker ŌĆö that's the only path.
- **`DEFAULT_TIME_WINDOW`** in `lib/timeUtils.ts` is the canonical "first window" ŌĆö `{ min: '08:00', max: '17:00' }`. Imported by `useDayTimeWindowsState.ts`, `createPollHelpers.ts: emptyDraft`, and `app/create-poll/page.tsx`'s today-init path. Don't re-inline the times.
- **Slot add/remove animates its height (creator form ONLY).** Each time slot is wrapped in `AnimatedSlotRow` ŌĆö a `grid-template-rows: 0fr Ōåö 1fr` + opacity clip (300ms) ŌĆö so adding a slot grows it in and removing one collapses it out, with everything below (Duration card, cutoffs) sliding to make room via normal document flow. The render forks `isVoterForm ? (existing instant ghost-row block) : (animated block)`; the voter form is deliberately NOT animated (its ghost-row + split-window semantics differ, and the feature was scoped to creation). Mechanics, all in `components/DayTimeWindowsInput.tsx`:
  - **Stable-id reconciler `reconcileRows(prev, windows, allocId)` is what makes EDITS not animate.** Time windows are plain `{min,max}` with no identity, and `useDayTimeWindowsState.onWindowsChange` re-sorts on every change, so naive value- or index-keys would make an edit read as remove+add. The reconciler assigns persistent ids: exact value-match first (unchanged slots keep their id), then positional pairing for in-place edits (id kept ŌåÆ no animation), then leftover prop windows become `'enter'` rows (inserted at sorted position) and unmatched existing rows become `'leave'` rows (kept in place to collapse where they sat). Returns the SAME array ref when nothing changed so the reconcile `useEffect([windows, isVoterForm])` can't loop. Deps are reference-stable per day (the hook only news the changed day's `windows` array), so unrelated parent re-renders (typing elsewhere) don't re-run it.
  - **Delete/add handlers are unchanged ŌĆö animation is purely reactive to props.** `handleDeleteWindow` still calls `onChange(filter)` immediately; the reconciler then sees the row missing from `windows` and flips it to `'leave'`. The `AnimatedSlotRow` collapses and fires `onLeaveDone` on the `grid-template-rows` `transitionEnd`, which removes it from `animRows`. No delayed-onChange or imperative DOM collapse needed.
  - **`AnimatedSlotRow` `open` init is `phase !== 'enter'` (NOT `=== 'shown'`).** At mount phase is only ever `'enter'` or `'shown'` (leave rows are always derived from an already-mounted shown row), so the two are equivalent at mount ŌĆö but the `setOpen(true)` fall-through after the enter/leave branches is **load-bearing, not dead code**: it handles leaveŌåÆshown *revival* (a slot deleted then re-added/re-matched before its collapse completes) by reopening the still-mounted row. Don't "simplify" it away.
  - **Rows absent from `windows` render a neutral non-interactive `<span>` (no trash, `aria-hidden`).** Covers both leaving rows and the one-frame gap between a `windows` change and the post-render reconcile effect. `windows.indexOf(row.window) === -1` is the "not present" signal; gate trash + edit + validation flags on `isPresent`.
  - **Inter-row gap is `pt-2` skipped on the first row (`idx > 0`), INSIDE the clip.** It must live inside the `AnimatedSlotRow` clip so it collapses with the row (no 8px gap snap on enter/leave). It must be `pt-2`-not-first (NOT `pb-2`-on-all, the first shipped form) or the last slot carries 8px of trailing space against the day's hairline divider ŌĆö the reported regression.
